Of which one method is that you make three or four cauteries, lining up according to the length of the mouse, following the shape of the liver cautery we mentioned earlier; and do not rush your hand through the entire cautery, and let the patient lie on his back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two edges, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is located near the mouse, where the rib of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevations by which you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Afterwards, place two burning irons until the heart is pierced on the other side, then draw out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you wish, cauterize the entire wound with three irons.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment, when it has thrown off corruption for a long time, and this is more valuable than the other treatments mentioned earlier.
de ydropisie	I have not found any mention of "ydropisie" in the text you provided. Is there a specific section or topic related to this that you would like me to summarize?
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not beneficial for someone with dropsy, except in the manner called "ascites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment is not effective, then you must make four cauteries around the neck, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the side, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast; and the cauteries should be close to the edge of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to discharge corruption for a long time, and do not leave off treating the patient afterwards; and healing will be hastened, and both intentions will come together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be like the key that we have shown before; and those for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been placed before.
de l’enfleure des piez	Here is how to treat swelling of the feet:
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone with dropsy and filled with yellow water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deep; thus, it would break through like a citrine's skin, and let the cautery be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards make two cauteries on each leg, two cauteries on each leg at the point of the cuticle; and let one cautery be long below the knee in front and the other behind in the middle of the leg; leave the cauteries on for a long time without dressing until they are discharged; afterwards cure the rest as we have said.
de la menoison	of the wound
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the stomach comes from coldness and moisture to such an extent that the retentive and digestive virtue which is in the stomach and intestines is weakened, and cannot be cured by any kind of cure; and you see the patient suffering greatly but with great strength, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said about the cautery of the stomach earlier, at the circular cautery; and four subtle cauteries around the mouth, each cautery being like a nail, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the point of the hip, and one cautery on each thigh, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or several, and are old and made up of large cold damp corrupt humors, and have been treated as we have said previously without any improvement, then apply cauteries: three on the spine of the back, one directly below the navel, one each at the sides of the anus, and if you believe that his stomach is cooled down, and the flesh does not cook, and the face appears swollen, then apply a large cautery on the stomach as mentioned before, another on the liver, and another on the mouse, all with a wedge-shaped cautery; and let the cautery remain for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating it, cleanse the wound until it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the softness called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut artery, then heat the cautery that seems like one razor, and then put it all ablaze on the cut artery; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the birth of the vein, where the blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there is much artery, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards cure with ointments until they are clean. And if you cauterize with a large cautery on an artery, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	Of poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then such an illness comes that it cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When someone has a fistula that is inflamed and filled with corrupt moisture and rotting matter, you should probe it with a very fine tentum, making sure you know the full depth of it.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery that resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the amount it has entered. Continue applying the cautery until the corrupt and decayed flesh is burned once, or twice, or three times depending on what is needed; but beware of burning the nerves that are within and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder or the intestine, beware of those areas and only perform cauterization in a fleshy spot where it is not easily perforated. Afterward, treat the area until it is healthy. If the area is sealed and the contents have been removed for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed. But if the contents have not been removed, know that the area is corrupted and the bone at the front is rotting; thus we will say about one of these in its proper place.
de la maladie des reins	Regarding kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	If cold pain comes in the kidneys and there is great windiness, and no woman's flow appears, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with the clavicle cautery we mentioned earlier; and if we cauterize it in the middle, it will have three cauteries in a row, which will be of greater help.
de la vessie	Regarding the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	If the bladder is weak and cold and moist so that the patient retains urine, then perform cautery on the front part of the bladder where the pubic hair starts, one on the right side and one on the left side, each cautery being as long as a hazelnut; and perform one cautery on the backside, or two if necessary, using the clavicle cautery according to the shape previously described.
de la marris	Regarding hemorrhoids (piles)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not permit conception because of it, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms delayed; and when they come, great pain is felt: then it is necessary that three cauteries be made around the pudendum, as we have said about the bladder cautery, and two cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be clove-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the groin
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous humors descend to the groin and cause it to move from its place, and the sign is that the thigh appears longer than the other when measured together; and if the location of the separation is found empty, then you must cauterize the patient above the groin with one cautery shaped like a circle, and extend it before the place around the groin as it turns, so that the groin is inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cautery be as deep as all the heart; and continue until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of groin pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the groin, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated for this with what we have said in the division but the treatment does not help, and the disease is ancient: then you must purge the patient of thick humors using foul-smelling pills or other good pills resembling them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After this, perform cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two ways: namely, using burning medicines together, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery has many ways, one of which is as follows: cauterize the box of the beard with three triangular cauteries arranged in this shape, making them deep and large, leaving the width of two fingers between each cautery. Make the cauteries olive-shaped; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle on top of the head of the beard, which makes four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	"And if you see it, cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have mentioned earlier in the case of dislocation of the hip joint; but do so in such a way that the circle contains the entire hip joint, and all the sharp edges of the heart are burned."
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which it is done for sciatica when the pain is felt in the beard and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient feels the pain, and one cautery above the ankle with three points on the left side; make the cauteries cutellar-shaped, and burn the thickness of a finger; if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers of the foot or near it, cauterize there with three or four points where it is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	"And if it is necessary to do more; and if the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with an elliptical or circular cautery, but be sure in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on too long so as not to burn the nerves and large arteries, and so as not to cause greater harm and contraction to the patient."
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who performed cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it until the leg became entirely swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a bout of diarrhea that caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in both parts together, perform cautery on one and the other according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men say concerning cautery of the thigh, this is the manner: make it one such iron and let its head be as thick as a hazelnut or a little less, and let it have spaces between them and let them be spaced equally like grains of millet; and let the spaces be on both sides and also like nuts, and let there be one handle made of iron well-fashioned; this is its shape.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And let it be heated until it is entirely red and glistening with heat, then place it on the boil of the sick person's haunch, turned to face the sound side; cauterize once with one cautery iron, leave for three days, then make an embrocation of butter, allow the wound to remain open for a long time; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed."
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	"Albucasis says that we use this cautery rarely due to its intense heat, and it is scarcely used. Nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries when it can be endured, especially where it causes inflammation."
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of medicine are such that you make an instrument with spaces between them on which the edge of the door descends, and it should be made of bronze or iron on one side long, and at the top have two nuts, each separated by the thickness of a thumb; and they should be open above and overlap each other according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Place the box of hot ashes on the patient lying on his healthy side, then press your hand firmly onto the box. Afterward, throw between the two circles of the hot water that has been heated over a fire for one hour; allow this to continue for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burning sensation.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For a burning sensation will occur, like that of fire. Once this sensation has passed, raise your hand along with the tool and remove the hot ashes; leave them in place for three days, then apply butter until the blackened skin is removed. Leave it for another three days to allow corruption to be drawn out; this is the final assistance after the treatment of ointments, provided the wound is clean.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make another tool like you did for the ashes, increasing its size accordingly; this is the method of hot water, as I have written in my treatise on medical corrections.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take quicklime and live stone, an equal amount of each, grind them together, and place them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	And place over that pot another well-plombed pot, and add sweet water on top of the quicklime and live stone until there is about two handfuls of it above the powders when you grasp it firmly; leave it thus until the water drops out through a small hole bored into the bottom of the pot. Then take all that water and sprinkle it over hot coals and quicklime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very hot and is administered in many works of medicine and cauteries of other limbs. For it performs the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize well the hair, such as tannic acid, honey, and live stone with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure in which a man was healed from the pain in his hair and sciatic vein, highly praised, and says that no other treatment was performed, and he was immediately cured with just this one cure. He then bathed as instructed below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And crush some fresh and dry verdigris and grind it with a lump of fat. Apply this mixture to the hip joint, thigh, and leg where pain is felt, and cover it. Leave it on for three hours until the burning sensation subsides.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then have him enter a bath until his body is slightly warmed. Put him to bed, and the pain will all go away and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such medications as a cautery unless after bloodletting.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat dung, it helps a lot. The cauteries should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and grease it with old oil. Apply it to the depression between the big toe of the foot and the one called the 'fascicle'.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take dry goat dung, burn it until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the linen. Leave it there until it is extinguished. Repeat this process again, continuing until you sense that the heat reaches the hip joint and the pain has ceased. This method of cautery is called 'goat cautery'.
de la dolor dou dos	"back pain"
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar matter spread coldly, cauteries are of no use in any of these cases except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After the patient has been emptied of fetid pills or others like them, one should place them on the back where the pain is located, three lines marked with ink, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see fit, make three cauteries or four at the middle clavicle bone according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes upon young children, and the sign of its onset is that they have a narrow waist when they stand up, and are pale. And you find in the dorsal spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to cure it, cauterize with the cautery called "celcle" according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery embraces each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, then cauterize around the spine with a cautery pricking two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating it until it is healed according to what we have said, make sure that you do not apply a cautery in the spine where there is any weakness of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	de la dolor des jointes
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pains in the joints are due to moistures that are spread throughout each member of the body, and when pain comes on in the feet, which physicians properly call "podagra," and when it is from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: Make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to prick on the face of the foot, then apply cautery with all the cautery that one calls "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains reach down to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, then apply cautery on each knee with three or four cauteries of each part, using the olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand beyond that until the point of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains extend down to the knee and the back, then the administrator should apply the cautery that we have mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two lines of punctures around the wrist; and if there is still pain in the arms, make punctures on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains extend to the ribs or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and give medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	But if you provide good care and purge phlegm, it will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	"On the rupture of the sinews"
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	"When operation comes in the anus, and the bowels descend to the thighs and this is newly begun, then it is necessary that when you see him cure himself, he does not eat that day, and let him use things that leave the belly so that the feces come down from his belly; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are relaxed, and stretch them out towards your two fingers, and press firmly below the operation on the bone of the thumb, and at each sign it should resemble half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery which has this form:"
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until he becomes pale and throws up worms.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels to their place; and the assistant should keep his hand on them so they do not move backwards; and open the patient's thighs well, and put one cushion under him and one servant on each thigh, and another on the chest where he holds the hands; then apply the cautery on the sign of the whole hand, from the thumb to the little finger until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bowel does not slip out while applying the cautery, so that you do not burn it and cause the patient's death or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with your cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be fine according to the measure of an egg, and for large people also large according to their measure; afterwards on the third day treat the place where the cautery was with butter until the scalding is removed; then cure it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound becomes well-healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be kept on a long time, so that his eyes do not bulge when he gets up to go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, let him bring a well-made bandage and wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and guards himself from excessive drinking and eating, and from raising his voice too high; and when he follows this instruction, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter the treatment for cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Chapter 45: Of the operation for piles
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When fistulas occur in other bellies and are known to you, and you see that they do not grow any further, perform the cautery of the cautery of the rear according to its quantity, and burn the third part of the heart; afterwards treat it according to what we have said. And some of the ancients say that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery in this shape.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the starting point of the fistula and draw a line across its width above it, and another below it; then apply your hand throughout the cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterization is lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Chapter 46: Of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called 'poins', and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness, weakness, strength, location, and twisting, and the nature of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first burn, that's good; if not, repeat the cautery upon it, for such is the custom that it must change in the limb to which it is close, so you must make the burns until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Chapter 47: Of stitches
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The swelling is sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you cauterize the eye, beware if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not diminish or remain, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make cauteries on the head: one within the head at noon, and another towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape; and let your hand be so placed that the cautery reaches to the bone, and so that the skins come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape from them; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	"And if the stitches are spread out everywhere and it is manifestly lost, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery near the ear, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another beside it, and two on each shoulder; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the back of the calf, so that you do not burn them; and sometimes one makes a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver."
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries I perform, the greater help I give, and the more profit it brings. And know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, as you will find them described in various iron techniques.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After applying a poultice of vetch flour with honey, perform other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices but is not healed, then apply cauteries to the limb according to its size. The cautery should be slightly penetrating towards the heart's span; afterwards, treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cauteries are applied to the hand, foot, and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb. And thus, if the swelling is removed; but nonetheless let no one meddle with this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of the ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" becomes inflamed, and medical treatments do not work, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep according to the thickness of the skin, until the blister is removed and its color changes; then treat it with a mixture of wheat flour and lentil flour with rose oil and plantain leaves, and pigeon blood and donkey blood, each one part; and mix everything together, and tie it with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of a chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre appears at its beginning, and you see it stop, then cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	Moreover, wise men say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, as I have seen happen before. It is rather more appropriate that it be cauterized around with the cautery called 'circule', as we have said regarding many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of inflammation that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called 'adubelati', and it lingers due to excessiveness or the weakness of the patient's body if they are elderly, causing them to have less blood, or because of time; and you see it hastening towards death: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she hastens to die
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it entirely with the cautery, then heat the cautery of which here is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand on the midpoint of that disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it departing in this manner so that the course of decay is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cautery with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease there is called "corrodens", which is nothing other than a consuming of limbs, for it consumes the limbs even as fire consumes dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate a fire cautery together with fire, then heat the cauteries - small and large nails according to what is needed for the location where the disease is; afterwards cauterize it on all sides until you erase all corruption, and let nothing remain of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places a poultice with oil until the burns of the fire are removed and all corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of poultices that generate flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days you see that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; but if not, then resume the cautery on what remains of the corrupted place.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this wound has sometimes been cured with hot medicine instead of a fire cautery; but nevertheless the fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already mentioned the cure for hot medicine in its proper place. Take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Regarding swellings that come on one's feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Frequently, at the feet there appears a disease called "clos" according to our understanding, which is a large broken thing that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is performed in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	Namely, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is performed by heating an iron cautery like a vault tile until it is red hot and made of good iron to the size that it can reach around the nail on all sides with subtle edges. Then place it hot on the nail, turning your hand all around the nail until you reach the head of the nail. Leave it there for three days until it begins to ooze pus. Then make a poultice of wild mallow leaves crushed with salt, and leave the poultice on overnight, and the nail will fall out and be completely removed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with anointing oil until it is clean.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are turned away from the body and happen often both in hands and feet, then you must bring cautery with hot water to it. And it is done like this: take a cane of brass or iron, or a feather of goose, and put on the nail and the horn, that is to say warts; and put the cane upon so that it encompasses all around, then put some hot water on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and can find a deep path for the hot water up to the root; and let the patient endure a little the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave him thus, and it will deroot itself altogether with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another until you root out all those that are on the body, then treat them with anointing oils that promote flesh growth.
li cure dou trembler	Here is how to treat trembling:
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shivers with coldness of nerves,
des pustules puans	of foul boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear on the body bathing-warm sores or foul pustules caused by large corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	Thus when they first appear it is necessary to apply a cautery to each head of the pustule: either a fine juniper wood cautery with its point heated in fire, or a long aristolochia root cautery, or else a lens-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they cauterize them at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and then they cannot grow further but the excess from which they come is eliminated, and they are healed. But it must be done after bloodletting.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound on the surface or at the incision of an aposteme or at the cautery of a member, and similar things. It is very painful to endure.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	"And indeed when this happens to anyone, then you should hasten to place your two index fingers on the vein wound, and press firmly until the blood beneath is pacified so that no more drips out; then put in the fire olive oil cauteries of various sizes until they are all red hot; then take one, either large or small according to the wound size and where the artery is severed, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding stops."
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	"And if it happens that the cautery is exhausted when you lift your finger from the vein, then take another quickly from those in the fire."
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	"And continue doing this until the bleeding stops. Make sure that you do not burn the nerve nearby and that no other harm comes to the patient. Know that when blood spurts from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped unless one of the four methods we have mentioned is used: cautery, extraction if it has not been treated, tight binding with thread, or medicines applied which have the power to stop bleeding. And let it be tied and pressed appropriately."
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	"And bringing about cessation of bleeding through tight binding with rags or applying hot things on top, or other similar methods, will profit little if at all."
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	"And if this happens to anyone and there is no doctor or medicine present, then one should place their index finger on the vein wound as we have said, and press firmly until the bleeding stops. Do not move your finger but moisten it with cold water frequently so that it becomes very cold until the blood congeals and ceases flowing; and afterwards do what is necessary with regard to cauteries and medicines."
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	"Here begins the second book of the remedies for wounds from cutting."
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	"We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases which require cautery with fire or hot medicine, and we have described their causes and remedies and forms of cauteries; and I have placed this chapter at the beginning so that one may find more easily what one wishes to know."
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	"Before I begin this chapter, dear friend, you should know that there is more danger and fear in this one concerning cauteries than in the first, and therefore it requires greater caution."
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	"For in the practice of this chapter there are many occasions for bleeding from opening veins, and incision on apostumes, and wounds, and extraction of splinters, and incision on stone, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many people die."
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake anything foolish.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many people come seeking treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Among them are those who so cling to their illness that they die easily due to the frenzy they find in their disease and the severity of their condition; from these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these are those who gain their sense of being cured, saying: 'Wait, I am healed'; yet the sick person is disheartened.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place greater care in your honor than in your desire for profit. Do not open foolishly but wisely regarding those from whom you can gain certain proof and praise; use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients to achieve their healing. This will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	"Dear friend, may our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen."
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	"Now I have arranged this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cauteries which I have already divided from beginning to end, so that you may find more easily what you need."
dou chief plein d’aigue	Chapter 1: Head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	"Know that this disease often occurs in infants at birth, when the mother's passage is too narrow for the child's head; and sometimes it happens without any known cause."
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	"And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than infants, and all those whom I saw died quickly; and therefore it seems to me that I may leave the treatment of such conditions alone."
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	"And I saw one child whose head was full of water and grew larger every day until it could no longer support itself; and the swelling became so great that it died, and this swelling gathered under the bone on top of the syphac, between the heart and the bone; and if the swelling is between the heart and the bone, and the aposteme is small, then you should make an incision through the middle of the head with a blade wide enough for the swelling to escape; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the swelling can pass through. Here is the form of the spatulum:"
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	"If the swelling is larger and the aposteme is bigger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:"
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	"And if the swelling is under the bone and you see the signs that the angles of the head are open on each side, and water jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, but nothing comes out: then you must make three incisions through the head according to this method:"
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after incision, remove all moisture forcefully.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After applying compresses and powders, put wine and oil on it, leaving it so for five days. Then remove it, treat the wound with dressings and ointments, keep the head wrapped evenly, and give the patient dry food and drink until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	"And another method of incision is to observe where the greatest enlargement of the aposteme and the gathering of water appear, for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right side, and sometimes on the left."
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	"Therefore cut there where the aposteme appears and the gathering of water, and make the incision according to what you can manage; and be careful not to cut the artery; and if a vein flows with blood, so that the sick person dies from the loss of blood and evacuation of swelling."
de reume	Chapter 2: Rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	"When someone has a disease called 'catarrh' in the ears or feet, and the illness is long-standing and does not improve with medicinal treatment, then the final treatment should be cauteries combined with ligating the two arteries."
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, then, when you close the eyes of the patient, that he turn his head back; afterward, rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient stretch his neck with both hands on the cloth; then look where the vein goes and the places of one and the other are after the ears, and then press them down; then mark the places with ink, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula at two parts, so that the cut goes to the bone, and this should be done on the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	"And if you see, push the spatula underneath the artery and cut it above it, cutting also two fingers wide across."
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood spurts out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the arteries do not appear by touch, then you must measure the quantity of space from three fingers' width, then mark with ink and cut to the bone; and the amount of blood that should be let out is six ounces, and perhaps a bit more or less depending on what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery. Then examine the wound: if it remains on the bone's point, cut off the scab so that no pus can come in, then squeeze the wound and bind it, applying ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	"Of dislocations"
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dislocation and catarrh occur due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples, accompanied by madness and similar conditions, it is treated with various medical remedies but not all of them are effective. Therefore, we draw out the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient shaves the hair from their temples and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, for it beats well there, and is rarely covered except in some men who are very cold; and if it is covered, then the patient draws its neck with certain cloths, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the place with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatumile of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then grasp it with forceps and carefully cut away any surrounding tissue on each side; if the artery is thin, use the tip of your nail to tease it out, then cut off that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not cut, blood will not flow freely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	"And draw blood from the.vi. veins, until.iij.; and if the artery is large, you should tie it in two places with a double strand of strong silk thread to prevent decay reaching the wound before the stitching, and let blood flow; then cut away the excess flesh between the two ties at that very moment, and then, if you wish, cauterize with the surgical cautery until the bone is reached; and this is the main procedure if the patient has no fever and is of warm complexion."
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Furthermore, cauterization aids in finishing off moistures (i.e., infections): therefore it is more helpful with moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When extracting arteries, one should fill the space with old cotton and place well-made bandages on top; once they are untied, cure it with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until it is healed. If blood flows from the artery while working on it, hasten to cauterize with a hot iron or pour vitriol into your hand and place it over the wound to stop the bleeding; if you don't have this available, rub the wound with your thumb until the blood congeals, then rinse it with cold water until the bleeding stops, and bind it as necessary. The best and easiest method for extracting an artery is to cauterize its channel with a two-pronged cautery iron, but make sure the prongs are well-spaced to retain heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the prongs are too thin, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be one finger's width of space between the two blades, and then once you have marked the two spots with the hot iron, place it on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the channel in two places; and let the two wounds be some distance apart because this cautery does not join them entirely together; and that is the shape of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears from the eyes flow down the channels that are above the forehead of the head, and it does not help to treat them with medicine, and you see the sick person's face becoming reddened, and feel on their forehead trembling like shivers; and if the eyelashes are thin and moist so that the hairs of the paper-like tissues have fallen off, and the papers themselves are heated and burned by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called this remedy "cure contuse" by the ancients. You should do this for the patient who has this illness: First make them grow hair on their forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead equally spaced according to its length; one of the incisions should be as long as two fingers midway down the forehead and continuing downward to the nose, and the other two should be placed on either side of the forehead above the eyebrows, but be careful not to cut the arteries that are located on either side above the eyebrows. Keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and each wound should be the width of three fingers when joined together. Have a piece of sponge and many cloths ready to wipe up the blood, then insert the spatumile instrument in this manner:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	Make the incision that is directly above the temple down to the second incision; then scrape away all the skin that is between the two incisions as far back as it reaches on the bone, and then make another incision from the middle one to the other second one, and finally extract this scalpel.
