si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision the instrument called "cultellaria," which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, not sharp; this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp costa blade towards the flesh of the heart, and the soft costa blade towards the bone, and press until it reaches the mid-line furrow.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels descending from the neck to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to those that open into the heart, and then do likewise in the middle furrow up to the other end; and then draw out blood evenly, and express the area for the blood taken; then place a wick of old cotton in each furrow, and lay wet compresses in wine, oil, and balm on top, ensuring that no boils come into being; and on the third day untie the bandages, and bring great plenty of sage tea, then treat with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments to heal wounds until healed.
dou reume des eulz	glaucoma
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When catarrh occurs frequently, and you see the eyes thin and small, and vision weakened, and the paper-like tissues burned; and the hairs fall out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the sick person sneezes; then know from these symptoms that these materials and this catarrh come only from many veins, and the remedy for it is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to raise their forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one across its width.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Start from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that move during chewing; and when the bone is exposed, then absorb all the blood with a sponge, and then open between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton and linen bandages; then tie on it cloths moistened in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses. When it has been removed, then you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then heal with drying agents.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster with them; apply it to these wounds to promote scar tissue formation throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Here is the section on "The Stopping of the Ears" from the medieval French medical treatise "La Grande Chirurgie":
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of these four things:
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When something hard like a stone or other thing falls into the ear and does not fit properly or grow in the ear, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, distill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil there, then bring about extraction; and when the time is right, make him sneeze with condimentum, and plug his nostrils when sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Very often fever occurs with this treatment; and if it does not occur, one should perform an extraction using fine forceps, of which there is the form here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not come out with the forceps, it is good to proceed with extraction using fine tweezers with a small opening. If that still does not work, make a hollow reed and insert its tip into the ear hole, then seal around it with soft wax so that wind cannot enter along with the reed; then heat it strongly, as often heat comes in this manner as we have described; if it does not produce heat this way, take birdlime, such as that used by birds, and put some on an instrument sharp for this purpose, wrap cotton around it, then press the birdlime against the stone or whatever it may be and heat it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Even if it doesn't come from all these things that we have said, then quickly split the ear before an abscess becomes warm and causes spasm; and the manner of splitting is that you first make the patient lie on their back, and draw out blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear at the place where it hangs down; and let the cut be like a moon shape until you reach the bone, then break it according to your power, and quickly suck out the marrow."
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	"And if it's a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one thin, subtle spatula according to this form:"
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that boil.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this if you think the boil is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made several incisions. Then extract it with fine forceps and apply suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is clean.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, in water that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to first sneeze forcefully and fill the ear with thick cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it does not come out through the boil, then so be it.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many needles according to the length of your thin and light fingers, heat them slightly in fire. Let the patient place one or two needles into the hole of their ear, and press with another needle from the other side, pushing one needle out through the other; continue doing this until all the water has come out, then take a reed and put one end into the ear while heating the other end with fire until it is burnt. Then repeat with more reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said in the case of stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	"In the extraction of a beast, if it is small bodied, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in division; but if it is large bodied that you can feel it, then administer extraction with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear."
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	"In the extraction of earthworms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in division and in treating distillations, and if the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear towards the sun: if there are any worms visible, then extract them with fine forceps, and if none are visible, then take the tube that has this form:"
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And place the finest tip of the instrument into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then suck strongly at the entire wound; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey coming out, then stuff around the wound with cotton as I have said in the case of stones; and if they still do not come out readily as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective for killing worms, which you will find treated in books on distillations; and distill your oils and medicines onto this instrument through which you shall insert them into the ear, of which here is the shape as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	"And let it be of silver or bronze, narrow underneath with one small hole, and above open for distillation; and for pressing inside the distillation there is one well-made instrument of brass for this purpose, and if you wish take one razor and wrap cotton thickly around its point; then throw your oil or juice and what you wish of medicines into the tube, and place the tube in the ear; then insert the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled well out of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little warmed by the fire beforehand before distilling it into the ear; and make sure that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be as good."
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Here is the section on "The Stopping of the Ears" from the medieval French medical treatise "La Grande Chirurgie":
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in its ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to injury of the ear, or flesh grown inside it, and some such blockages occur deep within the ear so that one cannot see them; and sometimes there is one pore missing from the hole, which is clearly visible.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, those that occur deep within the ear, so that one cannot see them, are difficult to treat in many situations, and in these cases it is necessary to put the patient's ear in the sun and look inside: if you see the obstruction appearing, then perform the procedure described below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	"And let it be sharp and cutting both before and behind, entirely full, so that it does not wound the ear; if the protuberance is of flesh born in the body of the ear, hold it with fine forceps, and cut lightly, until all that flesh is removed."
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operations are deeply embedded in the ear, then take a fine sharp razor and heat it lightly over the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the operation where the patient feels pain in hearing, pierce lightly and carefully, ensuring not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place a bandage according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Continue doing this for a few days until the wound is healed. Then take a plug and moisten it with rose water, powdered vitriol, and place it in the ear. If you see that the ear is swollen, you must remove the plug and insert another one moistened with cerote made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling has gone down; then cure it until it is healthy."
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	"And if there is discharge of blood, dip a sponge in cold water and wring it out, then place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the discharge of blood, which can be found in treatises on distillations."
de la char des papieres	"It seems like you're trying to translate "de la chair des papelards" which means "of the flesh of paper". However, it doesn't make sense in this context. Do you mean something else?"
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	"This is the remedy for those boils that come on moist skin and then dry up: you must stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut them open with a spathaula from their roots; then sprinkle powdered vitriol on the wound."
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	"And if they burst open and bleed, cauterize them with a fine lenticular cautery, and then apply the cautery again after the incision. This is often repeated until nothing remains of their roots; and once they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return."
de la gresle	"Here is the remedy for hailstones:
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there come on the papers of the eyes things that appear like hail in their shape and hardness, and therefore this disease is called 'hail', and it is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below; its treatment is thus: guard yourself if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is an easy thing to know; then make the opening wide, then scrape each part lightly, then grasp it with pincers, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	But if you cannot cut it without piercing the paper a little, then it does not harm the patient; and if the crack is large, stitch it together and heal it until it is sound; and if it is small, do not use force, for the medicine will restore it soon and fill it with flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	"And if the hail is descending into the ear towards the upper part, invert the paper, and grasp the hail with pincers, and remove it and press on both sides; and if the paper is separated by the incision, do not worry; and when the hail has been removed, rinse the ear with saltwater, and treat the wound until the patient is healed."
de la graisse des eulz	"Regarding eye fat:"
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is inside the threads of the papers above, and this happens more in children than in adults, and it harms their eyes greatly, and they have cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they lie on their faces all the time, and sleep thus, and their papers below their eyebrows are moist with the swelling and appearance that has been covered by the exinach that opens into the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press it with your two hands and feel it give way.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	"And the manner of treating it is as follows: the patient puts their head in your hand; then take one linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains eye fat on each side, then place it on them; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the eye fat gathers within the circle; then make a cut down the middle of the moistness with a sharp scalpel, making a wound no larger than the one made in the vein of wine; and cut deep into the skin until you reach the eye fat; and in various positions, eye fat comes out of the wound, resembling a piece of white fat."
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	"Therefore, extract it all with one piece of soft cloth between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to stick in the wound, so that you do not harm all the skin up to the eye, lest you injure it."
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	"And if the eye fat does not appear at the beginning of the wound, then slightly widen the wound lightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the wound, and squeeze out the bandages."
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such men who grind salt and place it on top to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal it until it is healthy again.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the place, then treat it with poultices that are soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	"Regarding eyebrow hair:"
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	"If eyebrow hairs are born joined together abnormally and entangled, they cause harm to the eyes, and bring about conditions such as constant tearing and softening of the eyebrows and whitening, to the extent that it causes damage to the eyes; and there are four ways to treat it: either by cautery with fire together, or by hot medicine according to what is appropriate before or after cautery, and it can be done either by incision and stitching, or by tweezers, depending on what I will say."
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	"It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the eyebrow away from the eye with your left hand; if it turns well, good. If not, insert a needle with one thread onto it; and let it be near the edge of the eyebrow where the hairs are attached to those hairs, and draw one thread up over the entire eyebrow, and turn it towards the razor; then make an incision downwards under the eyebrow, under the joined hairs, all along the eyelid from the large tear gland to the small one; then extract one thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth underneath the eyebrow, then press on the eyebrow with your finger, like the lid of a mirror, and in any case the figure must be according to the quantity that you see raise the eyebrow which is separated from them."
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need to cut off a large quantity of the paper according to how it has been softened; then make two lines along the entire length that you have marked, and begin from the larger line up to the smaller one; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then place the needle into one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape off all the skin; then join the two lips with a stitch of thread made of fine wool, and absorb the blood, and dry any excess threads on the two eyebrows with any sticky substance you have, if you can see this being done; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching using drying and constricting substances, because the paper will revive at the joining of the wound and its closure, but stitching is harmful (as the ancients said), and this is work done without fear; and there is another method: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure like the leaves of myrtle, as we have described, with three needles spread out according to the shape that is shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	"Then cut what is above the small forceps evenly according to the shape shown here:"
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	If you cannot hold the forceps and the thing is not even, take a needle with thread, insert it into the figure; place another thread beside the large artery and the second thread beside the small one, and gather them evenly between your fingers. Then raise your hand evenly, and raise all the skin on which you have signet-ed, as we have described, then close the two lips of the wound with stitches, and care for it until it is clean; And if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar softening ointments. And sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper turns: you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one or the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	"The cure for the canthus (corner of the eye) is as follows: and it is that you fold the paper and make an incision inside according to what I have said, and then make two threads by art, and two fine ties as long as the paper and the width of the spatula; and cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then join one and the other subtly on top of the oil paper, and tightly tie the two canthi from the two parts; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and shrivel and shrink until it becomes smooth."
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, cut through the forceps, then care for it until it is clean; And when the wound is healed and the paper is removed, the hairs will no longer prickle. And this is the form of the two canines that you should make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	"The operation is as follows: take a fine needle and thread it with one soft and fine silk thread; then tie the ends together subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm in length; then prepare another fine silk thread briefly, and tie its ends to the first thread; then the patient should put their head on your shoulder, and they should stand near the sun so that the operation is illuminated, for it is a subtle and delicate operation; then take the needle all along the hairline close to the skin, and pierce it into the paper hastily until you draw it up above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the hairline, and put it back into the hairline if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out of the hairline onto the paper with the natural hair."
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	"And if the hairline is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the hairline down all along the thread that you have prepared, until the hairline comes out of the hole above and you can see it with the naked eye; then pull the hairline and the thread together, and close the eye and let it heal for two or three days, until the hair returns to its place and the skin grows over it; and if the hairs are sparse, accompany one long natural eyebrow hair, and lift it up with that one which you leave, so that it is elongated and then lifted up."
de la porriture de l’oil	de la porriture de l’oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or decay occurs in the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting or cauterizing, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treating it is that you should break open this scab and separate the lips of it, and put in linseed wadding, and let it until it heals; and you must not use things that dry out and constrict in its treatment.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but there are things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or album water and linseed should be cooked, and ointments of diachylon melted in some oil, and one should wrap a wadding with it for the treatment of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you should be careful that it does not heal according to its former shape; and these operations that we have mentioned are only remedies for this illness, so that it does not return in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" under the eye is natural but accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and cut and cautery and similar things; and the way of the operation in it is that you take a needle, on which there is double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eyelid to the right, so that the threads come out through two holes in the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the entire needle, and cut with one wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure on the paper returns as it should be, that is good; but if not, then take one razor and place it in the cut, and turn the paper over, and make two cuts along the edges inside the paper; and let the holes of the two cuts be at both angles of the incision you have cut, and make one angle such that when they are joined together, the figure is like the figure of a letter called "I Greek"; then remove that flesh according to its quantity which was beneath the paper, from what supports the paper, then join the two separated parts with thread made of wool; then treat it as we have said regarding softening medicines and dressings, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or stitches or cauterization, then you must make a full slit under the hair of the paper, and according to what is said above; then open between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters prepare ingenious devices with all their power so that they make the figure return to its natural shape; and the sick person himself, according to what he needs of operations and instruments, in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	de l’acuité de l’oil et du mouvement des esperitz
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this fusion occurs in many men in such a manner that the paper on top is stuck with the white of the eye, and it cannot move nor perform its natural duties, then you must insert the point of a razor underneath the paper, and lift it up; and stretch them with pincers until you reach that which is attached to the subtile spatula, which should not be too dull nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot bear the spatula being too dull nor cutting the eye; and let your incision be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all of this assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye they make salt water, and lift it with fresh water, and collyrium. Then put a linen cloth between the paper and the eye, and put on the eye wool moistened with egg albumen. And after the third day use collyrium and healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the corner of the eye is in two ways: it is nerve-like and similar to one hard skin, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles moist white congealed blood. When you touch it with iron and try to grasp it with pincers, you cannot do so; both these appearances begin near the large tear duct, and gradually grow little by little until they cover the whole sight and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: The patient should put their head in your hand, then open their eyes. Lift the paper with your hand, then grasp the corner with small pincers and stretch it up. Then take a needle, and on it place one horse, cow, or ox hair, and a strong thread. Double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the corner, piercing it entirely with the needle, and tie the corner with a thread and stretch it upwards. Then scrape along the entire length of the hair the side of the corner that covers the pupil and the iris up to the head. Then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct using the subtle spatula and small forceps, leaving the natural flesh in the tear duct so that the incision does not interfere with the normal flow of tears. Sometimes the corner is stretched only with the needle and thread, as we have said before. Then scrape it gently with the soft spatula, which has this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure that the spatula does not touch the delicate flesh and damage it, nor should the pupil be pierced. After the incision, sprinkle a little crushed selbroit into the eye, and apply collyrium made of lead ore, leaving it overnight. Then treat it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerve-filled,
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully raise the nail above it, and if you see that it does not thin out nor the reason press thereupon, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red ochre ground together, and stop up the eye until the next day; then recommence the same work according to this very same procedure, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything opposes you in the eye, such as a hot sore, then apply milk and first cure the hot sore until it is healed, then recommence the operation just as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid harms the eye greatly, then suspend it with a needle and cut off part of it but not all of it so that tears do not come from there; then distill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows upon the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, sometimes there is born red flesh which covers the pupil and presses upon the papery skin and twists at the edge, resembling a pomegranate flower; and this is its operation: let the patient place his head in your hand, then open his eyes wide, and gather all that flesh with suitable tweezers, and hold it firm with strength; then cut away the first layer of flesh, and keep cutting all along to the very end with a razor, taking care not to wound the eye during this operation. And let the incision be made as we have said in the cutting of the nail and in small forceps for removing the boil, as shown later in this chapter; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, then dress the eye with crushed rue or distill upon it red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and place cotton dampened with eggwhite over the eye so that a hot tumor may form thereupon; and if anything remains and hot blood overflows, and you suspect a hot tumor, then leave the eye alone and treat the tumor with things that allay a hot tumor. Then return to your operation until it is clean again, and do thus for each layer of flesh joined in the eye by this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless you should alleviate the cure of each weak eye by the natural way; and in case of an accident, operate with iron; and do not put your hand into any operation until you see that these members can withstand this operation.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Before veins become reddened, which cover over the eye, they weaken vision and diminish its power daily.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, it is necessary that you first examine the eye where the vein appears prominent; if there's no other visible disease besides the prominence; then proceed thus: tell the patient to tilt their head toward you, gently press these veins at the inner canthus according to your expertise, and use a double-ended needle of this shape
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And there should be two hooks at intervals of one finger's breadth on the same body according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully tie those veins and squeeze out the blood hour by hour until you see the veins move away from the eye; and ensure that you do not cut the eye with the points of the spatumiles, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your task so that you only touch those veins; and when you have done this, then distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains of the seed.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect all of this in that hour, then apply a plaster to the eye made from soothing substances for eye pain, and leave it on for several days until the pain is eased and an aposteme is formed, then resume according to this method until it is healed; and this is the form of the treatment.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls a fistula "arissati": when you heal it with cautery and medicine that is very hot according to what I have said before, but it is not healed, then there is a device in it such that you must cut on the aposteme where it should die, and remove all of the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then take all of the instruments that are needed for this task; and they are called "aspre chief", and should be made of red iron with one sharp point like a file as it is in its present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the sharp point of the instrument on the bone that is corrupted, then twist it between your fingers and press your hand gently until you know that all of the corruption has been removed; and do this several times, then restore the wound with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the place is hard and no pus issues, and the body of the bow is hard, and it remains thus for forty days without worsening or becoming an abscess; nor does any bad accident occur, know that it is healthy. But if not, then there's only one option left: to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nostril according to this shape. And this is how you do it: uncover the bone a second time with iron, and use hot medicines. When uncovered, take this awl according to this shape; let the iron head have three angles, and thin the shaft right up to the tip as shown here
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the ear, and move your hand away from the eye. Then turn the drill until it pierces the bone and the patient feels by this that the vein is hit if he holds his hand over his nose. And then restore the location with dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the location, then the matter goes to the nose; so it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens fully in all directions, and there is no obstruction to the nose nor diminution, then you must bandage the patient; then wash it, then place cupping glasses or leeches without wounding to suck; then put on the eye a plaster made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye, and cover it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, and double each one into four, and then place them on top of each other according to how much the eye needs; then strain it with a firm bandage, and begin again with the cupping glasses to suck without wounding; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the plaster melts, you must remove it frequently; then remove the plaster after the day and night, and if you see that the eye is healing, that's good; if not, begin again with the emplastrum and bandages and plaster and cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the prolapse of the rectum
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the prolapse of the rectum comes and opens, and paper comes out like grains of resin, and it is horrible to see; therefore if you see it happen, the operation is as follows: take a needle and insert it into the root of the part below until it reaches the part above, then take another needle with one double thread from the part of the anus; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to its position; then tie the loop of the double thread around one part of the rectum and strain it well, then remove the needle and place on the wound linen moistened in egg albumen; and let it remain until the prolapse comes with the rectum, then treat the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the rectum on each side with a band of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has great protrusion, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from far behind the eye, and draw out the moist albumen and allow the eye to descend, and enter immediately; then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eyebrow
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a vein that collects in the eye, resembling descending water, yet it is not water. And the manner of its appearance at work is as follows: make the patient sit on an appropriate and straight seat, then take their head between your two hands, and move it until you see the vein rise up before your eyes; then pierce it, and let it not descend nor be disturbed by light, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the vein is not appropriate as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the patient is seated between your hands, then take the delicate spatula and cut through the cornea's connective tissue with the skin along its outer edge until the boil emerges; once it has emerged, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and mixed with honey, then treat it further until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have now the likenesses of waters in their divisions, and what should be used for piercing; work accordingly to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You must have the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and have them hold their healthy eye tightly shut; then place the eye paper in your left hand if the affected eye is on the left, or in your right hand if it's on the right. Then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the eye is left, or in your left hand if it's right. Place the tip of the almagda near the cornea along the thickness of a reed at the inner corner of the eye towards the nose, then gently push the almagda and twist your hand until you feel it pierce through to the empty space behind the cornea; ensure that the length of the almagda's path is equal to the length from the beginning of the pupil to the end of the blackness. Then you will see the bone through the clear cornea, and then place the instrument up to where the water is, then express it through one channel after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water flows downwards, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a brief rest, if the water rises through the second passage, insert the wick with the instrument. When it is firmly in place and no longer rises, gently remove the almagda by turning your hand little by little; then apply a drop of gemstone water to the eye, and lift the eyelid from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place over the eye a wad of wool moistened in rose oil and egg yolk, and bind it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are from our time, we place common bruised basil mixed with egg yolks on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then you should take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctiva, not too deep but carefully, and insert the almagda as we have said. After completing this procedure, prepare for the patient a comfortable dark room where he should sleep on his back for three days without moving, taking light food and keeping his head still. Bind him according to his condition until the third day, then untie him in the same dark room and test his sight with various objects. If he sees them well, then rebind him for seven more days. Do not perform this procedure during or immediately after the operation, but wait a while so that the water does not rise too quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess is about to form, you should open the eye in front of it on the seventh day, and use a plaster that draws out the abscess; and once it has been drawn out, close the eye and place a lint bandage over it for several days, ensuring that it remains in a dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then gradually leave the house little by little, and return to your usual habits; and know that no disciples should intervene in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	"And one came to us who was from Jerusalem, who told us that in their land they use almagda to pierce through, into which water is sucked, but nonetheless I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a novel thing."
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	"And these are the likenesses of the shapes of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and let them be made of pure silver:"
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	"And let their fronts be of this same subtlety, and the back have three sharp corners."
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nostril
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes various kinds of worms are born or found joined together, among which some resemble scorpions with many legs; and there are also such worms that have flesh of a dark color, and others that have flesh of fair color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore, in the case of those worms that are soft and not dark-colored, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun, open their nostrils, sprinkle honey onto the worms, and chase them out; then carefully pluck off as many as you can hold with tweezers using a fine, sharp-pointed probe on one side until you know that all of the worms have been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be scraped off, open it with one of the light, subtle instruments until nothing remains; and if it swells up or becomes inflamed, then treat it as necessary. And if they are malignant ulcers, rush to cauterize them so that the blood is stanched and all the flesh is removed, then pour on them immediately oil and wine or vinegar
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nostril opens and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healthy; but if moisture does not reach as it should, know that there is bone marrow in the bone above, which prevents the tool from cutting: therefore you must insert a thread of moderately thick linen, dampened with hot water, into the nostril, leaving a space of one finger or less between each fold. Let the patient place the head on the thread firmly and pull it through while smelling strongly until it reaches the mouth. Many children do this at school, and it is easy for those who wish to perform it. Then hold one end of the thread that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull them gently towards you in turn, as we have done.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the nostril has expelled all the corrupt flesh, then pull out the thread, squeeze out the blood, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment, then replace it in the nostril as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has completely destroyed any remaining flesh. Then place a wick of wool moistened with a little olive oil in the nostril for several days until it is clean, and if necessary use drying medicines. This is the form of the instrument used to purge the head, through which oils and nostril medicines are distilled.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp like a tube with the conduit also; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full in order to purge the head; and let it have many holes at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nostril
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there appears on the nostril a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large enough to be clearly seen; therefore you must cut it at its beginning, and remove all of its root, then apply cauterization or burning medicine to it. But if it is delayed until it is large, beware if it is hard, of dark color, and poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted aposteme. For when you cut it, great mischief comes upon the patient. And if the aposteme is soft to the touch, not dark colored, and you see that it can be completely cut, then empty out the nostril without fear, and cure it afterwards with drying and restricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nostril is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes upon one of these cartilages, it profits little, except perhaps in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, first examine if the wound is fresh throughout its blood; and then join the two lips with a stitch, and treat it until it is clean. But if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must scrape all the parts of their skin until they are sound, then join the two lips with a stitch, bind them, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder and crushed incense upon them; and place over the powders a piece of strong plaster or other adhesive plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is clean.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is as follows: you can join the wound together using needles, as we have said in the case of abdominal suturing; or with thread, as I have already explained to you.
des apostemes des levres	Of the apostemes on the lips
