A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have hard apostemes on their lips resembling grains of wheat, some small and others large. Therefore you must turn the lips back and cut along each one with a knife, then grasp it with forceps and cut it in every part; afterwards fill the space after the incision with ground vitriol until the blood is stanched; then leave it alone, and cure it afterwards with drying things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there appears on the gums attached flesh, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore you must hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, then let the bow or blood flow. Then place ground vitriol or other restricting and drying powders upon the wound; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: for it will not return afterwards; these are the forms of the instruments used to cut it.
des sordens	Of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes the teeth in the head are joined together, inside the mouth between the gums, with rough and sharp scabs; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green and wormy, so that corruption reaches the gum and the teeth smell bad. Therefore you must make the patient sit between your hands, their chin in your lap, and scrape the teeth or scabs until there is nothing left of them. And do likewise with blackness and greenness and yellowness and other stains until they are cleaned; and if what was there at first is removed, it is good; but if not, then recommence on the second day and the third until you have everything scraped; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping according to what the task shows, because those used for scraping teeth from the front are different from those used for scraping between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating a toothache, you must delay extracting it as long as possible because this should never be done except in the highest degree of necessity.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained due to toothache, you must be certain about the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain leaves the patient and they believe it is in the good tooth, and have that tooth pulled; yet still the pain does not depart, for we have seen this many times. And when you are certain about the aching tooth, then scrape around the tooth with a sharp spoon to ward off the gum on all sides. Then move it with your fingers or delicate forceps bit by bit until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the forceps; and hold the patient's head between your knees, and yours so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these tools and gently insert it on each side, and use the lever tool as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is cracked or broken, then you must fill the holes with wadding where the piercing occurred; and gently grasp it with forceps so that it does not break while extracting; and there must be careful bleeding around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take care not to break it, and if a piece remains, it will cause the patient even greater pain due to the wickedness of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware not to act like the ignorant surgeons who through haste and recklessness sometimes break the jawbone and do not follow what we have described; but often bring upon people great illness due to pieces left in the roots or the broken jawbone, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine, hot water, and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, sprinkle the area with powdered vitriol; and if that does not suffice, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the tools with which one should extract teeth first are those with long points and thick handles so that they do not double over when pulling the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large members so they do not bend during traction, and made of well-smithied iron, and toothed for holding movement.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	If the root remains at the breast, then you must put moistened cotton smeared with butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the joint is softened, then put inside the tongs called "algefri," with which the head seems like a parrot's beak; and they should be shaped within like a file.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these pliers, you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root and place the tool called "althali", namely, the crowbar; this is its shape
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break. If the root jumps out with this, that is good; if not, help yourself with all the tools, of which their shapes come hereafter
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this tool that has two handles, this is its shape
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools that are in front of the root of the teeth, and this tool that resembles large pliers; this is its shape
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these tools be strong so that they cannot break. Know that there are many dental tools and also others not counted. And the wise and subtle master finds his own tool according to what his works and the illness dictate for him, because there are such illnesses where ancient masters did not teach any tool due to their diversity of today. And if he breaks neither cartilage nor other bones, then he seeks among the tools that are necessary, which I have told you about, and helps himself with gestures; this is its shape
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not slip away but can grasp and remove it. Then restore the place with suitable medicines for that location. And if there is decay in the bone and it is small, then remove it with all these tools
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to their natural course and are misshapen in form, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is close behind the other tooth and not in its proper place, so that one cannot be placed or polished: then rasp it. And if it is next to the tooth, take this tool whose shape is like a small beak and made of iron with a sharp edge at the top
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And strike the tooth gently with your hand every day to harden it and so that you do not move the others. And if it is visible so that it can be polished, then use this kind of file whose shape is like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles. And gently file the tooth little by little every day so that it does not move too much and then level it at the end with any plane or scraper. And if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then file down its sharpness until it is smooth so that it does not hurt the tongue nor interfere with speech
quant li dent lochent	When teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loosened, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot chew what they eat without it hurting, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but to no avail, then you must restrain it with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never does. The thread should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth. If you see that the teeth are straight, take the thread and double-fold it between two healthy teeth first, then place the head between the loose teeth if there is one or more, until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side. Then begin covering again up to where you started, and hold your hand steadily and carefully so that it does not move. Your tying should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the head of the thread with a pair of pliers, and join them together, and place them between the sound teeth, so that it does not burn the tongue; then keep it thus tightly together as long as possible, and if it loosens, or the threads fray, tighten it with another thread. Thus it will remain and serve throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two sound teeth and the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place little by little, as we have said. And only let those who are wise and careful handle it, and sometimes the shape of a cow's bone tooth is made and placed where the defect is, and it is secured with wire as we have described, and it remains there for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the frenulum of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this binding occurs beneath the tongue naturally at birth; or due to an accidental wound. The procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth and hold their head steady with your hand while lifting the tongue. Then grasp the thick nerve ligament with forceps until the tongue is released from its attachment. If there is scarring or stiffness, which can occur from a wound, use an awl to cut through it. Be careful not to cut too deeply to avoid damaging the artery below. Once done, rinse with rose water and marjoram, or cool water, then place a linen bandage beneath the tongue each night so that the tissues do not stick together.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood starts to flow, then place crushed vitriol on the spot; and if the blood continues to flow, cauterize it with a slow-acting cautery iron, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it has a pale or black or hard appearance and the person does not feel it, do not touch it at all, because it is a chancre. And if it appears to be leaning towards a blenorrhoea, with moisture present, then scrape it off with an onion and make a subtle incision with a fine spatula and deliver it on both sides. If bleeding occurs from your operation, sprinkle powdered vitriol over it until it stops, then return to your operation and remove all the furuncle. Then rinse the area with sage and celandine and treat it with other remedies until it is completely healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	On swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If hard, small, and earth-colored boils appear in the throat, called 'godath,' which are properly called tonsils, if you treat them as we have described earlier but they do not heal, beware: do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	But if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, also because of blood flow; but let it fester until it becomes ripe, then you can burst it, or it will break on its own. And if they are whitish and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cut, but first check if the boil is resting calmly and is peaceful.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then seat the patient before the sun, and his head in your hand, and he open his mouth and the servant take the sword between their hands, and press the tongue below with all the tool, of which this is the form; and it be of silver or refined brass like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	"If you press the tongue against this tool and see the swelling, take the needle and insert it into the tonsil, then push it in further than you can. Then pull out some of the cloth with it, and cut with the tool, which has the shape of a forceps. Be careful though, as their tips are curved inward and they are very sharp. They are made of iron or steel:"
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if you do not have this tool present, use tongs, which have this shape:"
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	"And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other. And when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same manner. After the incision, the patient should gargle with warm water and sage, and if there is bleeding, he should gargle with water or cooked pomegranate rinds or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops. Then treat it until it is healed. And sometimes other swellings appear in the throat besides the two tonsils; cut these as you would the two tonsils."
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was near inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and it had almost closed up the entire throat, so that she could not exhale through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and would have died if left thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had been pierced twice through the two openings near it.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then acted swiftly, and inserted a feather into one opening, then drew it out with great care, extracting much bile; then pierced the other opening near the abscess, opened her mouth and pressed down on her tongue; afterward inserted the feather into the abscess, cut off a portion of it, from which only a little blood issued forth; and thus was the throat passage opened for the woman, and she began to drink water then wine, and I kept cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess continued to grow back, filling up the space that I had emptied out until it became very large; therefore I cauterized it with an iron instrument inside her throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I departed from those parts, and do not know what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	"of the eye"
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When tears descend to the eye, and it is dilated and long, it is called "perpendicular"; but if it is below thick and round, it is called "tear.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is curetted as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the hard abscess has softened, and it is thin, then you must cut it; but if it is round and gathered together and not long; and it is sanguine or of dark color or black, then you should avoid incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient thereby.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to its manner of blenching and length, make the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument mentioned earlier; then insert a needle into the eye and draw it underneath, and cut it with one or two instruments as mentioned in the incision of both mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut any more than the superfluity that exceeds the natural limit; for if you cut more, you harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of two kidneys, and treat until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears being cut, then you must use a device for cauterizing the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is hot and dry.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue on the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and fills it with hot water that is neither too thick nor too thin; and in placing this instrument gently, here is its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Et ait ou chief une cheveure où om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d'une cuillier, et met l'estrument a tout la medicine sus l'uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu'ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l'uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d'une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l'envoloupe sus certain estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l'estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s'aerde sus l'uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l'essue entor l'uve, de couton embut en burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arrosez d'aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu'il soit sanez."
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	"This cure is more powerful than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and mugwort and similar herbs, and assemble them all together in one pot. And put a hot ember into it, and let it boil well; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be one iron instrument made like this:"
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or brass, and one of the heads should be placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye is numbed. Afterward, repeat this often until the eye is dry, and ensure that you do not perform this procedure at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things can happen there; and do not perform it further than the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a goose feather and place it within the head so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot for it is good together with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	"Many times there is a bone stuck in the throat or spine of a fish, or some other thing. Therefore you should extract what you can see and press the tongue with the instrument towards the sun until you see it move. And what you cannot see but is stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge or a piece of flannel or a piece of lettuce root or a small piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it. And when it comes to the right place, it will stick, and then you can pull it out again. And if it does not come out from what we have said, then take one instrument made of lead in this shape:"
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	"And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can enter the throat more easily, and have the head raised high. And take care not to touch the epiglottis lest it close completely, nor push the bone inside. And it is better for the patient himself to insert the instrument in order to know where the thing is stuck; then he should draw it out gently with the instrument until it comes out."
de la sansue de la gorge	"de la sansue de la gorge"
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes bloodletting is performed without the use of cautery, as I have mentioned in my division, through the use of medications. And if this does not prove beneficial, then observe the throat of the patient towards the sun, and afterwards press the tongue with the instrument that I have described.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see bloodletting, then treat it with a small incision using tweezers or fine forceps.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not prove beneficial, take a goose feather and place it in the throat of the patient, then place the tip of the feather into hot iron, and perform this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient sweats throughout the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full hands of cold water and open the mouth, pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the blood feels the water, let it fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument mentioned in the fumigation of the eye. Do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is thus: take one pot which has live coals within, and let the pot be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, through which the head of the instrument will be placed. Then throw your fumigation into it, and the patient puts the head of the tube into their mouth, closing the mouth so that no smoke escapes but reaches only to the nose; and the stone shall now fall, and if it does not fall then begin the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and drink no water. And thus it will be necessary for the stone to pass through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats blood is like this: when it can be seen, resembling curved tweezers for entering into the throat; and it resembles a crow's beak, and has sharpness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot let go. And here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter on Abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory brings here from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two ways that one is in its same form, and those that it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those places where they are inside the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those in the fundament, and those in fatty tissue are different from those that come to joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the bowels have died according to their fullness; and there are some that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and they do not die according to their fullness, like those that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and they are left until they are quite ripe around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the main member, and if you delay its perforation until it dies, it will harm the main member; where it is near the fundament, pierce it before it dies; and it is not necessary to pierce a hard abscess without proper digestion accomplished, except for that which is near the fundament lest it penetrate deeply and form a fistula; nor can it be healed in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you must know the hour for piercing a boil that has ripened completely, and this is when the pain subsides, and the fever departs, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the bursting and hardening at the top of the boil, and other signs; and you must make the puncture where the boil hangs down most or where it opens more readily, and the puncture should be long like a reed. If the boil is on the hands or feet, or in joints near nerves and arteries, or in any flat place without wrinkle."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where it pleases, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you delay its perforation until it is confirmed by proper digestion accomplished, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it beforehand, the body of the venom will spread out, and it will be filled with much filth; and perhaps the edges and depth of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And some abscesses should be pierced according to the size of the body, according to what is necessary for the members.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must bring small incisions for small abscesses, small perforations; and for large abscesses, large perforations, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut into the heart, and cover; when they have become as hard as earthenware, and have softened, then one must do likewise as one does for boils: And there are such that are split into three angles, and there are such whose covering is done like a mint leaf, as abscesses of the angels; And there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, like soft superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them plainly; and when the abscess is large, and it has drawn much bow, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the bow at once, but draw out a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again afterwards; do this many times gradually, until all the bow comes out; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or elderly decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Sometimes the spirit jumps with the release of the bow, causing the patient to die unexpectedly.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat this chapter with great care. After you have pierced your abscess, open the wound and examine whether the wound from the abscess is small; if it's a full cut, bring linen or old cotton bandages. If it's a large abscess with many openings, stuff each one with a bandage so they meet each other. If there's a piece of skin cut from the abscess that you've cleaned around, fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it's healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	If bleeding occurs during your procedure, bring cold water and vinegar, wet the cloth, and place it repeatedly on the bleeding area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding continues, you should apply treatment and care, using the powders I have mentioned earlier in this book. If it is wintertime, and the place where the abscess is located is very nerve-rich, then you must put warm wet cloths on it, soaked in wine and oil. But if it is summertime, and the area is fleshy, then you should apply wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for three days as we have stated. Then remove the abscess, cleanse it, and treat it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	"And this is what one must know universally about the treatment of boils: I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of boils, and here is that chapter."
des soros	"boils"
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	And on the head, small abscesses appear, like those that are found in the flesh, similar to a goose's gizzard, and there are many such.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and moist like pigeons; and there are also those that are hard and stony to the touch. There is no doubt that if an artery is present.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is that you examine all instruments called 'entromissoire', from which the shape comes later, which thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	But if it contains moisture, you should wipe it with something long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, scrape it without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, because it returns immediately if you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it's present; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and these are the things that remain of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third day, until you know that there is no moisture left; then dress the wound with suitable ointment, until it's clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the boil holds much fat, cut it according to this shape with something long; and throw your bandages on it, scrape all around it, and make sure all your efforts go into drawing out the coat where it resides; and if the artery opposes you, do what I said later.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And likewise do with an abscess if it is hard, and when cutting and healing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	Cutting into a hard and moist abscess makes it easier because there is less blood involved.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are some abscesses whose heads have no moisture, and among these was an abscess that I cut open on the head of an old woman; I found the abscess like a hard, rough, white stone, which could not be broken; and if one had struck it with an axe, it would have done as much harm as striking a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	For other abscesses that come to the head, especially those that occur on the heads of children and at the roots of ears, open them always in the lowest possible place so that they may drain better; and heal them as is necessary.
des scrophules	"scrophules"
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin; sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and they are often connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each boil is properly situated within its own bone, as with the wound and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the types of these boils are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are evil ones that refuse to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Therefore, for the one that appears well-disposed to touch and is similar in color to the flesh, and moves from each part and is not hard to the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the vessel, and is not deep; then you should cut it open on top, scrape it from both sides, and draw out the two lips of the wound with forceps if necessary, as we have said for head abscesses; and remove it bit by bit, ensuring that you do not cut into the nerve or vein, nor slip with the scalpel too deeply, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you work, place powdered vitriol in the wound, or some powders that stop blood flow, hold the wound closed until the abscess quiets down, and the wound softens and begins to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And once the blood is stopped, return to your work until you finish it; then search on your thumb for any small scabs, cut them and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, you should not cut that scab at its base, but tie it with a strong doubled thread and let it fall off on its own without harm; then cover the wound with cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scab, then you must bring together both edges of the wound and stitch them securely, so that there remains no excess due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary for you to understand how to grasp the root of it, and draw forth fire, and then stitch it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold excessiveness, pierce where it opens, and pierce in the manner of those previously mentioned, depending on it. Then apply dressings with ointment and similar things so that they corrupt what remains from corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with anointing around the flesh until it is healthy.
de squinance	"Squinting"
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	"The ancients spoke of the cutting of the throat, but I have never seen it done in our land, and that is what their writings say."
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	"For those who squint, the epiglottis must be avoided; no help is to be given by this means, because all veins and arteries of the sick person are in the mouth or throat."
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	"When the disease is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis in order to avoid suffocation."
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it below three circles or four, with a small cut across between two circles or according to the quantity of the soft palate's cut, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for sectioning the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then extend the skin of the throat throughout the entire neck, then cut the heart until it reaches the throat. Avoid any visible blood vessels and then grasp the soft palate as we have said. This is proven by the cutting of the pharyngeal vein which emits fire from the broken place, and by the loss of voice; leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when the danger of strangulation has passed, bring together the two lips of the wound in the chest and stitch them closed without including the cartilage. Then apply medications that promote the growth of flesh until it is healed."
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	"Albucasis says that one should not perform this procedure until the throat is completely blocked, the patient is judged to be near death, and the fault lies with the air passages."
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then grasp the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow and breathes through the wound, thus avoiding death. And so the ancients ordered that the wound be left open until the heat of the disease has passed, which takes three or four days. Then they commanded that the wound be stitched up and dressed until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting some of the channels of the lung. And I was called to heal her, but found her dead also.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	"I examined the wound and found that there was blood coming from it, and I realized that she had not cut any vein or artery except for the throat, and air was escaping through the wound."
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and stitched the wound and healed it until it was healthy. And there was no other harm to the young woman besides her voice being hoarse, which returned afterwards to its former state; therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis one need not fear.
de la grosse gorge	"Of the enlarged throat"
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This aposteme is called 'hernia of the throat', and it is a large abscess with the color of a liver, most common in women. There are two kinds: natural and accidental; but the natural one has no engine (cause).
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two ways: one is similar to fatty tissue, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from an artery. There should be fear in these cases, but surgery with fire can only be done in those that are small, and it must be proved and searched for throughout the intramuscular area: if you find it as hard as a nut and not connected to any vein, cut it out like you would a boil, and remove all its covering if there is any; then examine everything carefully and treat it as necessary until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	"Of fatty tumors"
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many kinds of boils, all of which I will describe their similarities; and now I must tell you the difference between a boil and an ulcer.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	"I say that an exostosis is hot and febrile until the inflammation has passed, and the putrefaction is complete. Then the fever and heat subside."
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the nodule, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains lymph, which is its own sac and appears according to the color of the body, and begins like a jar, and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, either fatty or moist, and most have the colors I mentioned in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	"When you come to treat a nodule, it is necessary to first examine and explore the entire introitus with an instrument called 'intromitto'"
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining the swellings is that you take the moistest spot you find on the swelling and twist your fingers bit by bit until you know that the point has pierced the core, then according to the size of the swelling; then extract the lancet, being careful not to let anything spill.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture is clear in color, then cut it as I said for other swellings; and if after the lancet no moisture comes forth, know that it is fatty, so cut it in a cross, take it with forceps, and scrape it lightly on each side, guarding the skin where it lies that you draw it out clean with the nodule; and if you cannot draw it out clean, then draw it out in pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If anything remains there, then the wound returns many times; and if a bit remains and the blood begins to fester, then cover the wound with some corrosive waters, bind the wound tightly, apply soothing things to the hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed. And if the wound is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat those that enter the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	"And if the veins beat against you or otherwise, hurry and fill the wound with powdered vitriol, and let it lie for two or three days until the wound rots, and then rest the ebullition of the blood; then return to cauterize what remains of the boil."
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the shapes of the instruments for entering wounds, and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small. There are four square ones called "albaret" and one called "breb". They also come in three sizes to encircle fistulas: large, medium, and small. These are like the needles used to sew up wounds, made of tin, iron, or silver. The golden ones are most valuable and are especially preferred for encircling the openings of fistulas. They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of onions are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are onions that have two loops of three kinds each; and there are also onions with three loops, which are also of three kinds; and there are onions with two loops and onions with one loop only, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these tools are cutting, and there are some that do not cut much more than one side, with which one strips the nerves so as not to injure the vein or nerve; and among these probes are those replied in hands, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are used mostly in fleshy places such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar places; and sometimes another tool is made, like a fistulectomy probe according to this shape, with which blood is staunched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is placed sometimes at the location where veins and arteries are cut, and sometimes they are made according to this large shape:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when those begin to be corrupted, until they resemble female breasts; and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to treat them, should do so according to this form from line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape away the fat and cover the wound with medicine smearing flesh together, then sew up the two lips of the wound and treat it until it heals; and if the breast hangs downwards and is softened due to its size as happens with women, cut it into two parts above through two similar incisions; so that one end holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from this line .b. to line .g.; then scrape away the skin between the two lips and remove the fat, and arrange what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment until it heals; and if it does not heal or if the incision was not completely made because the patient cannot rest or due to bleeding, you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; leave it until it consumes the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	"Regarding boils in the armpits"
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"These boils that appear under the arms are usually hard scrophulæ with corners, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this shape, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when all the bone that is in the boil has been emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and heal it with appropriate ointment until it is healed."
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	"And if the boil resembles a scrofula, then cut it like we have said for incisions of scrofulæ, and if the wound contracts bone, then bring about cautery as we have said before."
de la routure de l’artere	"Regarding the rupture of an artery"
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is severed, and the skin above it is closed, then an abscess often forms, and likewise when a vein is enlarged and there is an abscess; and one can thus recognize this when it is for the artery, so the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your two hands, you sense its hardness; and when it is for the vein, so it appears reddish and inflamed; and it is foolish to cut into this abscess, especially when it is under the buttocks and in the corners and at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one must avoid cauterizing with fire, and especially the head, and also avoid inflaming an artery by cutting through the skin above it; then make an incision at the corners, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed; then place a needle underneath, and pierce it until it comes out on the other side, and tie the artery with two threads in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then prick the point between the two ties with an introducer until the blood flows out there, and remove the abscess; then apply a bandage in such a way that the ligature falls off; then treat it with ointment suitable for this purpose until it is healed. And if the abscess is due to an incision of the vein, then you must tie your hand to the abscess everywhere on the skin, then place the needle underneath where you are holding with your hand, and pierce it through, with one double thread so that you can pull it out from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have said, tying the ligature of one of two parts with two heads of the threads; and if you doubt whether the threads have been sewn correctly, then insert another needle under all the threads along the entire length of the abscess at the incision point of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cut into the abscess until the superfluity comes out; then cut away the superfluity from the heart and leave what is tied.
