Then place a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, then apply bandages and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	"Abscesses of the nerves"
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	"So just like abscesses come from the artery and vein when they are pierced or by excessive work, abscesses also come to nerves when they are wounded, and similar things."
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens most often to the shoulders and toes, and in all places where there are joints; it is the serious swellings, and its color appears like the color of the body, and it is found in many dispositions without pain. And when it is pressed strongly, the patient feels pain, but not deep within the body, rather beneath the chest; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and one that is in joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps contraction would occur; and those that are on the head or forehead, make the skin smooth.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is small, then grasp it with tongs and cut it at its root; but if it is large, then suspend it from an onion, scrape it off, then cleanse and join the wound together with stitches, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	"On large hanging pouches"
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in bellies and not elsewhere; and it is an illness called 'fungus' due to its similarity; and the roots are fine, and the heads large; and there are some small ones and very large ones. I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, with no difference between them, they were white, with fine roots and jagged edges, and moisture constantly flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found one to be XVIII ounces heavy, the other VI З. The work of the incision is such that you should look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist with a subtle root; then cut it at the spatula's wide edge, and have the cautery ready by fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	But when cutting comes too much blood flow, if your blood fails you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient fearful and afraid of iron incision, take a well-made thread of lead, and tie it around the artery as we have said, leaving it for two days. Then restrain it, and do not cease pulling on the thread of lead until you cut the artery, then pull it out without effort; if the roots are large, fear cutting itself for the belly, but you can well cut halfway, then cauterize so it does not return; then treat the wound, guarding that you do not cut the sheath which is reddish in color and poor in sense, containing milk secretion.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an enchanted aposteme, and I will come to the cure of cancer later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the swelling occurs from cauterization of a wound or tear in the scrotum, and is on the belly, and in some cases affects the testicles as happens with other injuries, or from blood coming from veins or arteries, according to what is said before, or from windiness; and if it's from a tear in the scrotum and an opening in the testicle, then the color of the swelling resembles the color of the flesh, and it's a light thing without pain, and has various openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the outlet of the intestines, then it is more diverse. And when you press it with your fingers it disappears and then returns. And sometimes it is hard and enlarged greatly at the entrance of the bath and from intense labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's from moisture, it's a light thing, and opens up well when you press it with your hand, without constraining; and if it's from blood, then the swellings are large and hard, and appear according to their quantity; and if it's from windiness, it's soft to the touch, and the appearance is such that you should look to see if it's from arterial or venous blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary for you to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I told you in the chapter on boils, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or for the boil, then you must command the patient to tie his loincloth, and be stretched out completely straight, then kneel at the foot of the bed; then he should lie down on his back between your hands, then go around the spot that you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the boil upwards with all the great unguent; then tie it tightly around with a strong thread or a strong silk cord, and let the knot be well fastened; then open half of the boil stretched out over the ligature, and put your index finger inside, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught in the ligature, untie it and put the intestine back into its place in the belly; and if you find the boil, take it at the root and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, and attach two strong threads, and insert the two needles crossed where you pierced them; then hold the boil in four places on the needles, and if you see it swell, remove the needles and leave the spot until it rots, and scrape away the dead flesh; or cut it when it is ripe and rotted, then treat the place as necessary, and cut open the boil as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as necessary, and sew up the wound.
dou chancre	Here is an old French recipe for treating a chancre (a type of ulcer):
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	"Of the kinds of cancer we have spoken about in the section, and how one must treat them with medicines, and how to avoid the cure by iron; and we say that cancer which has invaded the marrow requires great caution in its treatment. The ancients said that when cancer is located where it can be removed, like those on the breast or hip, and similar locations, it should all be cut out at the beginning. But when it is large and old, do not approach it, for I have never seen anyone cured of it; nor has anyone else before me."
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And the operation, when it is in a location where it can be removed, as we have said, involves purging the patient of black bile. Then make him vomit if he shows signs of repletion, and then prepare the patient in a good place to perform the operation. Then cut out your incisions or cancer, and remove all hair around it, and remove everything without leaving anything behind. Let the blood flow freely, and squeeze the wound with your hand or some other object, and if the bleeding is too much from the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops. Then heal it with another cure until it is healed."
de ydropisie	I have not found any mention of "ydropisie" in the text you provided. Is there a specific section or topic related to this that you would like me to summarize?
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already spoken in the division about the likenesses of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is done, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only 'eclites' [dropsy] is mentioned; and one should not touch with iron in these two likenesses: namely, tympanites and hippocrates, for they are deadly things; therefore when you treat this likeness of dropsy called 'eclites' with medicines, and the cure does not help, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as consumption and similar things; do not touch him with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient to be of strong virtue, and he has no other disease but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus: raise the patient upright on your hands, and the assistants press the belly outwards by pushing water at the lowest part of the breast, then take the spatula spinous according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut in two.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And then pierce the skin with this tool, and be careful not to cut so deep that it reaches the intestines when you insert it, nor should it cause bleeding. Then observe whether dropsy has entered near the intestines: if so, make your incision three fingers' breadth directly below the navel; but if dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the belly button; and if it's due to worms, make it on the right side. Ensure that the patient does not lie upon the incision so that superfluities do not run into this weak area. Then pierce all the skin with this tool, insert it, and lift your hand so that the spatula is between the skin and the fascia just as in flaying, to the depth of a nail or somewhat around. Then pierce the fascia until the spatula reaches the empty space, which is the location of water; then draw forth this tool, and into this opening insert this tool whose shape is thus:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a subtle silver chain, and is of light arrow or iron, and has in the lower part one small hole; and on one side three holes; and two on another side; and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision with which writers cut feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	And at the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it lets it now fall on the instrument; empty then a half or a third part, for if you empty more than necessary at this time, perhaps the patient will die from the dissolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the sick person's virtue signify, and his pulse; then draw the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now by the heart that stops the hole that is on the face, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then begin the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient enduring this, and draw a little quantity of water; do this for some days, and take care not to let it remain too long but just a drop of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water on them, then cure it with hot burial or sand, and often sweat, bath or sun, and coloring to drink; and cure it with drying medicines until it is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	"Regarding the swelling of the penis:"
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without any opening in their penis, or with a small one, or one not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary that it be pierced at once with the finest stilette according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place the fine platinum cap into the opening and tie it up and hold it thus for 3 or 4 days. When it wants to urinate, remove the cap and let it do so, then put it back on; sometimes no cap may be needed as the urine coming from within does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose wound is small are treated with the cloth of lead, as we have said; it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its place are burned, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating until they raise their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the bladder, and this is a harmful condition.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And the method of operation is this: the patient lies on his back, then lift up the tip of the penis and cut it like a feather until the opening falls in the middle, as it should. Be careful not to let too much blood flow out, for this happens often; if it does happen, stop the bleeding with whatever stops bleeding, and heal the wound until it is completely healed."
des pustules de la verge	"Regarding the blisters on the penis:"
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Many times these blisters appear on the penis, forming an ugly appearance of skin. Some are malignant and others are not; they must be taken with a very fine onion, cut out, and all cleaned up, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then treat with diafinicon ointment until they are completely healed."
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is malignant, of foul color and stinking, then you must bring fire cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it out, and if the wound is on top of the penis, with part inside the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the wound that is inside; and when it is healed, then treat the one outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if you treat them together, the head of the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come into its skin and scrotum; so all that is black and corrupted must be cut away, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour mixed with grated pomegranate rind and figs, then treat it with other remedies until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a discharge of blood occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And the cauteries help in two conditions together: namely, for the discharge of blood and corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and drawn back, then you should insert or conduct through it a tube of lead, and let the patient piss among it. And when the skin at the head of the penis becomes sore, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or which occurs because of a wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with the hairy instrument until the ligature is untied and the penis is delivered from all parts. And if it is difficult to separate these, then you should scrape it somewhat with the spatula at the head of the penis and skin; then carefully dissect between them, and put a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water there, so that it does not become sore again.
de la circoncision	"Of circumcision"
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	"Circumcision is not like other wounds that heal by themselves; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary to do the best and easiest work for salvation."
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	"I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children because it was not customary in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience."
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	"Because I have seen the greatest part of the masters and seniors who performed circumcisions using only one knife, sometimes for boys and sometimes with a novacula; thus it happens that the glans remains bare because there are two layers [of skin], and sometimes they cut the upper one and leave the lower one."
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	"But then they cover it [the glans], and the pain is doubled; and at the time of washing, the tip of the member is not securely exposed; and sometimes during the washing of the wound, the instrument slips and wounds the operation, and many times they are born like this so that they do not need any further dressing, as I have seen."
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	"Concerning the washing that is done on boys with all the length of thread, I have found through experience that this method is good because boys cut evenly both above and below."
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand thus, cut evenly throughout the whole time; but let the thread be well stretched around the skin; and make the manner of the first operation such that you cause the child to think, if it hears, that you are doing nothing but tie the thread around the stick only, and then let him enjoy all the ways that you can; then make him stand upright between your hands, and hide the forceps between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the stick and blow onto the heart, and pull it up until the head of the stick is inside; then clean it well from the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the left side with a double thread, then tie it under the first knot to the other knot; and hold it with two fingers by the second knot near the pouch and index finger, and cut between the two knots, then quickly raise the heart up and pull out the head of the stick; then let the blood flow freely, for this is the mucus; and put powder on it and on the powder a strip of gauze stuck with a cooked egg yolk tempered with rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	"The form of the foreskin at the time of washing should be like this: the two layers [of skin] should be thin and cut evenly, and each layer should be as large as the middle finger."
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	"The error in washing is when the glans is inside the incision; therefore, you must stretch it with your thumb before the edges adhere and close up, then cut it evenly; if you cannot hold it with your thumb, use tweezers to cut it."
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	"And if three days have passed and the skin below the penis is swollen, let it be until the inflammation has subsided, then gently scrape off the scab; cut it as much as you can move it, but be careful not to harm the penis itself."
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then treat the wound with the soothing powder that we have described earlier, and if too much of the glans is cut and it retracts upwards, do not worry about it; treat it as we have said until it heals."
dou retenement de l’urine	Of urine retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or coagulated blood, or bowels, or flesh born, or similar things, as we have said in the division. And if the urine is not released, and you see that there is retention due to a stone that lies in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to bend over his knees; and let him put his feet on his back, and extend his belly from above where the back is located, and let the patient constrain himself as much as he can; and therefore the neck of the bladder is forced upwards to expel the stone above, so that the urine may be released. And if it does not come forth, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments called 'syringe', whose form is as follows: let it be of fine, light silver, like the feather of a bird; and let the tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of issuing urine is thus: Take one doubled thread, and tie it to the top of a wad of wool or cotton, and insert the thread's end into the syringe; then cut off the excess wool and place it up to the syringe's top, then oil the syringe with oil or butter and dove's egg, and make the patient sit on a seat, and rise his bladder and penis with moistened oil and olive oil and hot water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis upward towards the belly; then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and when the patient feels it reach the empty space, and if this is not done correctly, it may be because the duct it passes through is twisted; then pull out the thread with all the wool wad by wad, and let the urine follow the wool, then remove the syringe, and make the urine flow; and repeat the process until the bladder is emptied, and the patient feels relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When the bladder is injured or contains blood, or is filled with decay and you see water and medicine dripping out of it, then use all the instruments called "clepsydra", its shape is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the high places are raised so that the medicine cup fits well without additional support, allowing for drawing out moisture when needed, and inserting when necessary. When you observe your medicines entering the bladder, place the spout of the syringe in the moisture, and draw out the fluid within. Then strongly reinsert the tube, so the moisture enters and reaches the bladder, making the patient feel it. This is the shape of the delicate clyster used to administer a clyster to the bladder: thus it is here.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and below it has one breast where the strings hang. Then take a sheep's bladder and put into it the moisture with which you wish to administer the clyster to the bladder. Then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a doubled thread, and heat this moisture on the fire until it boils. Then insert the spout of the clyster into the tube, and press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered it, so that the patient feels it has reached the bladder. And if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it, and pierce it roundly around the edge. Then insert a strong thread into these holes, and gather the circle together like a funnel, and put within it what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it onto the instrument. And do as you have done with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	de la moistor
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of treating stones and extracting them together with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between stones that are stuck in the kidneys and all their signs, and in which stones surgery should be performed; and in the bladder and in the urethra; and I will tell you about it clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones which are stuck in the bladder happen more often to children, and this is a sign that urine flows out of the bladder appearing like urine in its fineness; and it opens easily, and the patient grates his urethra, and he frequently pants, and then he becomes rigid; and many times these are the cause of inflammation. And it is easy to cure stones in children until they are four years old, but difficult in old people, and moderate in young people, those between youth and old age. And it is easier to treat those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by enema to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For sometimes it hinders seeking the stone
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lower them and move them below, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it rises from its high place; then have him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then search for it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut upon the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the touch of all, then moist your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is fully grown; and put it in his anus, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press upon it with your finger, and push it towards that side where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out his right hand with the scrotum upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the scrotum in the part where the incision is made; then I put the spatula copant, which is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between what is between the thighs and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; and let it be straight upon the stone, and your two hands always upon the fundament, and let the blow of the hammer be such that it is wide at the front and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; by chance the pressure might cause the stone to expel without labor; and know that there are stones with angles and margins: those are difficult to remove; and there are some that are beneath, similar to a grape, round, from which the exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	Therefore, for those stones that have angles and margins, make the cut wider; and if it does not expel, then you must extract with tongs which are like a chisel at the end, to move and grasp the stone so that it does not escape; or you put underneath it a subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot maneuver thus, then widen the small hole where the passage is, and if blood flows out, then stop it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first place the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut upon it, then let it expel, and afterwards extract the smaller ones if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then one must make a larger cut.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	If two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out continuously from where the wound cannot heal. Nevertheless, strive to draw it out with forceps, or cut it with pincers, until you pull it out in pieces. And when you have completed your work, then dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it up, and lay upon it a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to cool the hot inflammation. Then swathe the patient around his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie him, then rinse the wound very well with oil and water, then apply ointment of diaphoretic balm and ointment of Basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot inflammation comes to the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and urine is retained in such a way that it cannot pass out with the urine: then make an incision into the wound, and extract that blood, for if any remains there, it will corrupt the bladder. Then cleanse the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and aid him in every way that you know until he is healthy. And it is necessary that all the times that you treat him, you bind his two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it's in the path of the tube, and stuck inside, and urine cannot come out; then do what I said before, that you cut it many times, except this time use a curette to perform the cutting.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod made in this shape and having three points sharpened into one piece of charcoal:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take some thread and tie it around the tube below the stone so that it cannot move back into the bladder. Then insert the drill into the tube gently until it reaches the stone. Then turn the drill in your hand against the stone a little bit at a time, until you can pierce the stone from the other side. Then urine will soon come out, and then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is still inside the tube.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken and comes out with the urine, then the patient is healed. And if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders it, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then make an incision in the tube at the stone between the two threads, then extract it with forceps, untie the thread, and clean the wound of any congealed blood; and continue treating it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens sometimes that a stone becomes lodged in women, and if it does happen occasionally, its cure is difficult, and it is prohibited for three reasons: one is because perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-informed who dares to uncover herself before physicians, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that sometimes one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more hidden than that of the man, therefore it must make a deeper cut, and there is great fear involved. And if you need someone for this, then you should take a skilled midwife, and barely can she be found, and if you cannot find one, look for at least an expert physician; and present her with a wise woman knowledgeable in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to perform what you command concerning the examination of the stone; and observe very carefully whether the woman is virgin: then she must place her thumb on the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should press it down with her thumb, and recommend that she places her thumb in the vulva of the patient, and feel and press her left hand strongly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder downwards until she reaches the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the groin, where it is moved and well displayed, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move your hand above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then place the chisel in the incision, if you feel the stone so close to the wound that the stone can come out through fire, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know these similarities in order to know the outcome
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if blood wins you over, then put ground vitriol in place, and hold it there for an hour until the blood is stanched; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have tools ready that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to help you in your task; and if blood wins you over again, and it comes from the artery that was cut, then put powder on the wound and hold it with bandages and cloths, and do not recommence this, and leave the stone alone and do not pull it out, lest by chance the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the wound can be borne again, then return to your task until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	Carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquous hernia is nothing other than an accumulation of moist or white matter that is under the heart of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "spermatozoa," and sometimes it is actually in the wall of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg. And this is the skin of the testicle between the white spermatozoa that we have spoken about; and this does not happen unless there is pressure.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the cause of this hernia is weakness in the testicles, which allows this matter to become spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it arises from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: where it is declining towards jaundice, or colorless, or black, or watery white, and these are more; and these are signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is whitish like we have said, then the abscess is ripe, as long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess is ripe with part of the egg, and because of this one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the whites, one feels it well. Therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all the intruding squarely, from which its shape is here before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introduction, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cut it with iron, the patient must be healthy according to his power and the fullness of his body; then have him lie on his back, on something slightly high, and put many cloths underneath him. Then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on the right, and extend the wand to one of the two ribs of the heart of the joints. Then take the spatula and cut the skin of the joints in its proper place, from the long incision near the hilt, and let your incision be straight, dividing the skin of the joints up to the whites. Then carefully scrape it according to your power; then pierce the white full of water with a wide hole, and drain out all the water, then put on your bandages, and stretch the white upwards; and do not touch the heart of the joints, but only the white. Cut everything evenly or in pieces from its edge carefully, so that if you do not cut it well, the water will return. And if the egg slips during your work, reset it in its place when you have finished the work of the white. Then sew the two leaves of the heart of the joints together with a suture, then cure it like other wounds until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find that the egg is corrupted by another illness, then tie up the vessels hanging there to prevent bleeding. Then cut through the rib cage along with everything attached to it and remove the egg. Treat it as described above.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if water is gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first evenly, then squeeze out the blood, and place in the wound clean wool moistened in rose oil. And put on top of the two wounds another wool moistened in wine and oil, and put over them doubled cloths, and bind it all together according to this form
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and fill them with wool lint according to this shape and have them sewn together at the waistband of the breeches, and one end should lie on top of the buttocks up to the back, and the other at the wrist area; and the two ends should be held over the two angles, and all the bandage should be gathered in the loop of the breeches. And sometimes this branch is medicated with cauterization instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take one scalpel cautery instrument, and cut into the skin of the wounds, and heat it as we have said so that the white blister which contains the water becomes visible; then take the cautery according to this form, and prick that blister once with it, and scrape off this blister with this fine hot cautery
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in every way that you can, until you remove all; and ensure that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more saving; and move carefully to avoid blood loss, and cover the wounds with dressings; and if anything opposes you, whether it's an abscess, blood flow, or other things, then treat what opposes you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and cannot endure this procedure because of its horrifying nature, then perform a perforation, as I tell you. And when you are certain that there is no sign of aquatic humor, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then cut through the abscess at the lower part with a wide scalpel, and insert the perforation tube into the long bone of the body; ensure the hole is large enough for all the fluid to flow freely. Then place cotton on the wound and bind it, leaving room for the remaining fluid to drain. Next, dress the wound until it heals. And if the bandage does not allow fluid to escape through the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a pen or the instrument used to treat hydrocele, the shape of which is shown above. Then enlarge the wound and know that the fluid will collect again after six months or so, and when it collects as before, the patient's days will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	"Treatment of an abscess on the testicles"
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this vein there is fear and many dispositions, therefore it seems to me that it would be better if one lets it alone; and I will tell you the work and the similitudes of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come upon the body, especially upon the testicles; this is very common.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known that from sour and bitter superfluity spread over the joints or from percussion; and the color of the abscess follows the color of the body; and it does not find pain; and the abscess is severe; and sometimes there are few painful and piercing abscesses, and with foul color, and some come from an artery or inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and one must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That which is made from inflammation of a vein is known by its disposition at the expression of the touch of the fingers; and one can well make the incision upon this semblance and upon other parts; and it is that you cut the joint of the bones, then stretch the egg upwards, and let go the white mucus through the suspensory ligament in all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hard-boiled with these hairs attached, then you should remove the egg, and its shell; if it's air-filled at the surface, or in that which is inside the vessels, then you must deliver all of this membrane, and roundly remove the shell.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	"And if the origin of the growth is behind, you must cut it all out and remove the egg as we have said."
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And once your operation is complete, cover the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then dress it with other dressings until it heals."
de l’aposteme des coions	"Treatment of an abscess on the testicles"
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a boil covered by an wrapping resembling wool, with softening of the tissues, and the patient cries out when it moves; yet the treatment for this disease is quite fearful just as those mentioned earlier, but nonetheless we will tell you its operation according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	The patient should sit on an elevated seat. Then place the suspensory ligament of the testicles downward on your two fingers near the vessel close to the penis, and grasp it with your master finger, extending it firmly. Next, cut widely across the skin with a sharp scalpel over the vessels until they are exposed. Then strip back the skin from both sides as we have described for the extraction of temporal arteries. Insert a needle with double thread where the vein emerged first, tie it to the initial point, then tie it again at the other end. Cut along the middle correctly according to the length of the body and remove the corrupted moisture. Then treat the wound like others where a bowel has been inserted, ensuring that no vessels are cut which nourish one of the testicles; for through these no harm comes, but if veins come from all vessels, then draw the testicles from all vessels so that the scrotum does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels.
de la routure dou syfac	"On the rupture of the sinews"
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The event of this rupture happens due to the cutting that comes from below, or the stretching over the belly in the area of the groin, which causes the intestines to descend through one of the openings; and this opening is either from the caecum or from its stretching. There are two ways these ruptures come about, many times: either by impact, or jumping, or heavy lifting, or similar causes; And the sign when it's due to stretching of the caecum is that it happens gradually over a long time and does not happen suddenly; and the abscess is even all the way to its depth because the caecum presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	"And the sign that it is a section of the sinew is that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and there is diverse inflammation apparent under the skin near the surface, due to the issue of the intestine and the body's retreat from the sinew."
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	"And sometimes the loops also descend with the intestine, becoming trapped there and causing great pain to the patient, especially when they are pressed."
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	"And in these cases of iron poverty, why one must avoid this cure:"
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	The manner of performing this procedure is that you instruct the patient to put their hand inside the wound if they can; then lie on their back between your hands and raise their thighs; then stretch the heart upwards and cut all the long skin of the groin; then insert hooks of the hips as needed to open the wound, so large that the egg can come out; then scrape off the caecum which is under the skin of the groin until the hard white caecum is exposed on all sides; then put your right index finger into what leads towards the groin between the first caecum and the second one behind the bladder, and pull apart what is behind the bladder and between the second caecum; and then move your right hand inside the skin of the groin, and stretch the white caecum upwards with your left hand, and lift the bladder together with all the caecum towards the hips; and instruct the assistant to hold up the bladder and loosen what is behind it; and check with both hands if there is any intestine wrapped around the hard white caecum, and if you find anything, put it back inside the belly; then take a needle with one thick thread made of X threads, and insert it into the back part of the caecum which is after the skin of the groin; after the hips, cut the strings that appear until there are four strings; then tie them together in the shape of a cross, and tie the caecum with two strong ties, as we have said before, which is under the skin of the groin; then wrap the strings of the threads and tie them firmly with two ties so that no vessel that feeds it can enter there, and no abscess may come; and put the tie again according to the first tie two fingers away from it; and after these two ties leave one hand's width of caecum which is under the skin of the groin; and after everything else follow the roundness that the bladder has; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the groin until blood flows, and the bowels, as we have said before; then bring moistened wool in oil and put it on the wounds, and bring the tie that we have spoken about.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	"And sometimes the white sinew that we have spoken about is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding."
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Because this happens many times, and leaves the lien until it falls by itself; and if it delays in falling, then raise it with warm water, and put on what we have said until it falls; then treat the wound with another cure until it is perfectly healed.
