de hernie carnouse	Carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	"I never saw anyone who dared to perform this operation by iron."
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch that is bound together with the vis in such a way that you tie the vessels after cutting them lightly on the underside; then cut in between and treat the abscess of what opens until the vessels fall; and cure it as we have said until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes rupture occurs in the angles as we have said, and the area opens up; and no part of the intestines should come out at the joints, but if any do come out, it is little and can be repaired immediately. However, if it remains too long in this state, then gangrene or syphilis will form until the intestines come out; and this happens due to the extension of the syphilis which is in the angles as we have said, because it becomes stretched, softens and swells the area and opens up. The cure for this is cautery, as we have mentioned before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: lie the patient on their back between your hands, then cut into the swollen area of the rupture with a knife according to the amount of three fingers wide; then remove the syphilis that is under the skin that is affected, then take a rod and place it over the open area of the syphilis, and press it deep into the abdomen. Then sew up the two open areas of the syphilis on top of the head of the rod, sewing both together. Then remove the head of the rod, but do not cut any more of the syphilis or extend the wound or anything else, as I have explained to you in the cure for the rupture of the intestines; then treat it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cauterize with fire, cleanse it and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syringe is tightly closed and has no opening during dislocation. The cauterization is done at this stage and is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin over the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin over the joints becomes softened in some people because the tissues inside are softened, and it is unpleasant to see. When you want to treat it, make the patient lie on his back, and cut away the softened skin from the natural skin. Then sew the two lips together with one stitch, and if necessary, first sew the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches. Then cut between the stitches and cure it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	And know that castrations are forbidden in our law, and therefore I would like not to speak of it in this book; but there are two reasons why it is necessary: the first is so that a doctor can answer when asked about it and its treatment, and the second because we often need to castrate certain beasts for our aid, such as goats, sheep, cats, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method that we do by attraction, make the beast sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then grasp them with your hand until they return and you can no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	On castration by cutting: you must first tie the beast, then press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensiony ligament, and cut each testis once when they are well exposed; leave some portion of the scrotum and the subtle tunic that is over the vas deferens; this method of castration is more cruel than that done by attraction because it leaves no chance for some part of the testicles to remain, which could cause the beast to desire lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism occurs in men in two ways: one is such that between the two testicles opens also like the figure of a woman's nature, or there is hair, and sometimes it emits urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way in women, they have on their pubis both a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you cut away all the attached skin, and dress it like other wounds; in the second way, for men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Tengnèye
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigine is attached skin on the natural part that is too unsightly to see; some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you shave off the excess skin of the tentigine with your hand or a razor, cutting it lightly; and do not cut too deep, lest bleeding occur, then dress the wound until it heals. And there is another skin that grows at the mouth of the womb, the navel, and sometimes extends far, appearing like a cow's udder, whence the ancients called it 'cow disease.'
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must strike it, as we have discussed the cauterization, and continue treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	Erratique
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erroneous if the nature of the woman's womb is not pierced, or if the opening is small; and it is either natural from birth, or accidental due to illness that has occurred there; or it is caused by adhered flesh, or thin and subtle skin, or thick skin, and occurs deep in the marrow, or on the sides, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes flowers from being had; and its detection is through inspection of the womb.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears close by, then it seeks either your right side or left ear.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is thin and subtle skin, and it is close to the two lips, then act quickly, and thus: place your two index fingers together, with the woman lying on her back, legs spread; then press the two lips firmly until the thin skin is raised, and is over the swelling; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it there, and have the woman lie on her face each day so that it cannot adhere.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the shoulder blade is hard and thick, then you must strike it with a mallet resembling a laurel leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bandage is made of flesh, suspend it from an ox's horn and strike it with a mallet. Have ready stanching medicines such as aloes, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with yolk of egg; then apply a broad copper cauldron so that the wound cannot heal up; and do this for a long time, then apply a dry linen bandage; then treat it with other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the flesh comes gangrene, then it must be cut according to this manner, unless it is a blackened abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the blackened abscess that is in the gangrene, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Haemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that commonly occur without cause, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard. We have already spoken in the division about their likenesses, signs, and now I will speak of those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are deeply embedded in the flesh, and cannot be felt, then iron is not the cure.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those at the mouth of the anus, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Then you must put the woman in a cold house, then stretch out the hemorrhoid with forceps, and cut it at its root, then apply powder of medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia and dragon's blood and frankincense and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water. And if bleeding occurs, then have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gall nuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, then apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without piercing; then take linen, and soak it in comfrey juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ripe, then treat the area with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp peak, so you must cover it as I have said earlier; and then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	"Regarding boils of the skin"
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess occur in the buttocks, such as cancer and pointed abscesses, herpes, boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned earlier in this section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must discuss in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the buttocks, which is not like those that are filled with pus; and if you wish to know how to work with fire, first observe whether the abscess is growing at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make it bleed until the pain ceases; then seat the patient on a chair, with two small stools where they may recline, and prop them up against their back and bring their feet together at the thigh level; let their thighs be spread apart, place their arms beneath their knees, and tie them securely with a good bandage; then squeeze the bag towards the right side, and bring forth the instrument used to open the mouth of the wound, about which there will follow its form later on; and it is necessary that when you are bringing forth this instrument, you first insert the rod in order to know the depth of the wound, so that whatever enters may not go deeper than intended nor harm the patient; and if the instrument is too large, then cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause discomfort; it is necessary that they place the funnel of the instrument on top and moisten the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess opens, and it is gently cut with a scalpel in the hand, it must then be covered at its head, using a broad bandage. And when the wound is empty, you must put moistened tents into it made from rose oil or dry green oil; place them deep into the wound's marrow, and lay them on top of the marrow and around the linen cloth moistened with water where mallow or mallows have been cooked; then treat it after two days with an appropriate ointment until it is healed. And sometimes lift the bandage and the wound by enema using water and honey, and then with water in which lilies and celery roots have been cooked; then return to treating with the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is deep in the marrow, you must avoid cauterizing with fire, but treat it as we have said in its division.
de l’enfantement	Childbirth is a natural process by which a woman gives birth to a child after carrying the baby in her womb for approximately nine months. The following is an overview of the stages of childbirth and some traditional remedies used to ease discomfort:
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	First, the midwife must know the signs of natural childbirth: when she sees a woman pressing downwards and desiring to smell the air, then the child hastens to come out. Know that this childbirth is according to nature's form, with the child's head emerging first, followed by the afterbirth. When you see these signs, gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly, for when it descends onto its head, the afterbirth follows with it, and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities through good cleansing. Any child that comes otherwise is not born naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because sometimes it happens on his feet, and the body or shoulder catches fire, and the hands, or it happens on his belly, or else, and by chance they are turned over onto his neck, and in other unfortunate shapes; so it is necessary that the bath be wise and subtle in these things, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how to aid him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	"If the infant comes forth naturally upon its head, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool or let women hold her; and raise her nature of oil or fenugreek cooked. Then place the little spatula between her thighs whose shape follows:"
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the membranes and scrape with its nail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to administer a suppository of fennel with sesame oil to the woman; then make her sneeze with condimentum and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out first, then you must gently push them back little by little; and if they cannot enter, then make the woman sit on a chair, and raise her feet up high; then tilt the chair onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the tilting; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dying, then cut off the hands at the joint that was placed there earlier, and extract the child, and reset it properly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	At the birth of a child onto its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, one should raise it up. Then slowly turn it a little until it is even. Then take one of the feet and extend it a little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it can jump up to its hips, have someone hold it, and make it sneeze with mustard. If fire follows, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	"And if he does not sneeze as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is according to its natural shape."
Car adonques ist il legierement.	"For then it is easily put back in place."
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if fire does not come as we have said, then take musk, aloe juice, sesame oil, and melted gum, grind them all together in one mortar. Put this ointment on the woman's private parts, then have her sit in warm water up to her hips until she is moist below. Then put a collar of myrrh on her and place it under her, leaving it for an hour. Then have her sit on a chair, make her sneeze, hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, as the child will now come forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	"From the exit of the child onto its knees"
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, then the midwife puts her hands softly and gently; then she covers him on his neck, and let his feet hang down, and let him lie on the bed; and fold his hands softly and gently, and then she places his hands on his belly, and removes the pillows underneath until he is positioned correctly below; and if the child does not cry out, then take his feet and move them vigorously, then move his belly up, then place your hands there; and wipe the child softly and gently; and tell the woman to hold herself until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	"Regarding the child that comes out of the womb with one hand hanging down:"
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer bringing back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, and push her legs apart vigorously; then prepare the moss that I have described; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, then try to bring back the hand; and wipe the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, and tell her to hold herself until the child comes out further.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth opening onto her buttocks, and has spread out its hands, and turned its face toward its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient take his hand, then turn it slowly and gently; and when it is even, so place upon its nature muscillaige of altee and oil, as we have said, then instruct him to move it slowly; and when you have done this, then make him sit on the seat, and instruct him to sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way for the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When heat comes in this manner to the secondine, then cut the secondine with your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child leans on its face and neck, then cut from the cheek so that it is not held back, and the child dies; then put the child inside until you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to lie down several times: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Regarding the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, sometimes two at a time, and rarely three or four; this is not uncommon
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things and do not live if little named; I know these, that they multiply greatly, and they are desired by the syfac which divides them, which is attached to the cheek; and sometimes they also come out naturally like a tooth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they move out loudly, then treat them as we have said, and let the servant be skilled, and do quickly and easily what she does; and act thus as he knows how to move for healing.
de plusors enfans	"of many children"
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb for one, two, three, four, five, six, seven times, or even more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise Glorious One, and it is necessary that the servant knows everything about this, for similar things may happen; so act according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	"of a dead child"
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman with the dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and there is no discharge, and you are compelled by your duty to use your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and does not have an accident or fears death; then it is necessary that the woman lie on her back, and that her head be tilted downwards, and her legs raised up; and the servant take two sheets, or tie them to the bed so she cannot slide down with the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils containing musk, althea, fenugreek, and linseed, then the servant anoint his hands with these oils and musks; then insert them gently into the womb, then twist it once where you inserted your fingers that are suitable for this purpose, and be careful that the child descends headfirst; then fix the sheet in its eyes or neck or mouth or throat or beard or fundament or near the ribs, and if the descent is feet first, fix it to the thigh or side; and it is necessary that you hold the sheet with your right hand, and place the curve between your left elbow and arm, and insert it gently up to where it is empty; this is the shape of the sheet.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then thrust against the other side once, or twice if needed, so that the extraction is even; then stretch it evenly by moving from one side to the other, for easy removal, and let the claws be even for holding firmly, as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some part remains, then anoint the bailiff's two fingers with oil and place them in that part, and pull the other part; and if none remain, then put this claw higher up and do thus until it all comes out without force.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back because of constraint, then you must wrap a cloth around it until all is out; then cut at the joint of the sole or on the side, and likewise you must do with the other foot.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and narrow at the outlet, or there is a sharp-pointed assembly at its top, then you must place the spatula between your fingers and cut off the point and remove it; or round it with the tool called "almidach", whose form comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and likewise do if the child has a large natural head; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head does not come out and is pressed by force, then cut it until the moisture at the foot of the outlet comes out; and if it cannot come out, then cut it in pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	"And if the child is presenting by the feet, then the extraction will be easy, and the presentation at the mouth of the womb will also be easy."
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or breast, then you must pull it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and open the belly or breast until the moisture there flows out; and if other members are removed but the head remains, then place your hand deep into the marrow, and draw it up to the mouth of the marrow; then insert one or two fingers, and draw it out forcefully; and if the mouth of the marrow is constricted due to a hot abscess that has come there, then you must not work there, but rather arrange moist and fatty things; and the arrangement should include plasters, and such softening and moistening waters.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is lying on its side and you cannot make it lie flat, then arrange what we have said for a living child; and if there is no power to do so, then draw it out piece by piece, leaving nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if they come about the things that we have said regarding hot abscesses; and if discharges of blood occur, then let it be placed in cold water, restricting them, and other remedies are brought about.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	"I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been bitten by another, and the latter had died as a result."
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	"After many days, she developed an infection in her genitals, which swelled until it opened and began to emit a foul odor."
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	"I was summoned to treat her, and after examining her for some time, I could not heal the wound."
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	"I applied a poultice with strong drawing properties, and eventually two bones came out."
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	"I was very astonished at this, since the belly has no bones."
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	"Then I thought that these must be the bones of a dead child."
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I saw the wound and drew out many bones until the woman was much improved; and the woman lived for a long time thereafter, but sometimes a little bit of bone came out of its place. And I have recorded this chapter only because when masters find something unusual, they know how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	"to replace the womb in its proper position"
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	"Hereafter comes the form of the forceps, with which books are opened; and there are two turns at the two ends of the two handles."
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more delicate than the restraint, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood should be two fingers wide, and its edge one finger wide, and half a palm long; and inside the two hinges there should be two joints of this same wood, which are fastened on both ends, being half a palm long or a little more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the wound to open it when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling tongs; and it should have two heads with two attachments each, one palm long and two fingers wide. When you open the mouth of the instrument completely, have the woman sit on the bed, her feet dangling and her legs spread apart. Then insert both attachments together into the mouth, holding the head of the instrument under her thighs. Then open your hand fully along the instrument, just as you would with tongs, according to how much you want to open the mouth of the instrument so that the ball may come out as she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and multiplied in their likeness; and when the physician has prepared them, the more hastily the work is done, the higher they are among men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain any instrument that you have not prepared, because their necessity cannot be excused.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, you should command the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with gentian, and constrain your hands over her mouth and nose. If she expels it thereby, that is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, then take the pot, and make a hole in its cover, and place herbs inside that can open the mouth of the dead person, such as calamint, rue, anise, camomile, cassialine, and centory; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in the pot with water over the fire. Then place one end of a tube into the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the dead person, and hold it until the vapors enter the corpse. Then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and is not revived, then order the maidservant to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or musk lilac ointment, and then place it on the nature, and seek the secondine. And when she finds it, grasp it gently and extend it bit by bit straightly, so that the corpse does not fall during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pulled out. Then it will come forth and be released.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	Now if the mouth of the womb is too narrow, we have said the cure for sneezing, and fumigation with herbs. And if it does not improve from all that we have said, then make sure you do not touch; but what is at the mouth of the womb must be tied to the thigh of the woman, then perform a cleansing with tetraplmaction ointment. Then she will pass it and return it, and fire will come.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	"Therefore, it is necessary to perform fumigations with these [ingredients]: none of the ancients have proven fumigation with watercress and dried figs."
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The form of the instrument with which one fumes the woman to retain the fetus and the afterbirth is this:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like this in appearance: place the subtle head upon its nature, and widen the openings over the fire. Perform fumigation on hot coals, until the pitch is exhausted, then begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born with the anus not pierced, but sealed by a subtle membrane: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane at its tip, and not to touch it with a sharp instrument, guarding herself so that she does not touch it; then place moistened linen in wine and oil, then apply ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	"And if you doubt that it may close up again, then put a tube of lead into the hole and leave it there for several days, and remove it when the child is ready to go to bed."
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	"And sometimes this stoppage comes from a sudden wound or an abscess; therefore one must cut off that sudden growth: if it is cured, then treat it as we have said for the lead tube."
de la fistule dou fondement	of a fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come underneath the fundament are nodations, and growths that come beside the fundament deface, or in the space of both parts, so there is one fistula or several; and when this nodation is ancient, it aches, and produces moist white blainche or subtle bowels, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and they are known by those who see them in evacuation or windiness when the patient evacuates, and sometimes one sees some vers.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	"And there are fistulas that pierce up to the bladder and up to half of the penis; and they reach up to the hip joint and up to the knee."
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes the persistent fistula at the fundament, and not transient; and it is that you place your two index fingers on the fundament, and insert a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, then insert a subtle thread of silk or horsehair until you feel the thread with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there comes out no evacuation nor windiness nor worm as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	"And when the fistula is persistent up to the bladder or up to the urinary canal, urine comes out and it cannot be cured by medications."
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If the boil reaches the hip joint, then the inflammation extends to that location. If there's no twisting and the pain radiates around, it will soon burst open, and no medicine nor plaster applied suddenly would help; in such Persians fistulas there is no cure except labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who involve themselves with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not Persian and is not ancient, there is hope for healing through iron, as I have proven. Thus, the patient lies face down between your hands; they lift their legs up to their thighs and incline their thighs toward their belly. Then insert a tent of brass, or lead if there's twisting, until you know where the inflammation comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around their anus, then you must insert your two index fingers into it. If you sense that it has pierced through, and if between your thumb you feel either the skin or flesh, know that it is Persian. Therefore, do not intervene if it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Some say that one can heal certain conditions well, but this occurs rarely. And the aid given there consists in heating the cautery according to the width of the fistula as it is said before; then insert it hot into the fistula until it reaches near the fundament; and do this twice or thrice until you know that those broken tissues are burnt, resembling a bird's feather; afterwards cure with soft lint moistened in butter until that tissue comes off, then apply ointment gently between skin and flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed thus, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise, and if the tent enters but does not pierce all the way to the fundament which is behind it, and there is a thick covering of flesh or skin between your two fingers and the tent, and you see the fistula through this covering of the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula and thrust the tent forward immediately, then apply the cautery afterwards until it reaches the head of the tent; thus the tent will be released and will fall out; then cleanse those broken tissues resembling a bird's feather, leaving none remaining.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	"And if the pus comes between you and your work, then cauterize it with fire or an acrid medication."
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Because the fire cautery combines two things: namely, burning of adjacent skin and cauterization of blood and moisture; then treat wet wounds with burdock or crushed herbs until the place turns red, and let the burned skin rise in the wound; then dress the wound with dry compresses pressing hard on the hard skin.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	"For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return."
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	"And if a fistula comes out deeply from the anus and is far from the body, put your two fingers into the anus and inquire after it."
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between two there is the cloth or the sinus or skin where it is about to pierce, then apply fire cautery as we have said, or cut until the bottom, or if you can't, put tents and dress as before; but do not cut too deep that you cut the tissue holding the fundament, and let evacuations come without intention. Then dress it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or remove that cover and clean it after cutting near the fundament with a tent or other pointed instrument. Then cleanse the broken skin in the wound as much as possible. Then work to restore the wound and keep the fistula away from the fundament: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: when you insert the needle into the fistula and it is located on the side of the fundament near the skin above, then take a pierced needle at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	"And wrap one thread twice around it, and push the needle entirely into the fistula until it reaches the end."
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it passes into the margin of the fundament inside, then draw out the thread from that hole, so that you press your thumb on the fundament; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and tie them to each other tightly, leaving it for one or two days; and tighten occasionally until the threads cut through those tissues that are between them and drop off; then heal the wound until it is closed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	"But if the fistula does not open up on its own, then make an incision in any way that you are able to, if it is not too deeply embedded."
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"For one should not attempt to cut something that is too deeply embedded and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed."
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spinal needle used to open a fistula is sharp and pointed at one end, but not at the other, so that it does not cut where it should not, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	"hemorrhoids"
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often ooze blood; some have one, others have several. Those that are outside have a lot of moisture, and sometimes contain a little yellow water or blood, having the color of flesh. The cure for those who have hemorrhoids inside the fundament is to command the patient to strain while walking around in rooms until the fundament lets them out, and then grasp them with forceps or hold them with your thumbnail, then cut them at their base; if the nails cannot hold them due to moisture, take them with a piece of cloth, cotton, or wool, and pull them out with both hands, then cut them and sprinkle warm powders on them that can act as cautery; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, and heal them with other cures until they are healthy. If the fundament cannot expel them, cleanse the patient with a biting and sharp purgative to wash what is inside the fundament so that they can come out openly. When the patient strains and if the hemorrhoids have come out of the fundament, then the cure is easy; it is to grasp them with your thumbnail or forceps and cut them, then heal them as we have said until they are healthy, and avoid incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must prepare the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle, then draw the thread upwards and have the needle pierce through from the other side; then turn both ends of the thread under the needle and make it loose; tie the thread tightly and remove the needle, do likewise for all others, but leave one to drain excess blood. Then place a moistened cloth dipped in rose oil or cerate on the wound, apply it, and instruct the patient to rest. Leave it until it falls off, then treat it with ointment and other remedies until it heals.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	"Regarding the drying of fistulas in the fundament:"
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	"Many times there is drying out of fistulas in the intestines, either due to natural constriction or when the illness is old and medicinal treatments are ineffective;"
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must scrape off the scab above using a sharp point or your nail so that it does not become moist again. Then heal it as necessary until it is sound; if it cannot be healed, resume scraping more vigorously than before until it heals completely and the scab is removed.
dou fremit	"Regarding tremors:"
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small erroneous appearance before the body, and they go very deep; sometimes you feel them cold, and it feels like death from trembling, and it comes into the whole body, but more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	The cure is to take a rod made of an ostrich feather or a strong eagle feather, and place that rod on the trembling, so that its circle envelops the trembling entirely; then turn your hand around the entire rod until you grasp all around the trembling, and press it deep down, grasping the trembling by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	"And if you see fit to do so, use a feather made of brass or iron in this same manner, making sure it is thin underneath and pointed above;"
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	"Do not pierce too deeply to avoid causing pain and injury; if you wish, cauterize the tremor as is described earlier in the chapter on cautery."
de la forme dou clistere	"Regarding the form of an enema:"
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	"Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or molten bronze or moistened iron; and sometimes these instruments are small or large according to their intended purpose;"
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	"Therefore, those that should be used for treating children and the weak and infirm are small;"
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	"The shape of a small or large enema is as follows, depending on how full the belly is:"
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a disturbance or the belly is tied up, as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and there are two holes on one side and one hole on the other side; and the belly is where you put the medicines in an animal bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there is one stitch of hemp between each hole, then insert a strong thread made from twisted flax into these holes in the shape of an X or wound around, and gather the belly like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it with a strong string beforehand using an instrument, then perform a clyster; this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	**And let the medicament be neither too hot nor too cold**, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister squeezes with both hands until it is completely empty, then remove the clyster, and the patient raises their legs to facilitate discharge; and if the medicament wishes to come out, let it flow as much as possible; and if it remains overnight, it is of greater benefit.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if you perform a clyster for an illness of diarrhea of the bowels, and the doctor rushes to remove it, then reapply it until it is clean."
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	**And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament, or an abscess**, then let the clyster be as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of the thin clyster on which the skin should be stretched:
des plaies	"of wounds"
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	"We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about treatments for hands and medicines according to their completion."
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	"I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made from, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made."
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	**The things by which wounds are made are through stones thrown**, and cuts from sword or knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the locations on the body, such as a wound falling on the neck, head, back, belly, liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, for their remedy will come later in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is due to a blow from stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt the formation of a hot abscess: soak it immediately with cold water from the cephalic vein itself if there is little blood flowing from the wound, and let the soaking be on the opposite side of the injured part; and make the patient abstain from wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to soak it, then let his diet be reduced, and let him not drink wine nor eat meat; and place on the wound, if a hot abscess appears, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in sternutatory wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then apply powder which I will mention later to the wound while it is still fresh with all its blood, and protect it from the air; and if the ars has moved it, then apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	"And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut or similar ones, and its lips cannot come together by themselves, then bring them together by stitching, as I will tell you about stomach wounds regarding stitching."
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and deep, barely attached on one side, cut it off. Then treat the wound with medication and replace tough skin in place of leather, instructing the patient to eat large quantities of meat, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also poultry and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rottenness in the skin and it is not near the bone, cut off all the rotting flesh, then cauterize. And if there is an artery or vein exposed in the wound that cannot be stopped with medicine alone, tie the artery. If this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	"And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy: you should put in this powder which seals before air moves it."
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method of the powder is as follows: Take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live chalk three parts. Grind them finely and fill the wound, pressing firmly so that it adheres well and joins with all its blood. Then bind it tightly, leaving it unbound if it swells; for do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	"And sometimes this [treatment] is done with quicklime alone when one does not have incense nor dragon's blood, provided that air has not moved the wound."
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved the flesh, especially in summer, do not apply this powder; but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made from barley flour and water and honey, until it softens. Then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine tweezers. And I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	"About wounds to the neck:"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes on the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and one on the head, except that if the nerves of the neck or an artery are cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.
