If it's the nerves, there is no other remedy but to let nature take its course and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retreat. And do not apply anything cold to the wound, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest organ. But let the medicine be warm, such as hot water washed in soft water, mixed with rose oil, and cooked water also washed in soft water, and other mineral stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the wound is large, then stitch it up and bind it with bandages, and treat it until it is healed."
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and swollen full of pus, pierce it lower down; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, drain it, tie it, cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the heart, and the windpipe is guarded through which food passes, then cover the heart over the tube of the neck, and do not touch the neck but place it according to its natural shape; then bind it tightly, leave it for some days, then cure it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has impressed upon the bone, remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, burn them all if you can, those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound rots, and drain it and ligate the opening; and if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	"And if there are bones and fistulas in the wound, then treat it as I said in its chapter."
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	"About wounds from lances or knives:"
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If the wound is from a lance or knife and it's deep, look to see if any wind escapes from the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal. If it isn't deep but all its blood is fresh, don't apply powder at first nor tie it off so blood doesn't flow into it deeply, reaching the heart and killing the patient; instead, apply attractive ointment and bind it twice a day. And if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient lie on their back for three days or four or more. Then there will be no spasm, nor harmful trembling of the heart, nor straining of breath; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Therefore treat it with plasters and other remedies until it is healed. And if it cannot heal and opens up again, know that there is a fistula there; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it's simple, whether on the front or back, then treat it with what's before; if it's large, suture it; and if it's small, use powder. If it's pressed against the bone and has fragmented pieces, probe the wound, and cauterize any exposed vessels if they're severed; but if they're not severed, let the wound fester so that removal will be easier; and judge other wounds on other limbs as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"On rupture of the abdomen:"
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And the rupture of the abdomen can be large or medium or small. From a large wound, sometimes the intestines or their nerve may protrude, making insertion difficult and suturing more painful. Sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because it's harder to put the intestines back in without sewing them piece by piece. Also know that intestinal rupture occurs in four ways: two common sutures happen in abdominal closure, and two other sutures are common for other body wounds. Still, they are more specific with abdominal closure, which I will detail.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and some part of the intestines has been injured, and it is difficult to reset, this is done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen with cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or one cloth in boiling water only, or cook in hot water with cinnamon and cumin, and raise the intestines until the swelling has been removed; and sometimes use this restraining wine, and be careful to avoid harming the soul while disentering.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestines with water in which aloe and mallows have been cooked, for by this the entrance is cleared a little; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure should be such that no one cuts there without great necessity; and this is the instrument for breaking: cut into it in the curve and do not go further; see here its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines stick out, then carefully place them back according to their natural form in their proper place if you have the power, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is below the belly, then make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is above the belly, put the head and breast higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the rupture of the belly is in one of these two parts, put attention to ensuring that the wounded part is higher than the other.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	If the wounds are small, use what you have available, then take one of your ministers and gently pull out all the ruptured parts with his hand, and join the lips together; and this is the common manner of sewing, and it is that you take one or more needles according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave two spaces at the head of the wound and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce both heads of the skin with both heads of the sinew which is beneath the skin inside, until you have pierced it on that part, and join together all four heads of the sinew; then tie them with a double thread around the needle on both sides, then join together both heads of the wound neatly, and then leave two spaces and insert another needle; then bind the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease doing this according to what you need of needles until all the wound is closed; and let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and coarse, for fine needles cut through all the flesh, and those too coarse cannot enter well: therefore they must be medium-sized; and do not put the needles too deeply into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before it is sewn up; and then cut off the heads of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put tents or bandages on the heads of the needles for useful keeping, and leave them until the wound is healed. And this manner of sewing with needles is more useful in small wounds, for it suffices with one or two needles. The second manner of sewing is common, and it is that you join together both heads of the skin and both heads of the sinew together with one needle where there is a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these heads all four together, then sew back the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that cloth is sewn; and put between each stitch the thickness of a middle finger.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I reset the intestines for him after he had been ill for 24 hours, and the wound was closed until the 15th day, and I dressed it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not dress it with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put on the wound old cotton twice daily, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways to stitch: Take the needle and insert it from the outer part towards the inner one; when it has pierced through the heart straight on, then lay the head of the needle or the thread where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce through from the inner part towards the outer one. And the purpose of this stitching is to sew like a furrier sews furs, leaving the needle once on one side and picking it up again on the other side until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, which Galen describes properly, is done thus by some: they bring the two parts together naturally and apply one end of the catgut to the other in this way: insert a needle near the middle of one part and pierce only that spot, leaving both ends of the catgut; then turn the needle and have it pierced from the outer side until it enters on the inner side at the two ends of the catgut; then pierce both through the outer side until they enter on the inner side into two other needles which are placed on the opposite side; and this is the moist manner of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen thus says this word, and some confirm it: one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one needle must be inserted on one side, and the other on another, in the manner of those who sew hides. Know that when the rupture is inside the belly, the sewing is more difficult than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is thus: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the flesh has moved, so put back the intestines and the skin; then place powder made from the flesh nearby, and if the flesh has moved, place some ointment that is present until the wound closes; and stitch the edges together, and let the sinews and muscles be sewn up; then treat the wound like others until it heals. And if you do not have medicines, as soon as it begins to close, put old cotton on it and move it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But in many cases when the wounds are simple, you have no need of other medicine. And if you doubt that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then it is necessary that you moisten light linen in warm oil of roses or rose oil, and place it around the angles and under the armpits. And if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which happens often, rinse them with warm red wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines called "jejunum" cannot heal when injured due to the thinness of their walls and the delicacy of the entire body's structure, and their similarity in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back in immediately like the intestines while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, then tie off the part that is black so blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ties, and hang the two heads down from below the wound until the spleen falls out to facilitate extraction, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the bowel's rupture
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people because I saw one man pierced in the abdomen by a lance; the wound was to the right of the stomach, became infected and formed a fistula, from which waste and wind escaped; I treated it as best I could, not ceasing until he was healed, and the place was solid.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him being soldered, I doubted that the patient might have illness in his belly; and there was no harm, but remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; And some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied in this manner: take frogs with large heads, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the frog has opened its mouth, so place it on the two lips, so that it draws its mouth over; And then cut off its head, and this remains so that it cannot untie itself, then put another frog afterwards in this manner that before, until the wound is entirely closed; And sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And these heads harden in the intestines, and cause no harm to the patient, and one can tie the intestines with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that is very lean, and then tie at the head of this thread a thin twisted linen thread, then put the thread through the needle, and sew up the intestine, and reset it in the opening; And this manner of tying with frogthread is not foreign but according to the way of faith and hope; And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no art or health except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	"of fistula wherever it may be"
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes open, is universally called "fistula," and similarly when it is channeled and goes back in.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is truly a nodule that is hard and white, where no pain is felt, and it is also channeled like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it flows clear and then becomes thick; sometimes thin, and sometimes sufficient. I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that does not heal, and there is no flesh, is only so because of one of the eight causes: namely, due to the smallness of blood or flesh; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow flesh to form; or because there is too much bile; or the place is blocked up and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because corruption is a type of pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow in digestion, and health is delayed by nature and inflamed. And I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the remedies with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	"Now I must tell you about the treatment for fistula that is performed by handiwork."
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the face, or from the intestines, or from the bladder, or from some of the ribs, or from the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet; and also those that come to the main property of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are difficult to heal, and there is only work, and ignorance involved; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a tent of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, use it to search for it; and if the fistula is crooked, search for it with a subtle tent of lead, for lead bends much around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with tents, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture goes from one opening to another and cleanses it; then search for it with bleeding according to what I have said, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and how deep it is, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel at the pressure of your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the fracture and the corrupt flesh that is inside; and then heal it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, then you must cut very deep, as far as you can, then put moist tents in hot medicine water, and put them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If you don't feel any pain in the vein or nerve of the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, then cleanse until all the decay has been removed, then treat the surrounding flesh until it's clean; and if it isn't clean, and returns to its former state, know that you haven't gone deep enough: uncover further and search until you reach the bottom, remove all the decay, then restore it to its proper place; and if done so, it's well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep to reach; if there's no other option but to leave it to nature. But if there are small rotten bones and you can grasp them with forceps, extract them using appropriate tools. If many bones are affected, remove all of them without leaving any behind. And if moisture hinders you, yet there's no error or fear, cut away the moisture, flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place on the wound something irritating rottenness, and leave it until the place is rotted around the bones, and then they will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then wait only until all the blackness is gone from it, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of corruption and it comes up to the flesh of the bone; it must be cut away entirely up to the corruption, and then treated until it is sound; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to one man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was once a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to an inner cause such that matter came into the leg and there was a large abscess which did not have any apparent cause for opening. But foolish physicians operated so much on the abscess that it opened, and they corrupted many materials, and it became a fistula, and there were many holes that all excreted bile and moisture from the body; and many physicians treated him around two years, but none had any skill in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed through the holes in great quantity. And the skin of the young man became red, and had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, then searched all the holes, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried, and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and corruption had spread to the bone within; I scraped away what appeared of the rotten bone, and thought there was no other corruption but that which I removed; and began to treat the wound with dry medicines for a long time, but could not heal it; then started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and scraped it away, then removed it, and concentrated on healing the spot; but I could not do so until I cut around about a palm's width of the bone, and drew it out entirely, then filled it with medicines; and it was quickly healed and sewn up, but no longer needed to recommence the work except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure it, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and was of good constitution, causing neither harm nor discomfort at all, neither in breathing nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a linen cloth and tie it at the head of the exposed bone, and tell someone to hold it up high; then take another thicker linen cloth than the first one, and bind it over the flesh that is above the bone, pulling the rotted flesh downwards and uncovering the flesh on the spot where you wish to see, so that the bone does not wound the flesh; then place a hot iron or a red-hot coal under the bone to move the rotten flesh away; this should be done as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and also again afterwards.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, uncover all the flesh. Then place a branding iron underneath, and then use tweezers to draw the corruption from one side to the other, with the tweezer being as long as the corruption is wide, as we have said. And if the corruption is at the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and use tweezers on the bone it contains from the other side. And if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, there is no other remedy than cutting. And if the corruption is at the wrist of the hand or the wrist of the foot, that is very serious indeed, but nonetheless you must investigate this corruption and how it opens. And cleanse it in every way you can, but without causing harm to veins or nerves. Know also that there are many kinds of knives and tweezers for cutting these bones, according to their size, appearance, thickness, fineness, length, shortness, and hardness; and therefore one must prepare the appropriate tool for each type of operation. And know also that the work will show you which tool you need, according to your knowledge in this art and the evidence of the disease's symptoms.
dou feu	"fire"
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	**The head rots either from within or from without; and when you have treated that decay with medications but they do not help, then you must cover that limb up to the point where the decay begins, so that the patient escapes from death by this means, or from the greater evil of loss of limb. And the sign is that the limb becomes black as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, then that decay spreads limb by limb, and seizes upon the whole body; so act quickly and cover it, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous creatures, such as sea scorpions or vipers and similar ones, then cover the head of the two fingers but do not let any spices come up to the hand.**
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	**And if it comes up to the hand, then cover it at the joint so that the decay does not reach the arm; and if it is in the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, then it is death, and no external remedies can help unless there is a great quantity of its virtue. And do the same when decay comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cover it after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, cover the whole foot; and if it moves up into the leg, cover it at the knee joint. And if it goes above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to let the patient die. And the manner of covering or wrapping the limb is thus: you tie it above and below, and stretch out some ministers on one side of the ties downwards, and others on the other side upwards, and you cut away the flesh that is between the two ties with a wide spatula until the bone is uncovered; then cover it with wool, and put a cloth of linen on each side so that the wool does not touch the healthy place and cause the patient another lesion or abscess.**
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while working, cauterize the spot immediately using some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it's complete, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage and care for it until it heals. And I'll tell you what happened to a certain man: He had a blackening that seemed like burns from fire, starting on his big toe, spreading throughout his foot; when the man saw this corruption, he quickly cut off his foot and was healed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never does an abscess form in the flesh so deep that it collects a great mass of pus; then it becomes round and pierces through, the pus bursts out, leaving the area empty like a vessel; and the skin above is as delicate as a thin veil, not reaching down to the bone or nerve, such illness is called 'sain' and not 'fistula'; but if it stretches so long that it reaches the bone deep inside, then it is called 'fistula'. And the skin is such that you must cut around this skin entirely, even if it is delicate like a thin veil; and it should not be damaged due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin is damaged and corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it thus: observe whether the breast is large and the pus emitted has a foul odor. Then perform a clyster as follows using Egyptian medicine made like this: take aloe, oil, and litharge in equal amounts, cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine becomes red and thick like honey; then take some of this according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and administer it via the breast, closing the opening. Leave the medicine there for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; repeat this many times until the breast is cleansed and freed from foulness. Sometimes use a clyster of ash water when Egyptian medicine is not available. Take vine ashes, add water to them, let them soak, and administer them via the breast until you are sure that the breast is well cleaned. If the patient cannot tolerate it, or neither Egyptian medicine nor ash water helps, then perform a clyster with water and honey mixed with a little powdered litharge, or use a mixture of honey and wine which has properties to cleanse and wash, making the wound scar harder. Once this is done and you are confident that the breast is well cleansed, perform a clyster with medicine that produces flesh. Take diachylon plaster and cook it with rose oil and wine. If the opening of the breast is small and the clyster tube cannot enter, then widen it slightly using an iron tool and insert a wick of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened. If the wound is too large, then stitch it up leaving only one spot where the clyster can be inserted; if the opening that emits pus is above, then cut lower down where it is located.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bowel is deep, let no flesh grow into it; and if you cannot cover the wound from below as you see fit, prepare it in such a way that the bowel moves to its lowest point. For when the bowel is deep, let no flesh grow into it, and if you cannot cover the wound from below as you see fit, prepare it in this manner: let the bowel move easily downward, leaving nothing of it; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and stretch them over the linen cloth that covers all the wound. Then cut forcefully around the opening of the wound a little wider than the first one. Then gently apply ointment onto another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it on the wound to support the bowel, without removing the large outer cloth afterwards; but often remove the one on the wound to remove the bowel, and know what comes out of the bowel - whether it's poisonous liquid or a little or enough, or digested or undigested. And beware if the patient feels pain or numbness, and if there is an abscess or not. When your medicine has been applied in this manner and you see how it acts on the opening of the wound, know that the breast is already healthy, and the wound is approaching healing; then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes bow-shaped after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons have long lingered, do not despair of health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds take a long time to heal, and others who recover quickly; if undigested food jumps from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach has not emptied itself; and if the stomach takes a long time to empty and is far away, apply dry medicines of moist substance and dry virtue, such as diachylon ointment, for it contains much vitriol, which is the last medicine; take diachylon ointment and make it with rose oil and equal parts old wine; then cook and use it; and this same thing is done better when cooked with honey, if diachylon ointment is not present, or you can take mirrh, aloe, and frankincense, grind them, and mix the powder with the honey while it's on the fire; then spread it on a cloth and place it on the stomach, sometimes administering long pepper and celestine root, which is also called violet flour and centory; use simples or compounds: grind them, make them into powder, mix them with the aforementioned honey, and use it; if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this cure, know that the corruption has gone deep and affected the bone, hard members, or ligaments; then proceed with the cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	To treat a boil on the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritis is an abscess that arises under the nail of the little finger of the hand or foot, or sometimes appears on other toes; and when it becomes elderly and no care is taken for it, then comes the thick abscess, running and breaking out so much that it runs to the root of the nail, and sometimes runs over the whole thing; and the corrosion comes down to the bone, until there comes a foul pain, and the head of the toe becomes large, and the color becomes dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we have said in the division and the treatment does not help at all, then you must cut away with iron the entire excess that remains of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy. But if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to prick, and starts to fester, then you must place a hot iron under the nail where it pricks the flesh, lift it up, cut away that subtle and tender flesh carefully and gently, and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out, and remove the rotten part, for as long as the rotted bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see both are corrupted, cut one in front as was previously mentioned, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is inflamed and painful, you must first ease it; then cut the nail of the spina bifida diagonally from above, and ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel great pain. And if this happens, place something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain in the wrist
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Of the two joints that sometimes appear in some men by chance, one may be entirely fleshy, and another may have bones, and there may be a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, where their birth is between certain toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with any knot on the neck does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the neck sometimes moves; the measurement of one who is plump is light, cut it off from its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: you must take care of this.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one born with a knot on the back of the neck, first cut around the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	A dislocation that occurs at both knees simultaneously comes from birth, or from a wound, or from burning by fire, or from similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary to cut that adhesion so that the neck returns to its natural shape, then place between two wet compresses or cloths soaked in rose oil to prevent them from sticking together; or place between two thin pieces of lead until the joint is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a dislocation occurs at one of his knees with the palm of the hand, cut this dislocated joint in the manner that is appropriate.
des vils	Of the lowly
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large winding tubes filled with melancholic superfluities that come from various parts of the body, and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purge of bile, and then heal it with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cautery of fire is done in two ways: one is to cut them and draw off the black blood; and the other way is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first heat the leg with hot water very strongly until the large blood is subtilized. Then hold the leg of the patient from above the hip down to below the knee joint; then cut the vein in one place or two or three, with a wide cut. Then squeeze and draw out black blood by hand from one end to the other, as much as the virtue of the patient can suffer. Then tie it up, and tell him to bathe his wounds with cold water for several days afterwards. Repeat evacuation and cleaning when veins are full, which harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the veins is done in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, especially if there is a lot of hair. Then put it in warm water or heat it by the fire until the veins swell up and become red. Cut into the vein on the long side of the knee joint or below the ankle joint. Then open the skin with an awl and scrape off the vein from each side until it is visible when touched. You will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord. Then put the hook underneath, raising the vein from the skin. Then sew it to another awl gently. Cut again three fingers above the first cut. Then scrape off the skin over the vein until it is visible. Then raise it with the hook as before and sew it to another awl. Then make another cut if necessary, then lift it up and cut at the end of the foot. Then draw it out and remove it cut by cut until it is all out. If you cannot draw it out, take a strong double-thread needle and thread it through and tie it off. Then put it underneath the hook and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out. Make sure it doesn't break, as if it breaks you won't be able to draw it out or remove it, causing harm to the patient. When you have finished, place damp wool soaked in vinegar and rose oil on the wound and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the sinew is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cut it through; and pull it as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron tool used to cut the sinew is curved, and it does not cut through, so that it does not cut into the vein; and it should be thickly curved, for if it were thin, it would cut into the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is inserted into the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on dry land without moisture; but sometimes it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to rot that comes underneath the skin, like the serpent entering and winding between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a very great inflammation comes into the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to protrude forth, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head opens, you must wrap around it a piece of cloth from two and a half to two spans long, and knot it, letting the cloth hang down on the leg. And every time it leaks at the front, wrap the cloth around it again and knot it. If it is too long, cut off part of it, wrap the remainder, but do not cut it off at its root, for if you do so, it will retreat into the flesh and cause an abscess and corruption in that place, resulting in bad illness. Therefore, it must be treated bit by bit up to the head, leaving nothing on the body; sometimes this vein is when it has been treated five or ten palms long, and once a man came to me whose was ten palms long. When you cut it, put one ray into the hole and pierce it all the way through so that everything comes out. Empty the matter that is inside, and bring healing medicines to apply there against corruption for some days, then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Sometimes this vein is more humid, especially when it opens at the ankle joint or foot, where there are many pores and blood flows out abundantly; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land 'cattle sickness,' because it often occurs in oxen. It is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, traveling throughout the body both ascending and descending, causing pain as it moves from limb to limb. When it rubs against the skin, it causes sores. It arises from putrefaction of certain humors, like those that cause worms, serpents, and other parasites in the belly. Its malice is doubted because when it travels through the body, it can reach the head and enter the eye, causing it to become inflamed and destroyed.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drawn out, one cannot be sure that it is all out until it moves: therefore, tie the area above and below with a strong, tight bandage. Then make an incision and draw it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and not found, cauterize with fire until it dies. The greatest harm it causes is running through the eye, as we have said; but if you see it coming near the head towards the eye, press down hard on the eyebrow below it, then make an incision and draw it out. The patient should use bodily purifications and solvents for bad humors, avoiding foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From pain caused by windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "wakirir," and it is a pain that comes into certain limbs, and moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it move just like a worm to the shoulder, more quickly than anything, like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot, and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a little while later it spread throughout her body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it would often turn around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I marveled greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner before."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had heard many times that pain could move from one place to another, but I had never seen it as clearly as in this woman's case; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body and uncovered veins, which made this windiness more apparent; and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are dislocated, who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to heal this illness, and the patient feels that pain which we have spoken of, then lay it on quickly above and below, and then cut until that constrained wind escapes from its place; cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat those that relieve winds, like fetid pills and pills of serpentine, and similar others.
des saiettes	And arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"Sweats are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body where they flow."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are some with large points and small ones, and barbed and welded; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with splinters; and those which fall into any limb fall in two ways: either into the principal member, like brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidney, bladder, intestines, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore into any place of these members and the signs of death which I shall tell you below appear: then you should beware of extracting this arrow, for many die afterwards; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.
