And the sign of an arrowhead when it strikes and pierces the bone, and the eye socket above the brow jumps, is when there is darkness, swelling, redness, and inflammation in the eyes, and redness and swelling of the tongue, and spasm and disturbance of consciousness, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes there may be blood from the nostrils or ears; and sometimes it loses speech and voice; and from the wound flows white moisture like feathers, and also burning of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then take care of the cure, and remove the arrowhead if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	And the sign of an arrow striking the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and sometimes the arrow moves like a feather, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: then know without doubt that death has occurred.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"And the signs of sweat that affects the lung are: foam flows from the wound without pain, the throat swells, the patient changes color and sighs loudly while seeking cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	"And if sweat flows onto the covering of the lung, near the little ribs; there will be great pain and distress with sighing; and all the members of the shoulders move."
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if sweat flows onto the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will flow from the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if sweat flows onto the belly and much feces flows out through the intestines, there is no hope for recovery or removal of the sweat."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	"And if sweat flows into the bladder and urine flows out with fever, and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is deadly."
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"Other members such as the face and neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary muscles, spine of the back, buttocks, thighs and legs, and similar members are safe according to many different conditions."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When sweat is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me so that you can do likewise."
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened that an arrow fell into the ear of one man at the root of the nose: I tried it and pulled it out on the other side beneath the fat of the ear, and it was removed without damage.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye beneath the skin, and the arrow was reversed, so that only its tip could be reached facing the wood, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the eye remained healthy, and no ill happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabian arrow with ears; I cut the barbs and slowly pulled it out until I removed it, and the Christian remained healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled an arrow from a man who had fallen into his belly, and thought he would die; but after 30 days had passed, his condition did not change. I cut upon the arrow, engaged it, and pulled it out forcibly, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man on whom an arrow has fallen onto the back and the wound became solidified over it; and the arrow remained inside him and did not change its natural position nor caused harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another man on whom an arrow has fallen onto his face and the wound became solidified; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similarly.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow was pulled out from the man of the king's princes who had fallen into his nostril, which was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was entirely embedded when I was called for treatment three days after it had fallen.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt all around with a subtle probe and did not find it; but he felt pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was due to the tip of the arrow. I applied a plaster with atractive and digestive ointment so that the area would not swell; and then I saw where the arrowhead was.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed my hand on the wound for five days and reopened it again. The patient remained like this for a long time until he felt the arrowhead move one day within his flesh; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed corrosive medicine on the wound for many days until it opened. I tested it and felt the tip of the arrowhead moving in its place; then I applied more of this medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow was visibly exposed. Four months passed, and then the wound healed over so much that when I tried to remove the arrow with pliers, I could not pull it out. Therefore, I continued to experiment and devise various tools until I successfully removed it with well-made pliers, as described at the end of this chapter, after one day of effort.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored. I restored it nonetheless; the wound was healed, and the patient was completely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But I told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you can put your treatment on what I did not say, because books cannot encompass everything. However, wise masters compare even small things and find new works and instruments based on what is present or lacking in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows come out of the members they are stuck in according to two ways: either through the point where they entered or through another part. The one that exits through the point it entered is an arrow entering into flesh, and sometimes it exits without causing damage.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out immediately, let it be until the flesh around it is ripe and the opening is cleared. And similarly, if it is stuck in bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for a few days and move it each day. Then it will come out; if not, carefully incise all around it with a fine knife until the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bone of the head and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned become apparent to the patient: then do not pull it out, but let it remain there for a few days until it becomes level. For if the arrowhead reaches so far, death is near.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrowhead is stuck only in the bone and does not reach so far, and the patient remains for some days without bad accidents, then prepare to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the arrowhead is very deeply stuck and cannot come out; then apply caustics around it as I told you; then treat the spot until it heals."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it carefully. And if you feel it, then pull it out with some convenient instrument. And if you cannot do so because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead, and there are no bone, nerve, or vein involved, then cut until the wound is large enough. And pull out the arrowhead if you can, and if there are ears on it where it holds fast, then remove the flesh that is stuck in it by both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrowhead so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrowhead while pulling it, for then it would cause greater injury.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot draw it out at once, let it stay until the flesh around is corrupted; then draw it out, for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of the incision on the nerve and the vein, and find a way how you can move to pull out the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form that he was in when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow comes from another side, where some part of it is apparent, or if the skin is swollen at that spot so that one sees or feels it around: then cut there until tongs can grip it, and then pull it out. If it is stuck now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	"And if the arrowhead is held in bone, turn your hand around until it enters the bone and widen the hole; then draw it out."
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then resume the extraction until it comes out. And if the wood of the arrow is there, throw the whole wood away; and if the shaft has fallen and you see that pushing will help, then use a crowbar so that the point of the arrow enters into the notch of the tool; and then push it out, and if the arrow has been split, then push the tool with its pointed end inwards to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead is touched, then it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrowhead falls in the buttock or belly or bladder or side, and it is near, and you can cut on it, then cut there; but guard against cutting the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary; and treat until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used for extraction is like a bird's beak, and here it is depicted:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the stone.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the butt-end of the arrowhead is also like the feather of a bird, for pushing into the tip of the arrow, as here is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for inserting and extracting is shown here
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which blood is let for healing purposes, sixteen of which are on the head, namely: two temporal arteries behind the ears, called 'double herbes'; and two arteries that appear in both temples; and two veins in both eye sockets, called 'aspirers'; and one vein in the forehead; and one vein at the top of the nose; and two jugular veins in the neck; and two veins above the lips of the mouth, which are those veins called 'augulherich'.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used are two in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and laypeople call it "the vein of the head"; and the mean one is called "fast", and it consists of the cephalic and the basilica, and laypeople call it "the vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side, and laypeople call it "the vein of the belly", and it is over the fossa, and this is the one that is used, which opens clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the savatella is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is beneath the curvature of the pouch on the left side, and the second is the saphenous vein which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "the nose" that is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins that are behind the ears help with catarrh and migraine. The benefit of cupping, as I told you before, is that you should raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth. Then have the patient press their neck with their fist until two veins appear behind the ears in two places on the top of the head. Grasp them between your thumb and index finger, where you feel the pulse below your fingers, and squeeze gently. Then take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone. Next, raise your hand along the vein above until you cut through both layers of skin and vein completely, making two fingers' width, and let out as much blood as you see fit. Then press and bind it so that it is well drained; I have already spoken about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The benefits of cupping two arteries located on the temples include treating headaches, colds, and chronic eye conditions, as well as removing water from the eyes. Here is how to do it: Have the patient press their neck until both veins appear clearly; feel the pulse beneath your fingers and squeeze gently. Then lift your heart above the vein with your index finger and insert the lancet underneath, lifting the vein up and cutting it like you did with the other two veins. Let out blood according to what is necessary. Then release the patient and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, followed by cotton. Finally, bind it tightly and leave it until it is well drained. We have already spoken about their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting from the frontal vein is as beneficial for old facial diseases and headaches and redness; and its qualities are such that the patient strains their neck in twisting, until the veins appear; then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein and strike with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow according to the amount you desire; then loosen the patient's neck and bind the vein until it is sealed with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	"Nevertheless, the bandages should not be too tight, and tie them diagonally because the bone is close by, and sometimes the bandage breaks when it's thin."
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The benefit of the two veins that are in the temples is for the eyes and their diseases, redness, inflammation of the eyelids, and facial diseases; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient strains their neck by turning it, as before; then bleed them, and let the blood be drawn horizontally, a bit long, a bit wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	"And if the bandage is thin, it might break. Then wipe away the blood until you have enough, and then tie on cotton, tying it securely."
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting of the vein of the nose is beneficial for ague, and frenzy, and facial illnesses, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, especially when it is chronic; and the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient strains their neck, then presses their nose with your left hand, and takes a long, fine lancet, and inserts it into the lip on the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep in, and let the blood flow according to your need, then leave it overnight, for it is quickly restored; this is the form of the lancet
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bloodletting of the two veins helps with the narrowing of the anus, and the onset of measles, and many illnesses, and ringworm, and gangrene, and herpes, and esthiomenitis; and the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient strains their neck downwards on both sides, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the patient's head, and the patient sit on one seat, then make a wide cut in the long vein, then draw temperately some blood, or as much as necessary; then do the same on the other vein, then untie the bandage, and press both veins moderately so that the patient does not faint. Let it until morning, until the wound is healed
de la sainie des leivres	Concerning the care of the eyes.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	"The bandaging of the veins above the lips helps with colds in the mouth, gum corrosion, cracked lips, and around the nose."
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the method of eye care is to have the patient sit before you and hold their neck steady as I've said; then turn your hand, and look at the two veins, one on the right eyelid and one on the left, which are recognized by being black, and having small black veins around them: therefore cut both, and if you don't recognize them or are uncertain, then cut the larger of each side, and do likewise for the two veins above and below, as it's the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Concerning the treatment beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The treatment of the veins beneath the tongue aids after the treatment of the facial vein, and is used for narrowing of the throat, and diseases of the uvula, and diseases of the mouth; and the method of the treatise is that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, lifts their tongue, and looks beneath each side for a black vein: therefore cut both, but do not go too deep, as arteries lie beneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins of the head are commonly opened in two ways: either with a wide-bladed lancet or with an olive-shaped one like a cutting edge, and these are called "anesils"; they are wide and slender according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	"The shape of the mirror bandage is very well-known and is wide as you can see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	It is necessary for opening hairy veins full of thick, visible blood that contain thick and turbid blood; this is the shape of the olive blade.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"It's more pointed and thin, used for bandaging small veins with clear yellow blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps those suffering from ailments below the throat, neck, face, and belly. The cutter must cut deeply and beware of the artery beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and blood flows profusely, he must stop it as I said before; the blade should not be pricking but cutting like an 'anesil'.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilisk does not open manifestly, then you must remove it and replace it with another one; or if you want any vein from it, or if you want to sew in place of it the vein inside the arm: it opens manifestly; and heat the blade on anvil with annealing fire, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see that you can recognize the place of the vein, then before removing the arm, touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with fire-annealed blade; but be careful not to hit the artery when you see the place swell, for that is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see something like urine from a child coming out above, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: quickly then, put your finger on it steadily, then remove your finger when the bleeding stops, which often happens; then tie the arm, and leave it thus, and do not let the patient move it; and be careful, and do not let him move until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	"If the bleeding doesn't stop and you're alone without a doctor nearby, tie the artery if it's visible because its head retracts. Then compress the bleeding."
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig bark, and cut it open, then take one half and tie it securely until the next day; if bleeding stops, that's good. If not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop bleeding; these treatments are not harmful in many cases due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's bond.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bandage for the vein in midsection helps draw blood from above the head and below the body because it is composed of basil and celandine as we have said. The surgeon should be careful about the nerve beneath, and if he probes too deeply, he may inflame the nerve and injure it, which could prevent healing. This nerve often surfaces, but in some men it does not due to its thinness, so you must heal it with the instrument anesil; and avoid damaging the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed with the olive-shaped flame or the myrtle-shaped flame, for this is the safest of all veins, as there are neither nerves nor arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to search for the lightest location, and if one misses the mark the first time, they should try again; sometimes the location becomes swollen in some people when one misses the mark the first time, but this causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of cauterization depends on your skill.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is performed not only for the sake of maintaining health but also to prevent future illnesses; and bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins located on the head: namely, the cephalic, temporal, and basilica veins. Bloodletting should be done at the beginning of Lent before dinner, and in autumn and winter after meals when signs ofpletion appear. Bloodletting should take place on the first or third day, two to three hours after noon.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The ointment administered to the sick has no fixed time limit. Instead, it is used when needed throughout the day and at all times. It is not necessary to anoint children until they are fourteen years old, nor women who are pregnant for less than four months or more than seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old people who have passed the age of sixty should not be cauterized.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When someone wants to be anointed in any manner, they must first cleanse their intestines with a light enema if there is much retained feces. This ensures that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the intestines into the main limbs. Avoid anointing those who are too salty from eating meat, or who are drunk, regardless of how much they have consumed; also avoid those who are dropsical, and those recovering from a recent colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, menstruation, hard labor, sleeplessness, fasting, or anyone lacking vital force due to injury or illness. Then refine the humors with foods, drinks, and medicines if you can, as long as there is no impediment preventing it; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood. Anoint around the third vein of the chest, as we have described earlier in this text. That day, avoid hard work, excessive eating or drinking, sexual activity, and similar behaviors. Be cheerful and happy, with the anointing one standing taller than the one being anointed. Rub the arms twice or thrice, then gently press the ligature above the middle to ensure it is not too tight or loose, as this can hinder blood flow. Then moisten the cloth with a little old oil, place your left thumb on the vein below where you wish to anoint, ensuring the vein is neither too full nor empty before pressing firmly with the ferrule.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow like strings in the leg, and some such that are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein; and thus there are many; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be careful in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If the vein opens on the first attempt, that is good. If not, try again a little lower or higher, but avoid inflamed areas.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the wound is swollen and the patient fears it, let him rest for one or two days without tying the arm; perhaps pustules may come out; do not enter into a bath, then resume washing if it pleases him; and if the hole is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it does not flow enough blood as you see, then apply fire to that hole itself with all the flame directly; and work a little hastily before the wound swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not recommence the cautery, and put some oil ointment on it, for it lightens the body's blood, and in this place the oil's ointment is beneficial. And similarly administer oil ointment in every venesection that you perform on veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing is done with troacle and bowels of euphorbium when it is put on the place; thus it subtilizes the blood and scatters when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess appears there, which happens often, especially when the vein is not cut deep enough that time, then hasten and apply a sponge soaked in warm water and salt to the place, and keep it there for an hour. And you must do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains at the place afterwards for some days, do not worry about it; and if you see it, apply some mixture of aloes or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an boil appears during the bleeding of the basilica vein; then place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft under pressure from your hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not apply anything we have mentioned, for fear of causing an artery to burst; but instead make a dry plaster with one egg and harden the area, then cauterize it with another cautery until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And let each person bleed according to the strength of their constitution and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if it is thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the full and strong person who needs bloodletting to make a larger wound, and let the flame be wide; but for the weak one, do the opposite, and they should be pricked often with a thin needle, and this should be done by cutting across, not piercing; and this method of bleeding prevents loss of blood and damage to nerves, and is better than long or wide pricking.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body is weak from bleeding, give him softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is overheated, then bleed him three or four times; and if he has a cold constitution, let him eat before the bloodletting softened bread in mulled syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bloodletting, after losing much blood, then he should smell broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to vent his arm and bleed again later on, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed little by little according to his remaining strength continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to vent their arm after the first bleeding and has a strong body, should bleed again seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to wash themselves elsewhere should do so on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood inside the body that is already heated and causes fever; therefore, it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the wound opening until it weeps freely. Then, when you have washed all conditions of healing, place your hand on the swollen area as it heals, ensuring the patient does not move from the wound opening, which happens often if the healer is negligent; but it is not necessary to do this when you see that you need to untie the bandages and let blood flow again the second time. If the wound is curved, straighten the arm quickly, for this would be bad. Instead, leave it until it bleeds a second time. Or, you can touch with the tip of the flame so that the frozen blood at the wound opening may come out, then place a cloth soaked in cold water on it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, then leave it alone and do not squeeze it too tightly until the boil is healed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to draw blood a second time, then wash him in the same spot or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm can be washed instead of the vein in the head because it is composed similarly.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of healing is thus: the patient puts his hand in warm water until the blood vessels become red. Then it should be bound moderately so that the wound appears well, and now heal it across, not wide or long; make the opening large and heal close to the joint of the hand. If blood cannot come out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough. But if it is summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for this is done more often in winter than in summer. The healing of this vein is safer than all others, as there are no arteries or nerves present.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve for the healing of the right hand is beneficial for all ailments of the liver, and this is its method: constrain the hand, and place it in hot water until the vein becomes swollen, so that one can see it; and if the salve runs sideways, and if you cut it entirely along its length, nothing will harm; and do not go too deep with it, for nerves lie underneath all bare of flesh; then return the hand to hot water, so that blood does not freeze in the wound and cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as necessary, then place oil and linen on the vein to bind it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The washing of the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mice (gout), and do everything as I have told you concerning the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the Sophene is beneficial for all illnesses that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of flowers [flux], and illness of the loins, and of the old thighs and legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are such that the sick person places their foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it breaks, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and many loins go through there above the foot; therefore anoint there where the largest loin passes, or at the ankle, which is more beneficial.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you wash it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and cut across it as in cutting, and make the wound shallow.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if blood cannot flow out, then immerse the foot again in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the ligature fails the first time, then recommence the second above a bit, for the place is salted; do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and thus do likewise to the sinew of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and its washing is beneficial for pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the ligature's quality is such that the patient enters or leaves the bath, and stretches above the ankle four fingers in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then tie the ligature in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is better that you cut it, for the place is dry, and it is very prone to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then tie any vein of the leg that opens towards the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make the blood flow as much as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put cotton on and bind it tightly; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Regarding cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or earthenware, or glass. Cupping is performed in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping that is done without injury is of two kinds: either it is performed with fire or without fire. Cupping done by striking and bloodletting is performed in fourteen places on the body, one of which is at the top of the head; another in the neck; two others on both sides of the neck; one under the chin; two on the shoulders; one on each hip; two on the arms; two on the legs; and two on the ankles. Cupping does not involve drawing blood except from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken at all, unlike cupping done on veins. It should not be administered with or without fire in any case ofpletion where the entire body needs to be emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary to perform cupping due to illness or custom, we will administer it at the beginning or end of each month and also at every opportunity. For there are those who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head; others findpletion and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness before their eyes; some see blood drops in their mouth, have an swollen tongue, and spit blood; and still others dream of seeing bloody and wounded people, the dead, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the month, we order cupping to be performed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sneezing of the mouse aids the heat that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after evacuation of the entire body; this ventilation replaces the sneeze of the cephalic, and one who is cold-natured or has catarrh should not use it, for it does them great harm. Old men nor those with cold maladies on their head should also not use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who are often cured by it become accustomed to it, and therefore the cupping glass should be placed a little lower down out of fear of becoming accustomed."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Ventilation in the neck replaces sneezing from the head and basilica. It is beneficial for the narrowing of the breast, splitting the channel of the lung, coughs, and repletion. However, it should be done gently, as too much pressure can cause imbalance to the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Ventilation at the second ribs of the neck is good for headaches, ophthalmia, migraines, strangulation, and pain in the roots of teeth. It replaces sneezing from the basilica; you should instruct the patient to express their hand on putting it, so they do not block the artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	"Winds beneath the chin are beneficial for mouth diseases, gum decay, and similar ailments that affect the mouth; they are located at the level of the two lips."
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"Winds on the shoulders are beneficial for diseases caused by heat and excess."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventsation of the ribs is equivalent to that of three veins in the arm, as it attracts blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to go too deep with his iron, for the place is bare of flesh, and full of nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	"The cupping glass placed on the buttock is beneficial for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below. The cupping glass must be large and made of earthenware so that it may draw well; otherwise, if it were too delicate, it would break and cause great wounds."
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	"The cupping glasses on the legs draw clearly because they attract blood from the whole body and are beneficial for old back pains, sciatica, bladder pain, and they strengthen the joints. They are located at the level of the two sophenes and the two ankles. However, prolonged use can weaken the body and cause swelling in certain dispositions."
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	"The method of applying the cupping glass is to first place it empty and suc
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	"And if the blood is thick, one must strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood."
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	"And if the blood is very thick, one must strike a third time. And when we wish to draw only a little blood at a time, it suffices to strike once."
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish for much blood, let us recommence often; and if the blood is thick, go deep with your iron, until the point pierces suddenly; and it is fitting for those who have thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the ventsouses with aperitive and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucurbita seed oil; and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	"And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones."
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one whose skin is tender and has wide pores is being treated, no oil should be placed there, but it should be washed after the ventsation with rosewater, or cold water, or morel water, or cucurbita water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	"And those who have too much moisture, they should rise from this with oil of sage, or myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things."
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have abundant excesses should rise from old wine, or water of mustard, or decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar ones; and one should not bleed before the bath nor during it, but afterwards an hour or two; and one should not sleep after bleeding, and they must warm themselves when they are about to be bled and when they are being bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if one who has bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed; then they should take cold things such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce with garlic, and similar things; and eat figs, and castrated ram meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with cold complexion should take honey syrup, and medium fragrant wine which is between old and new, and eat peaches, figs, and small birds and chickens; and on the day they are to be bled, they should drink more than eat; and sometimes one must give treacle or muscat to certain men before or after bleeding, to strengthen the main limbs; but let the blood be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Ventouses placed without piercing are those applied to the liver, womb, foot, belly, mouth, back, and hip. These areas cannot withstand piercing, and such use is only for drawing blood from one member to another, as when we apply them to the breasts during milk fever. They remove viscosity from members by applying ventouses to the belly and mouth to reduce swelling. They alleviate pain where there is obstruction or stone by attracting it through their absorptive power, perhaps removing an obstruction or dislodging a stone from its place. Similarly, they are used when there is retained wind in the liver or womb. These ventouses are administered empty for suction alone; sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in cases of pleurisy. In this manner, one fills the ventouse with hot water or water in which appropriate herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	"The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:"
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let there be two of them with a width of half a palm's breadth and a depth of two palms, and on each side around the middle, there should be one small hole like for inserting a needle; let it be made of brass, softened beforehand so that it does not cut the patient when placed on the limb. And in the middle, there should be a transverse rod of brass or iron to hold an inserted candle, and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who use them; for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of old people, and those of the thin are different from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must place this cupping glass on the limb in such a way: insert the candle of wax or flax into it and place it across the rod that is inside the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass and does not burn the patient. Then place it on the limb, making sure that both holes are aligned as we have mentioned earlier, so that when desired, steam can escape through them, and remove the cupping glass; then take out the flax cloth as before and repeat this process often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping procedure used for treating pleurisy, which is acute, there is no tube or opening, and it is not filled with fire except when full of air, and it is placed only on the member; and that is its shape.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without fire are those cupping procedures used only in members where one cannot place cups due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, such as the two eyes and others like them. And the qualities of using these are that when you find leeches that are in clear, sweet water without any injury, then take them; and place them in a vessel of sweet water until they become famished and have nothing in their bellies. Then have the vein and cupping prepared, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the leeches on it. And when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where one can put a cup, then put it there, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the wound with egg yolk, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the wound bleeds too much afterwards onto the body of the wounded, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on until the bleeding stops; and if the blood is multiplied, then place powdered vitriol or gum, etc., until it stops; or you may put half a handful of peeled fava beans on the wound, and leave them there until they adhere to the wound, now it will stop; and if you need more, take others.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the blood vessels do not wish to clot, then rub the wound with fresh blood or insert a needle into it until some blood flows out, and then place them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are falling off, powder some alum and barley flour or ash onto them, now they will stick.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	"This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for fracture and dislocation."
