Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish physicians cast themselves aside from this chapter, having never seen any of the ancient books nor read a letter of them; and therefore the science in our land is estranged, for I found never any good one; and know nothing thereof, but by the science of the ancient books, wherein I have studied so much that I have treated the science therein, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have plainly described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have abridged it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are arranged.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book that those who seek understanding and remain faithful to the truth should study these pages and chapters so that those who are experienced may learn and teach this noble art to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when breaking or dislocation or torsion or contusion occurs in anyone, if any thing hinders you altogether, such as weakness of body, or child, or old man; or if the time is not very hot, nor too cold; and avoid cold things, namely cold drinks, and flesh of poultry and venison, and drink no wine, neither eat fat meats, nor fill yourself too full with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you are in doubt of a hot aposteme, nor of an expansion of matter to the limb. Let the patient return to his former government which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to unite, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with foods that promote growth and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, fish, and red wine, and similar things."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For by such nourishment the bones are strengthened and the fracture heals more quickly."
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the elderly and decrepit cannot be well reset or mended according to their nature due to stiffness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, like the bones of young children; but take care, align on the broken bone two large splints which join together and hold the limb in place until it heals properly; do not cut off any part of its work, and therefore it should be nourished with wholesome foods.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse and manifold in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For a fracture of the head is different from one of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the various types of fractures."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"For there are fractures that occur suddenly, like those caused by a fall or blow, such as cutting a feather in half with scissors."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And some fractures come with wounds while others have only a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own device and proper tool in the restoration, according to what the memory brings back into its place; and the breakage of the bone is known by the twist being there, clearly apparent by touch, and audible when pressed with the hand; but if there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient feels no great pain, then there is no breakage. But it can still have a twist, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb yourself but apply the medicines mentioned below and then gently immobilize it with bandages."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fractures which go into the air, and are in two parts dislocated, it is necessary to set them evenly at the point before an abscess comes; and if a hot abscess comes, let it be for some days until the abscess subsides; then set it even with the motion that you can do lightly and gently, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than those where there are pieces; then hold it as it is necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, then stretch them from two parts, if it is hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the limb are disjoined, you straighten them by all means and join them in their places with the motion that you can do, and guard that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and join well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"And feel with your hand whether it is well aligned or not: if it does not seem so, then straighten the limb gently without immobilizing it too tightly nor pressing on it as some do to cause inflammation and contracture of the limb, as we have said many times before."
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set, ensure that the patient does not move it at all, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning nor in any other manner; and make sure that the limb is securely fastened so that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For if they feel no pain, it is not set properly, and you must position them so that they feel no pain; and ensure that it is set correctly, so that there are no twists when it is restored; and the condition of the broken limb is as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that fractured limbs are diverse in size, length, and shape."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones: they must be wrapped with soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg: they must be wrapped with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the entire large limb and squeezes it evenly on all sides so that there is no gap; then tie it around with light pads, three or four turns depending on the limb, and press your hand a little on the whole bandage, then go up above the fracture and squeeze less so that the fracture can separate a little; and soften the bandage bit by bit until you grasp most of the healthy place, then take another bandage and wrap it around again on the broken place; then return to the part below the fracture and squeeze evenly, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first binding above; then put linen or cloth pads between the bandages so that they are all even, then tie everything together with a sling and then put well-made splints on it if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place upon it a warm, soothing ointment that draws out the swelling, and leave it like this for several days; then press with your hands or with something half as wide as a large cane reed, freshly cut, or with a piece of wood used to make wedges, or with a palm leaf rib, and shape them according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the bandage that you place on the fracture must be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as necessary for the limb's size or thickness. Then press on the bandages just as you did at the first wrapping, then tie above with a suitable thread, as in the first wrapping over the fracture; tie more tightly at first, then looser; and the threads must be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, like those used by foolish people who make their bindings from twisted flax cords, it is a great error because the binding cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each bandage.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the edges of the stitches after tightening in place, then put underneath them wads of linen or wool gauze so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that you should not tighten all the bandages on the broken limb immediately on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	When the limb is large, do not apply hot poultices until after 5 to 7 days, or more, depending on the heat of the emerging abscess; and here is the manner of the ancient emplastes for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and apply this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations and twists: take of gum arabic and myrrh and aloe and aloeswood, each .v. oz.; frankincense, also .v. oz; galangal, viij. oz; and grind them into powder, mixing it with albumen from an egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and swiftly restores broken bones, useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of poultice that is good for twists: take mugwort and wormwood, each nine drams; myrrh and aloes, each eight drams; aconite six drams; bolic armenic ten drams, grind well, mix with water or plenty of eggs, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of poultice for joints and bones out of their places, to alleviate pain and prevent the bone from being cut and broken: take new linen, soak it in warm water and cooked oil, and apply it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore anything, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and removes pain appropriately.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat broken bones: Take dried fig leaves and earth peony leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of using plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to soften the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of comfrey, camomile flowers, violet petals, wheat flour - each one part; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is hot, mix it with moistened coriander water or water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger plaster for when a hard abscess comes to heal the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of comfrey, linseed, balm, melilot, safflower, violet and camomile flowers - each one part; grind and mix with salt water, fresh water or wine, according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	"Hippocrates writes in his book that one should apply to the broken limb only cerate made from wax and oil, with nothing else added. He says it should be neither too soft nor too hard."
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	"And it seems Galen that one should apply to the broken limb for restoration dry things a little warm, like myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar substances, as we have said."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	"Another method for poultice that is good for wound and pain: take mullein leaves, chicken feathers or hairs of shaven men, mugwort and common sow thistle in equal parts, grind them, mix with the grease."
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove it a few days later, and make sure the patient does not feel any pain or movement of the bone from its place; if there is pain at that spot or itching without rest or swelling, hurry up and remove the plaster immediately. Use a light cloth and wet sea sponge, dip it in water and apply to the area until the itching stops and the pain is soothed. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen moistened with rose oil on it and secure it with a bandage until you are sure there is no heat from the abscess; then start again with gentle binding and a little plaster, not pulling too tightly as before; continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	"And if you see that the boil is hot and red and painful and swollen have all disappeared, and you need poultice and wrapping again, then resume it, just as you did at first."
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	**And if it comes to nothing in the limb of what we have said, so let it not be dislocated but after three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according as one sees, until the fracture appears, and the joining of the flesh approaches; then it holds more firmly than before, and the flesh grows thick, just as I have said earlier; and if you see the place drying out too much, know that nourishing cannot come to it; therefore apply hot water compresses, all the times that you dislocate it, and this should be every third day, and slacken the bandage a little; by this work thus the nourishing comes to the limb, and swiftly repairs what those foolish physicians do who reset the limb crookedly: this is wicked, and so are their works, and I see nothing else but letting [it] be and working rightly.**
des diverses manieres de brisure	"Regarding the various ways bones can break:"
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures there are, and diverse forms, and the causes are distinguished; for there are fractures caused by percussive blow from a sword, and the neck bone shatters all the way down to the hip bone beneath it, like wood or stone; thus this manner of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	"Or the sword cuts across the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called 'absolute'; both these fractures have large or small wounds."
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	"And if there is impact with embossed blows, or splitting or crushing from stones, or falls onto stones, or other similar causes."
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	"And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the periosteum under the bone or goes through it, this type of fracture has large or small wounds."
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And yet there is fracture that is wound in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, thus this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound made by striking with stone or falling or similar cause brings the piece of bone inward, and the place hollows like a cauldron when struck on it; so enters stone within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those who have moist bones in the head, like a child's head; and it occurs in all these manners of fracture that small pieces are displaced like stars; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	"And we recognize all kinds of fractures by their displacement, inspection, and the corrupted flesh that is on them."
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	"A capillary fracture is recognized because when the bone is uncovered and rubbed with a finger, the fracture appears black."
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	"In treating a fracture, beware of complications from illness. If you see no signs of bad accidents such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, spasms, fever, eyes protruding and turning red, or other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt."
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	"But if you don't see any frightening accidents and hope for a good outcome, then begin the treatment."
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	"And when an injured person first comes to you in wintertime, it is necessary to reset the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury."
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	"And if it is in summertime, hurry to reset the bone before the seventh day, so that the periosteum under the bone does not become corrupted and the accidents we mentioned do not occur."
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone breaks reach the skin that covers the brain, then you must cut open the broken part as follows: take the patient's head and uncover the bone in every way possible, gently over the wound's shape. If bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone or a hot abscess appears, aid with what is necessary; then fill the space with dressings moistened in rose oil; let the wound rest until the hot abscess is eased and ensure there's no more bleeding. Then begin to remove the bone around it, done in two ways of working: one way is to cut narrowly ahead.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he applies another cut, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is to have many cuts of varying sizes, some narrow and others wide, all pointed and made of fine iron. Work carefully so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	If the bone is hard and strong, it is necessary to drill around it before making cuts with chisels, taking care not to cut too deeply so that they pierce through the soft bone of the skull. Each chisel should have a guard or circle on top to prevent the point from penetrating too far into the bone. You should have several chisels so that each one fits properly in its place along the length of the bone, allowing you to have chisels for all types of skulls. These are the three ways to shape chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To drill around the fractured bone, place one chisel on the bone and twist it with your hands until you feel that the bone has been pierced. Then move the chisel to another location a little further away and continue drilling all around the bone. Next, use incising chisels to remove the strip of bone between the holes, working as carefully and gently as possible so that you can easily grasp the bone with your hands or with tools such as tongs or forceps. Be sure not to touch the cerebellum or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, then reset the sharp edge left by the bone with another tool resembling an awl, but it must be thinner and more delicate than other awls. If any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with tweezers; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	The other method is that of Galen, which is quicker and involves using strong pressure, as he himself stated.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone where the break appears moved so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place underneath the head of this lenticular incision tool, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side alone, for the parts are hot on both sides, such that the blade is towards the bone; then strike with a little hammer above, so that you gently tap the bone all around, and take great care of the skin that is underneath; if it adheres to the bone, remove it lightly, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not reach to the tissue, and the bone is only cut on top with small pieces, then cover that unevenness and remove the bone flakes with a fine razor file of which you should have several quantities to adapt best to each location according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Then use coarse rasps first, and afterwards finer ones, until it is smooth enough.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each of the other types of capillary cuts and subtle breaks, you must adapt your approach according to its direction; this is not something that can be learned by someone who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is exposed, then you must take one linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it upon the wound; then take another cloth doubled over two or three times, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can, so that you do not hurt the wound, then apply one more linen bandage on top, and do not pull it too tightly such that it only touches the wound; and leave it thus for one or two days until the inflammation has eased, then remove it, and administer medicines such as iris root, vetch flour, frankincense powder, and similar things; and from these things make a powder and place it upon the wound, and always apply soft medicines without biting; and ensure that the wound is always clean, so that you do not leave ointment nor let bowels assemble thereupon, for when bowels gather on the brain cloth, they will corrupt and decay, causing great harm to the patient; for when one places something biting upon the wound, it will necrotize above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be very careful if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, and do not hesitate to doubt yourself.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness comes from the medicine that has been applied, having such virtue, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix it with one drachm of wax, and put it on the face. Then treat him in various ways until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose are broken at once, or just one by itself, for there are two bones there; the lower one is cartilage and does not break unless it is hit hard or twisted, but then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your little finger or a reed into the nostril and place the break evenly against your index finger at the pouch below, until the nostril regains its natural shape. Do this gently and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then use a small rod about as thick as your finger to align it properly.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then do likewise, and hasten to restore it on the first day if possible. If not, after the seventh or tenth day when the swelling has subsided, then insert into the head of the nostril lint strips of linen cloth if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or insert another strip on the other side if the break is there; ensure that the strips are thick enough to fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some surgeons say that one should grease the tents with butter and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but rather the tents should be greased with a mixture of egg albumen and ground millstone. Then leave it alone until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Sometimes feathers from a goose are used instead of strips, with a soft cloth wrapped around them to keep the break in place while the patient breathes through it; do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if inflammation occurs in the nose while you are working on it, then insert softened wax or cotton moistened with rose oil or a little diacylgonine.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess forms, then apply this plaster: ground sesame flour and incense powder mixed with egg white. Then place light dressings on it and do not bind tightly. If the fracture in the nose is small but broken into many pieces, extract them using appropriate tools, then sew up the wound and treat it with appropriate plasters and ointments for healing flesh wounds. And if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents and apply splints of lead until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below and there is no wound on the outside, and the break is only on the outside with no fracture inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side of the jawbone, insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if it is on the left side, use your right hand and gently insert your index finger behind the break, then align it with your other hand from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is displaced in two places, then provide traction on both sides until it is aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth are displaced or broken due to movement of the jawbone fracture, then fix them with a gold, silver, or silk thread. Apply wax on the broken jawbone and place a doubled cloth over it; then put a well-made splint or a piece of leather on top, matching the length and width of the jawbone, secure it to the cheek where possible, and instruct the patient to rest and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the alignment has changed, remove it on the third day and reposition it correctly. Apply a plaster made of flour mixed with egg albumen or sesame flour after removing the wax; then apply light linen over it. If the plaster remains effective and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals, which usually takes three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if inflammation occurs, administer the treatments we have mentioned many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, ensure that no piece of bone is missing; carefully remove it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have removed all these pieces and there are none left, then sew the wound closed if it is wide, and apply some bandages to prevent infection until it heals.
de la forcele	With tweezers
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The shoulder blade can break several times in front, towards the shoulder, and there are three ways this fracture can occur:
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	"And the work is such when there's no wound, that you should have two assistants: one to hold the arm which feels broken; and the other stretch the neck towards the part. Then place the break evenly on your two hands so that its shape is as it should be, without appearance or displacement."
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	"And if you need to stretch further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of cloth or wool, and its size according to your necessity. Then extend and lift the arm, gripping the ball with your hand so that you can align the break evenly as it should be."
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	"And if you cannot pull the head of the arm forward because it is deeply set, then the patient must lie on their back and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder. Then push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the arm is lifted."
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	"And then align the break with your two hands. If it is displaced, you must cut above it. Gently pull out the pieces and if the bone cannot meet due to any obstacle, cut one of the incisions that you have made. But place this instrument under the arm to support the joint:"
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it should resemble a spoon, and not be lifted up, and be as wide as is necessary according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two heads, as you see, one wide and the other narrow like the opening of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of hot abscess, then cut the wound open, and if the opening is small where you doubt a hot abscess, then fill the wound with rags and bandages according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	"And if hot inflammation occurs, soak a bandage in rose oil mixed with honey and vinegar, and place it on top."
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The treatment of bone fractures when there are no wounds or cuts is as follows: place the poultice made from millet flour and egg white on the bone, then apply light bandages, and place a support under the armpit if necessary. Then take a very wide bandage about a palm's width, put a doubled cloth over the bandages and poultice, then wrap it tightly with an elastic band three fingers wide and long so that both ends of the bandage hang down. Place the elastic band on the fracture and wrap the bandage around the neck and under the healthy shoulder blade and under the fractured one, tightening each part individually. When you see that the bandages hold the fracture in place and that the elastic band does not move over the broken bone, reinforce it every day until the bindings loosen. Then make the patient lie on their back and place a small pillow under the armpit to lift the shoulder up. Lighten the pressure on the fracture by supporting the shoulder with a sling tied around the neck; do not untie it unless an accident occurs, for up to twenty days. Then resume the poultice if necessary, continue to tighten and leave it as is until restored. It takes about twenty-eight days to heal, but some people may take less time.
de la brisure de l’espaule	"About the break of the shoulder:"
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder bone breaks or moves out of its proper place, and it cannot be perceived except by touch; arrange it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form in every possible way; then place on the spot powder from a millstone with abundance of eggs, and light dressings, and cover it with a double cloth. Then place over it a wide and thin bandage, somewhat wider than the shoulder, and if there are hairs under the bandage in some part of the shoulder, fill that hair with linseed dressings so that the bandage lies evenly; and then bind it firmly all around with a large bandage so that the bandage does not move from its place. Look at the dressing each day; and every time it moistens, bind it again, and put the bandage back in its proper place if it has moved. Have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be reset in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is completed, untie it, and be assured, for it is not a bone that can move easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	"And if a fragment of the bone sticks out and is not under the heart, then cut it off and proceed as we have said in treating the fracture of the collarbone to appease any hot inflammation."
de la brisure dou pis	"About the break of the arm:"
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the back.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it droops downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks support, and faints suddenly, sometimes vomiting blood, and the horse's eye appears in the broken bone.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back with a cushion between the shoulders. Then press the shoulders down and bring together the ribs of the two lower sides gently but firmly until the bones are aligned correctly. Then place dressings and bandages over a thin strip of salt or light wood, wrap it in cloth, and bind it to the broken bone so that it does not move. Wrap the bandage around the back and tie it securely. Check the dressing every hour and tighten it if it loosens. If it needs to be removed due to corrosion, itching, pain, or inflammation, do so quickly and reapply a new dressing. Then bind it again until it is healed."
de la brisure des costes	"About the break of the ribs:"
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	"Know that rib fractures only occur in large areas of the back and chest. They are not broken except by blows to these areas and can be felt clearly upon examination."
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a splint and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	"And if the rib fracture leans inwards, the patient feels great pain and sharpness like that of pleurisy because the bone pierces the lung. They experience shortness of breath, weakness, and vomiting of much blood. This is a serious condition, and the ancients considered it deadly."
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	"And there are those who say that one should administer foods that cause the belly to swell in order to push the fracture back into place."
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	"We do not do this because hot inflammation may arise if it has not already been present."
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	"But if it is already present, we treat it."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	"And some say that one should place cups on the area to draw out blood forcefully, and this seems reasonable. However, there is doubt whether the cups attract impurities to the site due to the weakness of the body."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And some say that one should cover the area with a warm woolen cloth moistened in oil and place splints between the ribs to align the fracture, then treat it like pleurisy with foods and medicines."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels such severe pain that they cannot bear it due to the bone pressing against the bandage, and there is doubt about the state of the limb, then one must cut over the location of the broken bone, placing something underneath the instrument to protect the skin. Then one should trim the bone lightly and gently pull it out, after which one should stitch up both sides of the wound if it is large, and apply splints until it heals properly.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess appears, place moist cloths soaked in rose oil on it and apply them to the location. Treat the location as necessary for an abscess, and keep the patient lying on that side until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a break of the bone of the neck occur, and rarely does it bend; and also with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note if their hands are softened, swollen, and insensitive, unable to move or stretch, and when pricked with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many cases. If they move and feel when restrained or pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar condition occurs in the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note if their feet are softened, and if the accident has occurred that is present in hands, and windy ventosity and excretion occur without voluntary control; and when they lie on their belly, excretion occurs without voluntary control.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he falls asleep on his back and wants to mount [a horse], then he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Such are those who are mortal: do not labor in their care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then it is the lesser of the two evils.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you watch if there is any hot abscess, then put rose oil or linseed oil on the spine until it is appeased; then put one of the comforting and drying poultices on it, and hold it down with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel the pain until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone comes out of joint, then cover the chest; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one stitch, then treat it with ointment for internal wounds until it is healed. And if the bone of the knee is broken, which is called the 'knee cap', put your left hand's pouch on it and hold it even with the other hand by force, then put the poultice and splint on it if necessary; then bind it up, and if there are any bones out of joint, open them up and remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	And concerning the breaking of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It can happen that the thighbone is broken, and if it happens, there will be little harm to the head. And it opens up on the long side, and inclines toward the parting of the thighs, and pain and soreness come to the person where it breaks, and it swells at that place.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you stretch your hand out until you are over the break. And know what the break is like and its shape. And if the break is only at the top, then put it back in place until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is on the long side or inclines inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that you can clearly see the restoration of that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back in place, then put a poultice on it, then put a splint made of wood or bone on it and bind the break so that it does not move. And hold the area under the ribs until the bandage is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if any hot abscess comes, do not touch it until the hot abscess is appeased. And then put on what we have said before. And then return to the restoration and bind it as it should be, if there are no bad accidents. And that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	And concerning the breaking of the elbow
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The elbow is that which is between the arm and the shoulder blade. And if it is broken, it should be restored in one of two ways: either by taking a piece of smooth wood like this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two pieces of wood together with two ropes and hang them up high. And make the patient sit on a chair. Then lay their broken arm on the wood so that it hangs down and rests in a curve of wood. Then put some heavy weight or let the minister pull it down. Then the master should put the break back in place with both hands until it is correctly aligned.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that one places the patient on their back, and they lay their hand on their neck, then commands two helpers: one to hold what is above the break of their hands, and the other to hold below all in one line, stretching each one to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then press down on the lien below and above the break, and extend each of the assistants to their respective sides.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then place one lien in the middle under the thigh, and another towards the side, under the fracture; and likewise if the fracture is towards the side, then lightly place a lien without labor, so that the fracture is even on its site and on the side; then set the fracture evenly as it should be, and hold it steady, if no inflammation comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if inflammation occurs, do not stretch it until the twenty-seventh day, and put a warm moist cloth on the axilla and rose oil until the inflammation is appeased; then stretch it, and the manner of stretching is as follows: place the splint on the break, then bring the arm onto the supporter, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the bandage, and stretch it onto the supporter and onto the arm so that the arm is in line with the stars, if nothing prevents it from being stretched, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, then use stars (traction devices) and place a larger and stronger star on the break than the others, with two fingers' space between each star, and let each star be large enough to pass the break three fingers from each side; then stretch onto the stars, as I said at the beginning of this chapter about stretching on the break, but more strongly and without pulling apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the splints and the binding as we have said, in the time when you are resetting the broken limb, and you doubt the hot inflammation, then leave it bound for seven days as we have said; then examine each day for three days after the binding to ensure that no pruritus or swelling comes to the site, so that the nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then let him not be untied until after 3 days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach. Place one cushion full of even wool under the shoulder blade, and watch every hour of the day or night to ensure that the broken limb does not move or the ligaments soften; then apply the plaster by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have mentioned earlier, in such a way that at first it is subtle, but when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset forty days after, then one should untie them and apply baths and ointment medications to set them in place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the restriction is ugly and stuck on, it must remain untied for forty days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Here is a possible translation of the passage on "la brisure du bras" (breakage of the arm) from the medical treatise "Cirurgia" by Guy de Chauliac:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones called the two "fuscile", one of which is small and extends to the wrist; the other is large and located beneath towards the little toe. Sometimes only the large "fuscile" breaks, or sometimes only the small one does, and occasionally both together do so.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the little bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and so is the healing; but when the big ones are broken, healing is difficult, and more serious if they break one by one.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it should be gently extended and set straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	But if it's the large bone, you must pull harder; and extend it over the cushion, and draw the little finger higher than the others, and let the thumb be lower than the others, and have the patient lie crossed on themselves, with the cushion placed high before them so they feel no strain. Then stretch the minister's left arm towards the bottom of the patient's hand or elbow, and another minister should help with the other side above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then the physician sets it straight according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces missing, then each must be placed back in its proper place. If any piece is still unable to grasp the heart, and cannot be restored to its original position, then one should cut above and below the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is also a wound, I have spoken of it in the chapter on special cases; so take care accordingly.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if swelling occurs at the beginning of restoration, take a bandage made from rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft, and wrap it gently over the swelling until it subsides.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cerote, and place there the emplaustre of the powder from the mill with abundant egg. Then put in the staples, and let the staple for breaking be always stronger, and a bit wider than the others. And know that it must have six staples on the arm in various positions: whether the breaker is in one bone or two; and let it be straighter above the breaker than elsewhere, and always less strained apart, as I said at the beginning of the chapter. And let the drapels which are on the breaker be soft and moist, not hard nor rough. And let the threads with which it is strained be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the lien after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.
