And if any bad accident occurs to the member, such as itching which comes to the member, then you must rinse the member with hot water until that itching is appeased; and let the member rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the straitening, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, so address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you are careful that the nourishment cannot reach the member because it is too tightly bound, then you should loosen it a little and let it rest like this for a few days until the nourishment comes to it, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, then do not untie it for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or whoever around, then he can put his hands to his neck, and keep his neck even, and guard against movement and twisting, and sleep on his back; and know that this dislocation is healed in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	Chapter 21: On the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and also on the forearms there are few fractures, but many dislocations occur.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or dislocated, then let the patient sit cross-legged and sit upright directly in front of him, evenly; then place his hand on a cloth laid out flat, and extend the broken bones by the minister, and join them evenly by the master, so that they are well-aligned. Then apply the plaster and splints if there is no swelling present, then place one splint according to the size of the affected area; and let it be wrapped in a linen bandage.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	"And if the fracture is on the inner side around the belly of the foot, make a bandage of cloths and instruct the patient to press it onto their broken foot; then hold it with a long cloth strip, and let the knot be soft as large as the sole of the hand, and secure it in place."
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	"And if the fracture is on the backside, then you must place a bandage above and another below in the sole of the foot so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the hand, and make sure the binding between the two is secure."
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	"And if the fracture occurs at any of our fingers, if it's the thumb, then align it properly; and bind it with the sole of the foot, and if you see fit place a small, straight splint to elevate the fracture and prevent movement. And if the fracture is on another finger, such as the index or one of the others, then align it and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together in one binding, whichever is better, or place a splint above like on the thumb; and beware of inflammation and arrange for hot poultice treatment, and secure whatever comes from it, as I have said."
de la cuixe brisie	"About a broken thighbone:"
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	"The thighbone is often broken and it is evident when it rotates forward or backward; and the treatment for this is to bind one tie above the fracture and another below."
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	"And the patient lies on their face, then each of the attendants extends his tie to his side equally; this is when the fracture is within the bone."
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the dislocation is near the root of the thigh, then let one ligament be towards the hilt, and the other ligament below the dislocation.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And similarly if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be near the knee, and let the extension be downwards; then the physician puts the bone even with both hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then applies the splint and bandage, if there is no abscess coming out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	"And if there is heat inflammation, allow it to subside before returning to your work and treatment; the binding is done in this manner."
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a hard doubled bandage of two or three layers, and retain the excess, then twist the leg until the heel reaches the root of the thigh, and insert one long thread between the hip and the leg, near the knee from below, and bring the ends of the thread upwards; then wrap the bandage around the leg and hip, then place splints on the fracture, and place one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and hip with soft cloths to evenly distribute pressure, then begin to tie firmly three or four turns on the fracture; and as you go higher up the fracture, tie less tightly; then take the two heads of the thread that you inserted between the leg and hip, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the head of the thread until you reach near the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this until no abscess or swelling appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	"And if inflammation occurs, untie it and address whatever comes from it, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they should be removed if possible; and if not, then the space should be split open and pus drawn out; and treat it as we have said until it is healed."
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	"And sometimes the thighbone is fractured in such a way that splints are placed on it, as in the case of the arm; nevertheless, the patient does not limp when the fracture is treated in this manner."
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	"And know that the thighbone is restored in about one month, or a little less or more, according to the different constitutions."
de la ruelle dou genoil	"About the knee joint"
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the tendon of the knee there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it is only a crack or hole, and this happens in every wound, and without wound, and this everyone feels.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is like this: put what is broken back onto its two sides so that it can be assembled and moved. Then put on a splint, and if necessary, use a rounded staple to hold it in place, then tighten as needed. Then rewrap all the bandages we mentioned earlier for other fractures, such as hot compresses and similar treatments. Put whatever treatment is appropriate for each condition so that it heals properly.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that the leg has two bones, of which one is rightly called «mustelz», and the other «foscile»; and it undergoes the same breaking as the arm does, and for this reason the treatment is the same as that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the "mustelz" bone is broken, it turns inward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and it can be seen clearly; and it turns beneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore prepare an extension and place it evenly, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the break is ugly and there are many fragments, then the extension should be smaller and lighter, and adjust it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when you have completed your task, then take two strips of wood, hollowed out to fit around the leg on either side, and long enough from just below the knee downwards. Then wrap each strip with a bandage above and below, tie them together in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, which is good; some people also use one splint made of wood, long enough for the leg, and place it there to prevent movement, especially where there is a wound. And every day move the leg gently to see if there is any heat or other infection. Until then, continue treating until it is healed."
de la brisure des os dou piet	"On the breaking of bones in the foot"
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	"The ankle does not experience any fractures, but sometimes a bone in the foot and the toes can be broken, and there is often contusion in various positions."
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	"And if there is a fracture of the bone in the foot and you see the bones protruding one over the other, then place your foot on the ground like someone who wants to walk, and put your own foot now on his where the bones are raised. Then press down until they return to their original position; then apply the splint and padding. Place a small tray with two holes under the sole of the foot, then strap it tightly around the foot with bandages and other necessary materials."
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	"And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage because you will find that the bones are aligned again, whether they were broken or dislocated."
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	"And if there are any broken toes, then set them back in place as we have described for the fingers of the hand. Then place a splint along the length of the toe and slightly wider. Place the tray that I mentioned under the foot and strap it tightly around it. If there are two or three or more broken toes, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a cloth of linen, and strap the tray under the foot. And let them rest on top of the tray so that they are well supported."
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	"And you should not forget the other things that we have mentioned for other fractures. Treat each case according to its nature."
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	"On the fracture of the bone of the wrist"
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, make her sit wide-legged, then incline her towards the back part, and let her be held from behind. Then fill the hollow of the woman with cotton, putting in as much as one stone. Then lower the woman gently and gradually raise her back until the cotton reaches the entrance of the nature, and the bone returns with the stone. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it. Do this for about seven days or so: then the break will be healed. And if you want to see, take a sheep's bladder, tie a tube at the opening, and put the whole bladder inside the nature. Then blow into the tube forcefully until the bladder is inflated within. Then the nature will return to its original state; then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said concerning the thighbone. These breaks are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice, and let them hear my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break indicates in many ways the right path to restoration; therefore, listen.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	For a broken penis, take a goose's gut and put it around the penis. Then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three or four days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	If there is a break with an open wound:
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	He who has a fracture with wound, especially if it is large, as in the thigh bone or shoulder bone or similar, should be bandaged now, so that the bandages we have mentioned witness this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, you should then rinse with vinegar, or with whatever else you have available, and immediately afterwards reset the fracture that same hour, or on the following day, if a physician is not present.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a physician is present, then wait until the ninth day to reset the fracture, until the inflammation has subsided. Do not touch it on the third or fourth day either, for you would thereby cause an evil outcome
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone fracture is apparent above the chest and exposed, then it is necessary for you to carefully align it with your hands, with minimal extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not sufficient to align it with your hands, then use this tool made of iron, which is either twenty-seven or eighteen inches long, and its width should correspond to the size of the wound. It is necessary for a physician to mold three or four of these tools according to what is needed in each case of fracture; it should be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend under pressure on the member being treated, and it should have a pointed end and be thicker at its midpoint, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palm" because the curved bone should be placed on top of the exposed head of the bone; press them together at once until they align evenly with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is slight and the tool cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut off the head of the bone so that the tool can gain purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you are unable to realign the bone as previously mentioned, then use an appropriate tool such as a chisel or knife to cut it with all your might. Then, remove any remaining sharp edges and small splinters from the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset but the patient still feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Do so until it is in its natural place. Then moisten a cloth in black stiptic wine and apply it gently if it is summer. Do not put cerote or other oily substances on the wound, as they will cause rot and corruption. Then apply splints once you have reset the bone, leave the wound open, and cut away excess skin around the wound according to its size. Be sure that the wound is not constrained with the break, for many foolish physicians have done this and caused harm or death upon the patient. Make the bandage softer and more gentle than usual for other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil may come of it, as we have said, and you find pain in its place, then one must not put on bandages; but wrap it tightly around with firm cloths, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when after one or two days you see the wound begin to heal, then remove what you have put on it with all wine, and apply healing salve to it, such as tetrafarmacum and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must massage the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is warm and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	"And the limb must be positioned in such a way that the bowstring runs down easily."
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	"And even if many days pass and the bone still cannot unite but again dislocates, know that there are small fragments of bone causing this pain, so you must treat the wound with a compress and remove all these unwanted fragments."
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears in the place, or other kind of corruption, then you must treat it according to what is said in this chapter beforehand.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and lies open upon the limb, such as the hipbone or shoulder blade, or other similar large bones, then do not pull it out, for many times death results from it; but leave it until it rots. Perhaps it will fall out by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	"from the bruises that come from the soldering"
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	"We often inquire about the health of the limb after a fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb can be unpleasant; sometimes the limb cannot perform its natural functions."
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	"Therefore, be careful if the bone is fresh: if the limb swells up, apply medicines that are astringent, such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others. Take any of these things or all together and mix them with wine that is astringent or with egg yolk or with vinegar; then place it on the swelling in bandages, and tie it tightly and do not untie it for several days; then remove it and start again until the swelling has disappeared. Or you can tie it around a piece of well-made lead; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from limbs. And if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it open on top and remove the excess flesh. Or have it shaved by some barber until it is gone, and treat it until it is healed."
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	"of the limb that is weak after a dressing"
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored,
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat,
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	"When a limb is twisted after an injury,"
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	"If a limb is twisted after healing, and the bone breaks open, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and such procedures are blameworthy, and great evils arise from them, and even death may result. Nevertheless, if the dislocations and twistings are fresh, then they ought to be fomented with hot water, or mollifying herbs should be cooked, like willow leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make one mollifying plaster, like diacylгон well-made, and take the musk of willow, and confect it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply the plaster; or take figs and grind them with coltsfoot leaves and similar medicines that soften the union.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation occurs due to continuous and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And arrange for the limb to be moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	"And if the twistedness is old and hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed by iron, then it should be cut down to the bone with a delicate and light scalpel; and pay close attention and take care in treating it."
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	"Here begins the book of dislocations"
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	"A dislocation occurs when a joint is displaced from its proper place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, and the patient feels great pain and great injury."
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	"When dislocation happens to anyone, it should be immediately reduced without delay."
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	But if one delays, the place swells up, and sometimes it is scarcely reset in its place; therefore do not move the limb when it is swollen: often it brings about gangrene and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, have the patient lie down, then leave him until the inflammation has subsided; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each limb as they come into their place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	"And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet."
des mandibules	"jaw dislocation"
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	"Rarely does the jaw become dislocated outward, and there are two kinds of dislocation in both cases: either it is slightly displaced from its proper place and softened a little; or it is completely dislocated and hangs down towards the chest, so that saliva flows out of the mouth and he cannot hold it in nor close his mouth, and he wraps his tongue with speech."
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	"When the dislocation is small, it returns to its proper place through several positions."
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a manner that the assistants hold the patient's head, and the physician puts his fist into one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other two hands are placed equally to apply pressure; and instruct the patient to relax his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	"And the physician places it back in its proper place until it returns to its original position."
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	"If the dislocation is severe, especially if it affects both jaws simultaneously, then apply warm water and oil soaks until the dislocated parts become slightly softened; do not force the reduction, as we have said."
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then place moistened cloths made of rose oil and wax on it, then lightly bind it with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, his head held still between two pillows so that he does not move to either side nor exert himself in chewing, but take light food until the pains are gone and the jaws are healed; and then he may chew what he wants easily, and need not strain to open his mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is fully healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	"And if the two jaws cannot be reduced properly within an hour and are not returned to their original position, then fever and other constitutional symptoms may arise, sometimes diarrhea, sometimes vomiting of bile."
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	"When you see these signs, know that it is a serious condition; many people die from this within nine days."
de la forcelle	"of the jawbone"
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	"The jawbone cannot dislocate inwards along its length and within the throat; however, it can sometimes be dislocated outwards at the chin, which is quite noticeable."
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms; then firmly press the place with your palm, and it will return; then place the emplaster and bandage, and bind it tight; and the shoulder which is towards the side cannot dislocate; if it does not, and if it dislocates even once, reset it to its place as we have said; then place the emplaster and bandage, and bind it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and likewise the head of the shoulder is reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	"On shoulder dislocation"
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder dislocates only in three ways: one is that it dislocates at the part of the elbow below; and the second is at the part of the armpit; and sometimes it dislocates above, but this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind due to the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the elbow, especially in those who have much flesh, for in these ones it snaps quickly; in those who have little flesh, it barely jumps out, and returns quickly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that there is an injury or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot boil, and they believe that it has dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must examine it until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations are recognizable when they are below towards the elbow, and there is a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, which you will find clearly manifest in their diversity; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and below the elbow touching the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand close to their side nor move it in any way; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly upon touching; and this manner of dislocation is difficult to reset when it is old or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the physician lifts the sick person's hand upwards, then places their elbows under the buttocks and pulls the joint forcibly upwards; and the physician lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it beneath, it will quickly return.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within several days after, then it is necessary for the patient to be bathed in warm water; and let them be administered moistening and soothing remedies, such as a decoction of marshmallow and fenugreek and melilot in water, and this should be applied. Then let the patient be propped up on their back, and place under the armpit a pillow of even consistency, not too soft nor too hard. Then the physician places their heel on the pillow, gently lifts the virtuous head of the shoulder, and pulls the hand of the patient; and another attendant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards. Thus, the shoulder comes back into place, and if you wish to reset it according to this manner: have present a man who is taller than the patient, standing straight against the side. He places his shoulder under the armpit of the patient and lifts the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs from the arm; and another attendant pulls the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, hang with him some heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also reset in another way: and this is that one drives a long stick into the ground, with which the head of the shoulder is as round as the pistol, and neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but let him have soft cloths beneath, and the patient stands on the length of the wood; then his hand is stretched down on the other side appropriately, and the joint returns to its place quickly; and if it will not return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick of II arms in width and IIII palms in breadth, which has the head round enough for the mouth to enter deep beneath the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place soft cloths on the head of the wood so that the wood does not bruise the sick person, then place it under the buttocks of the sick person; extend the arm along the length of the wood and tie the bandage to the wood and at the elbow of the hand, then place the arm upon a support made from a bone as wide as possible, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whatever way that may be, then you must place under the buttocks a pillow of even wool; then apply the plaster prepared with powder from a millstone, with incense and egg white all around the shoulder and bind it firmly under the buttocks, turn the bandage over the plaster, and wrap the hand around its neck, and let the hand remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they should eat little until the member is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then they may eat more afterwards after five or six days, and move about; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another cause, then you must administer cauteries at III points, as it is set forth in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and after twenty days the joint still does not stay in place, nor can they raise their arm upwards, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set back in its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the breast and the nipples, or behind them, is caused by a blow or stretching of the hand, and another bandage should be applied; and care should be taken until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there comes pain in the member and slowness in movement, then the sick person should bathe many times until that pain is alleviated and returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Regarding dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated outward and returns inward; and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially front and back, then the dislocation has not been reduced, because one can see it well and feel it clearly; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the sound one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is crushed, and it cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reduce it before abscesses occur there because if an abscess occurs then the reduction will be painful and perhaps cannot be reduced entirely, especially when it is behind; such a dislocation is worse than others and causes great pain and sometimes gangrene may occur
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the reduction is when it can be done thus: you should extend their hand with both of your hands; and their arm should be spread wide, and the hands of the doctor according to the elbow around, over, and under, and push the joint into its place at the base of the thumb or at the root of the palm until it returns to its proper position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when you fold their hand onto your hand and push the elbow that is dislocated from the root of the palm towards you.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and indeed two assistants extend the arm, and two assistants hold it, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm on each side, then wrap a doubled cloth long and wide around it; and when the physician has joined the joint with his hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint forcibly until it returns; and when it is in place, then put dry compresses with powdered egg yolk on it, and hold it firmly, and suspend the arm around the neck of the patient, and leave it for a few days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly set in its place, he unties the bandage and leaves it alone; but if you see that the joint has not healed properly, then begin again with the compress and the bandage, leaving it like this for several days until it is securely placed; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it feels pain afterwards when the joint has been reset, and it moves again, then bathe and rub it gently and press until it is soothed; or put on the joint a poultice of fatty mutton grease, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, then rub the joint temperately, then replace the poultice, and then enter the bath again; and do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see fit, then put on fern of hot moist chicory with butter, and hold it there; thus it will return to its proper condition.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand:
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joints of the hand are dislocated, and their return is easy,
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is thus: you place the sick hand on a table, and the servant extends the hand, and the physician places it evenly, so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns completely. Then you must look to see if it is properly in place; then the patient places the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient places their backhand on the table, and the physician places their hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good; if not, then press with soothing plasters and leave it thus without beginning again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, then the joint remains twisted; and does not harm the patient any further than as long as the hand is crippled, and can grip nothing at all: know then that the nerves or arteries are cut; so there is no other way to heal it but by cautery near the case, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	"And when the hand is in place, then apply the plaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it thus."
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, then moisten with hot water, and rub it until it becomes soft."
de la dislocation des dois de la main	This appears to be a heading or title in Old French: "Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand".
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Both thumbs of the hand may be dislocated on either side, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the belly; therefore, if dislocation has occurred, press it back into place until it returns. Then hold the top of the thumb and tilt it towards the part where it was dislocated. Leave it for two days, then reset it on the third day and wrap it tightly as we have said. Remove the bandage on the fourth day and move the thumb gently, then bind it again. Repeat this often until it is secure. Do likewise if the thumb is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do everything in the same manner until it is healed.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	This appears to be a heading or title in Old French: "Of the dislocation of the spine of the back".
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	"When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no remedy, because the patient is already dead."
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that evacuations occur involuntarily and cannot be held back. Sometimes certain limbs become softened, such as both thighs or both arms, or even the spine moves in four parts; this one which moves at the back is called 'gilbositis'. If gilbositis has come from infancy, there is no cure nor healing for it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falls or impacts or similar things, the ancients prescribed various remedies with grand words, but not all had great benefit; however, I have summarized them according to my intention and formed tools in diverse manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast before, none has health; and likewise that which comes directly to both sides, and one can only cure properly that which comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be extended on his face evenly, and have support underneath him so he does not bruise himself; then stick one stake at the head firmly into the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a band around the hips of the patient, and another at the thighs, knees, and ankles; and two servants shall hold the bands, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and let them be held fast, the stake as we have said, and the physician place his palms firmly on the spine until it yields.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board of three spans long and place it under the skin, with the patient on their side. Insert the end of the board under the skin, then place the middle of the board on the spine; let the physician put his feet on the other end of the board and press until it returns to its proper place. And if you wish, do this in turns for the shoulder that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you drive two stakes into the head of the patient's arm, one of a great span apart, and towards the feet two others, with a palm's breadth of space between each stake above and below. And let there be a hole in each stake where the joint turns, and let the stakes be firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move. And between each pair of stakes let there be one turning stake on which the joint turns, and let there be two small stakes of a palm's length for turning the joint. Then tie the bandage that is among the stakes to the joint towards the head, and the other bandage towards the feet at the other joint, and each minister turn their stake with all the bandages, and the master shall set the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equal, place a drying plaster with plenty of egg on top, then the dressings, and then apply the iron from a tablet three fingers long, pressing on the location of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and let the patient rest quietly until they are healed; and if any problem arises at the end of their recovery, administer softening and soothing medicines along with the iron we mentioned earlier; sometimes one may even apply a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance resembles dislocation in the lower spine, but do not presume this is dislocation: it could bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	"on dislocations of the hip"
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	"Know that at the joints of the hip and shoulder only dislocations occur, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is unstable in four directions: inside and outside, front and back; but more unstable inside than others, and little unstable in front and back."
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the sign of its dislocation within is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, the sick one appears longer, and the sick knee joint opens more widely, and the sick person cannot bend their knee at the fire; and the place near where there is heat and swelling is also dislocated, because the head of the thighbone has moved there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who is afflicted by this is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of one who has it before him is that he stretches his leg well according to its length; nevertheless, he cannot bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot do so, and he retains his urine, and the angle swells, and when he walks, he limps on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one who has it behind him is that he cannot straighten his knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the angle is softened, and the buttock is placed under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment for this type of dislocation is that you should examine whether the dislocation is old or new, and if it has remained in its position without care, then there will be no need for treatment, and he must not have any swelling.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where dislocation is recent,
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare the assistant strongly, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or where it is bound on the knee; and another assistant extends his hand thus that he places his hands under his buttocks, then pulls gently on a soft rope attached to the hip; and another holds the head of the rope; and all extend upwards and downwards at once until the patient lifts off the ground together.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	"This manner of extension applies to four types of dislocations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good."
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	But if not, then you must treat its similarity. When the dislocation is at the hip joint, you must place the patient on his healthy side, then put the rope on the root of the hip and the place beneath the angle, then pull the rope upwards towards the angle and towards the forceps. Then another assistant takes the patient's arms and embraces the great bone of the sick hip, and extends it strongly outwards: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot bind it in this manner that we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a soft strong rope on the two heels and on the two knees, and let the affected leg be extended two spans more than the other; then hang him from the top of a pole, and let him be two arm-lengths above the ground; then command one servant to embrace the hip joint, and let another servant hang with the patient, who embraces firmly the hip joint, for the dislocation returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the front, then let the patient lie down, as we have said in that case who has gout; and draw one rope over the affected leg properly, and over the foot also. Then place two stakes, one at the head and one at the feet, and stick one stake between the thighs of the patient in this manner: And have moist cloths ready around it so that the patient does not blister. Then let each servant extend towards him, and the physician put his hand equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place a board and press thus as we said in the condition of the ribs; have the patient lie on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	"And when the dislocation is towards the front, one must extend the dislocated leg quickly, as I have said; then the surgeon places their knee on the angle of the dislocated hip, presses with their other hand above it, and extends it downwards towards the knee."
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, do not extend the patient downwards or lift him up, but have him lie as if his hip were dislocated backwards, as we said about childbirth on the two hips; and place him on his face, with his leg extended as we said earlier, and press on the joint with a board; this will be done when the patient extends his legs and they are even. Then join the thighs, apply the splint, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move. Let him rest for three or four days, then untie it and reapply the splint. If they appear equal, bind again as before and leave it for three days. Then untie it and let the patient walk gently until his limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	**Treatment of Dislocations of the Knee**
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and behind; it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the hip, and if it does not align with the hip, know that they are dislocated. And the treatment for all such cases is as follows: make the patient sit upright, extend their leg if possible, place your back on their thigh, and put their foot on yours; then grasp their knee with your palms and pull it between your thighs, then bend both sides of the knee forcefully. Another assistant should extend the patient's foot until the knee returns to its proper place, and the sign that it is properly aligned is when the leg lightly touches the hip. Then apply the plaster and bind the leg to the hip tightly for three or four days before removing it. The patient should not walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not yet fully aligned, then extend it forcefully as we have described in the treatment of dislocation of the thigh, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Regarding the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel can sometimes be injured and sometimes fully dislocated both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign of this is that the ankle is swollen, and it points forward at the part where it is dislocated; the reduction is easy, and one should gently extend the arm with both hands when it is merely agitated.
