Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, then you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the leg above the ankle with your left hand; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then lift it up and gently place the foot up high; do this twice, alternating between pulling and lifting the foot; if it returns, that's good. If not, then begin the procedure again, for it will return. And if it cannot be returned in this manner, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and firmly plant a pole in the earth between his thighs, tying cloths around it so as not to wound the patient; then one minister should hold the thigh, and another extend the foot with both hands or tie it to the collar of the foot; then each minister should stretch evenly, and the pole should always be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient steady when he is stretched. Then the master puts his hands on the dislocation, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, then place the plaster and bandages on it, and press firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature loosens, then press it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if they walk before this time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If inflammation occurs, you must calm it as we have said elsewhere until the patient is healed."
des dois	I'm here to help! Please provide me with more context or information about what you'd like assistance with regarding "des doi" (which translates to "the two of them").
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	"If the two joints are dislocated, they should be gently stretched without force, and it is an easy thing to do."
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the ankle, then you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on two boards so that they are completely straight, and place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when it is even and nothing opens, then place two boards under the sole of the foot, then press firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let them rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	"Regarding wounds and dislocations at the same time"
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When an injury comes with dislocation and it is wished to be restored, many times the patient dies: therefore, do not be presumptuous in its treatment unless you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are compassionate and merciful but not hasty; rather, at the beginning use soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of healing. But when there is hope, then reset the limb to its place before the hot abscess arrives; and once the limb is in place, administer remedies for soothing heat, and treat the wound as it ought with drying ointments. And if there are fractures or crushed bones, set them and do what we have said for simple diseases. Guard against entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this is worth more than your armor and body.
Amen	Amen
